"2579"	"wilder, heartier interest, if she had built a fire under him."
"2580"	"Tom felt that it was time to wake up; this sort of life might be"
"2581"	"romantic enough, in his blighted condition, but it was getting to have"
"2582"	"too little sentiment and too much distracting variety about it. So he"
"2583"	"thought over various plans for relief, and finally hit upon that of"
"2584"	"professing to be fond of Pain-killer. He asked for it so often that he"
"2585"	"became a nuisance, and his aunt ended by telling him to help himself and"
"2586"	"quit bothering her. If it had been Sid, she would have had no misgivings"
"2587"	"to alloy her delight; but since it was Tom, she watched the bottle"
"2588"	"clandestinely. She found that the medicine did really diminish, but it"
"2589"	"did not occur to her that the boy was mending the health of a crack in"
"2590"	"the sitting-room floor with it."
"2591"	"One day Tom was in the act of dosing the crack when his aunt’s yellow"
"2592"	"cat came along, purring, eyeing the teaspoon avariciously, and begging"
"2593"	"for a taste. Tom said:"
"2594"	"“Don’t ask for it unless you want it, Peter.”"
"2595"	"But Peter signified that he did want it."
"2596"	"“You better make sure.”"
"2597"	"Peter was sure."
"2598"	"“Now you’ve asked for it, and I’ll give it to you, because there ain’t"
"2599"	"anything mean about me; but if you find you don’t like it, you mustn’t"
"2600"	"blame anybody but your own self.”"
"2601"	"Peter was agreeable. So Tom pried his mouth open and poured down"
"2602"	"the Pain-killer. Peter sprang a couple of yards in the air, and then"
"2603"	"delivered a war-whoop and set off round and round the room, banging"
"2604"	"against furniture, upsetting flower-pots, and making general havoc. Next"
"2605"	"he rose on his hind feet and pranced around, in a frenzy of enjoyment,"
"2606"	"with his head over his shoulder and his voice proclaiming his"
"2607"	"unappeasable happiness. Then he went tearing around the house again"
"2608"	"spreading chaos and destruction in his path. Aunt Polly entered in time"
"2609"	"to see him throw a few double summersets, deliver a final mighty hurrah,"
"2610"	"and sail through the open window, carrying the rest of the flower-pots"
"2611"	"with him. The old lady stood petrified with astonishment, peering over"
"2612"	"her glasses; Tom lay on the floor expiring with laughter."
"2613"	"“Tom, what on earth ails that cat?”"
"2614"	"“I don’t know, aunt,” gasped the boy."
"2615"	"“Why, I never see anything like it. What did make him act so?”"
"2616"	"“Deed I don’t know, Aunt Polly; cats always act so when they’re having a"
"2617"	"good time.”"
"2618"	"“They do, do they?” There was something in the tone that made Tom"
"2619"	"apprehensive."
"2620"	"“Yes’m. That is, I believe they do.”"
"2621"	"“You _do_?”"
"2622"	"“Yes’m.”"
"2623"	"The old lady was bending down, Tom watching, with interest emphasized"
"2624"	"by anxiety. Too late he divined her “drift.” The handle of the telltale"
"2625"	"tea-spoon was visible under the bed-valance. Aunt Polly took it, held it"
"2626"	"up. Tom winced, and dropped his eyes. Aunt Polly raised him by the usual"
"2627"	"handle--his ear--and cracked his head soundly with her thimble."
"2628"	"“Now, sir, what did you want to treat that poor dumb beast so, for?”"
"2629"	"“I done it out of pity for him--because he hadn’t any aunt.”"
"2630"	"“Hadn’t any aunt!--you numskull. What has that got to do with it?”"
"2631"	"“Heaps. Because if he’d had one she’d a burnt him out herself! She’d a"
"2632"	"roasted his bowels out of him ‘thout any more feeling than if he was a"
"2633"	"human!”"
"2634"	"Aunt Polly felt a sudden pang of remorse. This was putting the thing in"
"2635"	"a new light; what was cruelty to a cat _might_ be cruelty to a boy, too."
"2636"	"She began to soften; she felt sorry. Her eyes watered a little, and she"
"2637"	"put her hand on Tom’s head and said gently:"
"2638"	"“I was meaning for the best, Tom. And, Tom, it _did_ do you good.”"
"2639"	"Tom looked up in her face with just a perceptible twinkle peeping"
"2640"	"through his gravity."
"2641"	"“I know you was meaning for the best, aunty, and so was I with Peter. It"
"2642"	"done _him_ good, too. I never see him get around so since--”"
"2643"	"“Oh, go ‘long with you, Tom, before you aggravate me again. And you try"
"2644"	"and see if you can’t be a good boy, for once, and you needn’t take any"
"2645"	"more medicine.”"
"2646"	"Tom reached school ahead of time. It was noticed that this strange thing"
"2647"	"had been occurring every day latterly. And now, as usual of late,"
"2648"	"he hung about the gate of the schoolyard instead of playing with his"
"2649"	"comrades. He was sick, he said, and he looked it. He tried to seem to"
"2650"	"be looking everywhere but whither he really was looking--down the road."
"2651"	"Presently Jeff Thatcher hove in sight, and Tom’s face lighted; he gazed"
"2652"	"a moment, and then turned sorrowfully away. When Jeff arrived, Tom"
"2653"	"accosted him; and “led up” warily to opportunities for remark about"
"2654"	"Becky, but the giddy lad never could see the bait. Tom watched and"
"2655"	"watched, hoping whenever a frisking frock came in sight, and hating the"
"2656"	"owner of it as soon as he saw she was not the right one. At last frocks"
"2657"	"ceased to appear, and he dropped hopelessly into the dumps; he entered"
"2658"	"the empty schoolhouse and sat down to suffer. Then one more frock passed"
"2659"	"in at the gate, and Tom’s heart gave a great bound. The next instant he"
"2660"	"was out, and “going on” like an Indian; yelling, laughing, chasing boys,"
"2661"	"jumping over the fence at risk of life and limb, throwing handsprings,"
"2662"	"standing on his head--doing all the heroic things he could conceive of,"
"2663"	"and keeping a furtive eye out, all the while, to see if Becky Thatcher"
"2664"	"was noticing. But she seemed to be unconscious of it all; she never"
"2665"	"looked. Could it be possible that she was not aware that he was there?"
"2666"	"He carried his exploits to her immediate vicinity; came war-whooping"
"2667"	"around, snatched a boy’s cap, hurled it to the roof of the schoolhouse,"
"2668"	"broke through a group of boys, tumbling them in every direction, and"
"2669"	"fell sprawling, himself, under Becky’s nose, almost upsetting her--and"
"2670"	"she turned, with her nose in the air, and he heard her say: “Mf! some"
"2671"	"people think they’re mighty smart--always showing off!”"
"2672"	"Tom’s cheeks burned. He gathered himself up and sneaked off, crushed and"
"2673"	"crestfallen."
"2674"	"CHAPTER XIII"
"2675"	"TOM’S mind was made up now. He was gloomy and desperate. He was a"
"2676"	"forsaken, friendless boy, he said; nobody loved him; when they found out"
"2677"	"what they had driven him to, perhaps they would be sorry; he had tried"
"2678"	"to do right and get along, but they would not let him; since nothing"
"2679"	"would do them but to be rid of him, let it be so; and let them blame"
"2680"	"_him_ for the consequences--why shouldn’t they? What right had the"
"2681"	"friendless to complain? Yes, they had forced him to it at last: he would"
"2682"	"lead a life of crime. There was no choice."
"2683"	"By this time he was far down Meadow Lane, and the bell for school to"
"2684"	"“take up” tinkled faintly upon his ear. He sobbed, now, to think he"
"2685"	"should never, never hear that old familiar sound any more--it was very"
"2686"	"hard, but it was forced on him; since he was driven out into the cold"
"2687"	"world, he must submit--but he forgave them. Then the sobs came thick and"
"2688"	"fast."
"2689"	"Just at this point he met his soul’s sworn comrade, Joe"
"2690"	"Harper--hard-eyed, and with evidently a great and dismal purpose in his"
"2691"	"heart. Plainly here were “two souls with but a single thought.” Tom,"
"2692"	"wiping his eyes with his sleeve, began to blubber out something about"
"2693"	"a resolution to escape from hard usage and lack of sympathy at home by"
"2694"	"roaming abroad into the great world never to return; and ended by hoping"
"2695"	"that Joe would not forget him."
"2696"	"But it transpired that this was a request which Joe had just been going"
"2697"	"to make of Tom, and had come to hunt him up for that purpose. His mother"
"2698"	"had whipped him for drinking some cream which he had never tasted and"
"2699"	"knew nothing about; it was plain that she was tired of him and wished"
"2700"	"him to go; if she felt that way, there was nothing for him to do but"
"2701"	"succumb; he hoped she would be happy, and never regret having driven her"
"2702"	"poor boy out into the unfeeling world to suffer and die."
"2703"	"As the two boys walked sorrowing along, they made a new compact to stand"
"2704"	"by each other and be brothers and never separate till death relieved"
"2705"	"them of their troubles. Then they began to lay their plans. Joe was for"
"2706"	"being a hermit, and living on crusts in a remote cave, and dying,"
"2707"	"some time, of cold and want and grief; but after listening to Tom, he"
"2708"	"conceded that there were some conspicuous advantages about a life of"
"2709"	"crime, and so he consented to be a pirate."
"2710"	"Three miles below St. Petersburg, at a point where the Mississippi River"
"2711"	"was a trifle over a mile wide, there was a long, narrow, wooded island,"
"2712"	"with a shallow bar at the head of it, and this offered well as a"
"2713"	"rendezvous. It was not inhabited; it lay far over toward the further"
"2714"	"shore, abreast a dense and almost wholly unpeopled forest. So Jackson’s"
"2715"	"Island was chosen. Who were to be the subjects of their piracies was a"
"2716"	"matter that did not occur to them. Then they hunted up Huckleberry Finn,"
"2717"	"and he joined them promptly, for all careers were one to him; he was"
"2718"	"indifferent. They presently separated to meet at a lonely spot on the"
"2719"	"river-bank two miles above the village at the favorite hour--which was"
"2720"	"midnight. There was a small log raft there which they meant to capture."
"2721"	"Each would bring hooks and lines, and such provision as he could steal"
"2722"	"in the most dark and mysterious way--as became outlaws. And before the"
"2723"	"afternoon was done, they had all managed to enjoy the sweet glory of"
"2724"	"spreading the fact that pretty soon the town would “hear something.” All"
"2725"	"who got this vague hint were cautioned to “be mum and wait.”"
"2726"	"About midnight Tom arrived with a boiled ham and a few trifles,"
"2727"	"and stopped in a dense undergrowth on a small bluff overlooking the"
"2728"	"meeting-place. It was starlight, and very still. The mighty river lay"
"2729"	"like an ocean at rest. Tom listened a moment, but no sound disturbed the"
"2730"	"quiet. Then he gave a low, distinct whistle. It was answered from under"
"2731"	"the bluff. Tom whistled twice more; these signals were answered in the"
"2732"	"same way. Then a guarded voice said:"
"2733"	"“Who goes there?”"
"2734"	"“Tom Sawyer, the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main. Name your names.”"
"2735"	"“Huck Finn the Red-Handed, and Joe Harper the Terror of the Seas.” Tom"
"2736"	"had furnished these titles, from his favorite literature."
"2737"	"“‘Tis well. Give the countersign.”"
"2738"	"Two hoarse whispers delivered the same awful word simultaneously to the"
"2739"	"brooding night:"
"2740"	"“_Blood_!”"
"2741"	"Then Tom tumbled his ham over the bluff and let himself down after it,"
"2742"	"tearing both skin and clothes to some extent in the effort. There was"
"2743"	"an easy, comfortable path along the shore under the bluff, but it lacked"
"2744"	"the advantages of difficulty and danger so valued by a pirate."
"2745"	"The Terror of the Seas had brought a side of bacon, and had about worn"
"2746"	"himself out with getting it there. Finn the Red-Handed had stolen a"
"2747"	"skillet and a quantity of half-cured leaf tobacco, and had also brought"
"2748"	"a few corn-cobs to make pipes with. But none of the pirates smoked or"
"2749"	"“chewed” but himself. The Black Avenger of the Spanish Main said it"
"2750"	"would never do to start without some fire. That was a wise thought;"
"2751"	"matches were hardly known there in that day. They saw a fire smouldering"
"2752"	"upon a great raft a hundred yards above, and they went stealthily"
"2753"	"thither and helped themselves to a chunk. They made an imposing"
"2754"	"adventure of it, saying, “Hist!” every now and then, and suddenly"
"2755"	"halting with finger on lip; moving with hands on imaginary dagger-hilts;"
"2756"	"and giving orders in dismal whispers that if “the foe” stirred, to “let"
"2757"	"him have it to the hilt,” because “dead men tell no tales.” They knew"
"2758"	"well enough that the raftsmen were all down at the village laying"
"2759"	"in stores or having a spree, but still that was no excuse for their"
"2760"	"conducting this thing in an unpiratical way."
"2761"	"They shoved off, presently, Tom in command, Huck at the after oar and"
"2762"	"Joe at the forward. Tom stood amidships, gloomy-browed, and with folded"
"2763"	"arms, and gave his orders in a low, stern whisper:"
"2764"	"“Luff, and bring her to the wind!”"
"2765"	"“Aye-aye, sir!”"
"2766"	"“Steady, steady-y-y-y!”"
"2767"	"“Steady it is, sir!”"
"2768"	"“Let her go off a point!”"
"2769"	"“Point it is, sir!”"
"2770"	"As the boys steadily and monotonously drove the raft toward mid-stream"
"2771"	"it was no doubt understood that these orders were given only for"
"2772"	"“style,” and were not intended to mean anything in particular."
"2773"	"“What sail’s she carrying?”"
"2774"	"“Courses, tops’ls, and flying-jib, sir.”"
"2775"	"“Send the r’yals up! Lay out aloft, there, half a dozen of"
"2776"	"ye--foretopmaststuns’l! Lively, now!”"
"2777"	"“Aye-aye, sir!”"
"2778"	"“Shake out that maintogalans’l! Sheets and braces! _now_ my hearties!”"
"2779"	"“Aye-aye, sir!”"
"2780"	"“Hellum-a-lee--hard a port! Stand by to meet her when she comes! Port,"
"2781"	"port! _Now_, men! With a will! Stead-y-y-y!”"
"2782"	"“Steady it is, sir!”"
"2783"	"The raft drew beyond the middle of the river; the boys pointed her head"
"2784"	"right, and then lay on their oars. The river was not high, so there was"
"2785"	"not more than a two or three mile current. Hardly a word was said during"
"2786"	"the next three-quarters of an hour. Now the raft was passing before"
"2787"	"the distant town. Two or three glimmering lights showed where it lay,"
"2788"	"peacefully sleeping, beyond the vague vast sweep of star-gemmed water,"
"2789"	"unconscious of the tremendous event that was happening. The Black"
"2790"	"Avenger stood still with folded arms, “looking his last” upon the scene"
"2791"	"of his former joys and his later sufferings, and wishing “she” could see"
"2792"	"him now, abroad on the wild sea, facing peril and death with dauntless"
"2793"	"heart, going to his doom with a grim smile on his lips. It was but"
"2794"	"a small strain on his imagination to remove Jackson’s Island beyond"
"2795"	"eye-shot of the village, and so he “looked his last” with a broken and"
"2796"	"satisfied heart. The other pirates were looking their last, too; and"
"2797"	"they all looked so long that they came near letting the current drift"
"2798"	"them out of the range of the island. But they discovered the danger in"
"2799"	"time, and made shift to avert it. About two o’clock in the morning the"
"2800"	"raft grounded on the bar two hundred yards above the head of the island,"
"2801"	"and they waded back and forth until they had landed their freight. Part"
"2802"	"of the little raft’s belongings consisted of an old sail, and this they"
"2803"	"spread over a nook in the bushes for a tent to shelter their provisions;"
"2804"	"but they themselves would sleep in the open air in good weather, as"
"2805"	"became outlaws."
"2806"	"They built a fire against the side of a great log twenty or thirty steps"
"2807"	"within the sombre depths of the forest, and then cooked some bacon in"
"2808"	"the frying-pan for supper, and used up half of the corn “pone” stock"
"2809"	"they had brought. It seemed glorious sport to be feasting in that wild,"
"2810"	"free way in the virgin forest of an unexplored and uninhabited island,"
"2811"	"far from the haunts of men, and they said they never would return to"
"2812"	"civilization. The climbing fire lit up their faces and threw its ruddy"
"2813"	"glare upon the pillared tree-trunks of their forest temple, and upon the"
"2814"	"varnished foliage and festooning vines."
"2815"	"When the last crisp slice of bacon was gone, and the last allowance"
"2816"	"of corn pone devoured, the boys stretched themselves out on the grass,"
"2817"	"filled with contentment. They could have found a cooler place, but"
"2818"	"they would not deny themselves such a romantic feature as the roasting"
"2819"	"campfire."
"2820"	"“_Ain’t_ it gay?” said Joe."
"2821"	"“It’s _nuts_!” said Tom. “What would the boys say if they could see us?”"
"2822"	"“Say? Well, they’d just die to be here--hey, Hucky!”"
"2823"	"“I reckon so,” said Huckleberry; “anyways, I’m suited. I don’t want"
"2824"	"nothing better’n this. I don’t ever get enough to eat, gen’ally--and here"
"2825"	"they can’t come and pick at a feller and bullyrag him so.”"
"2826"	"“It’s just the life for me,” said Tom. “You don’t have to get up,"
"2827"	"mornings, and you don’t have to go to school, and wash, and all that"
"2828"	"blame foolishness. You see a pirate don’t have to do _anything_, Joe,"
"2829"	"when he’s ashore, but a hermit _he_ has to be praying considerable, and"
"2830"	"then he don’t have any fun, anyway, all by himself that way.”"
"2831"	"“Oh yes, that’s so,” said Joe, “but I hadn’t thought much about it, you"
"2832"	"know. I’d a good deal rather be a pirate, now that I’ve tried it.”"
"2833"	"“You see,” said Tom, “people don’t go much on hermits, nowadays, like"
"2834"	"they used to in old times, but a pirate’s always respected. And"
"2835"	"a hermit’s got to sleep on the hardest place he can find, and put"
"2836"	"sackcloth and ashes on his head, and stand out in the rain, and--”"
"2837"	"“What does he put sackcloth and ashes on his head for?” inquired Huck."
"2838"	"“I dono. But they’ve _got_ to do it. Hermits always do. You’d have to do"
"2839"	"that if you was a hermit.”"
"2840"	"“Dern’d if I would,” said Huck."
"2841"	"“Well, what would you do?”"
"2842"	"“I dono. But I wouldn’t do that.”"
"2843"	"“Why, Huck, you’d _have_ to. How’d you get around it?”"
"2844"	"“Why, I just wouldn’t stand it. I’d run away.”"
"2845"	"“Run away! Well, you _would_ be a nice old slouch of a hermit. You’d be"
"2846"	"a disgrace.”"
"2847"	"The Red-Handed made no response, being better employed. He had finished"
"2848"	"gouging out a cob, and now he fitted a weed stem to it, loaded it with"
"2849"	"tobacco, and was pressing a coal to the charge and blowing a cloud of"
"2850"	"fragrant smoke--he was in the full bloom of luxurious contentment. The"
"2851"	"other pirates envied him this majestic vice, and secretly resolved to"
"2852"	"acquire it shortly. Presently Huck said:"
"2853"	"“What does pirates have to do?”"
"2854"	"Tom said:"
"2855"	"“Oh, they have just a bully time--take ships and burn them, and get the"
"2856"	"money and bury it in awful places in their island where there’s ghosts"
"2857"	"and things to watch it, and kill everybody in the ships--make ‘em walk a"
"2858"	"plank.”"
"2859"	"“And they carry the women to the island,” said Joe; “they don’t kill the"
"2860"	"women.”"
"2861"	"“No,” assented Tom, “they don’t kill the women--they’re too noble. And"
"2862"	"the women’s always beautiful, too."
"2863"	"“And don’t they wear the bulliest clothes! Oh no! All gold and silver"
"2864"	"and di’monds,” said Joe, with enthusiasm."
"2865"	"“Who?” said Huck."
"2866"	"“Why, the pirates.”"
"2867"	"Huck scanned his own clothing forlornly."
"2868"	"“I reckon I ain’t dressed fitten for a pirate,” said he, with a"
"2869"	"regretful pathos in his voice; “but I ain’t got none but these.”"
"2870"	"But the other boys told him the fine clothes would come fast enough,"
"2871"	"after they should have begun their adventures. They made him understand"
"2872"	"that his poor rags would do to begin with, though it was customary for"
"2873"	"wealthy pirates to start with a proper wardrobe."
"2874"	"Gradually their talk died out and drowsiness began to steal upon the"
"2875"	"eyelids of the little waifs. The pipe dropped from the fingers of the"
"2876"	"Red-Handed, and he slept the sleep of the conscience-free and the weary."
"2877"	"The Terror of the Seas and the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main had"
"2878"	"more difficulty in getting to sleep. They said their prayers inwardly,"
"2879"	"and lying down, since there was nobody there with authority to make them"
"2880"	"kneel and recite aloud; in truth, they had a mind not to say them at"
"2881"	"all, but they were afraid to proceed to such lengths as that, lest they"
"2882"	"might call down a sudden and special thunderbolt from heaven. Then at"
"2883"	"once they reached and hovered upon the imminent verge of sleep--but an"
"2884"	"intruder came, now, that would not “down.” It was conscience. They began"
"2885"	"to feel a vague fear that they had been doing wrong to run away; and"
"2886"	"next they thought of the stolen meat, and then the real torture came."
"2887"	"They tried to argue it away by reminding conscience that they had"
"2888"	"purloined sweetmeats and apples scores of times; but conscience was not"
"2889"	"to be appeased by such thin plausibilities; it seemed to them, in the"
"2890"	"end, that there was no getting around the stubborn fact that taking"
"2891"	"sweetmeats was only “hooking,” while taking bacon and hams and such"
"2892"	"valuables was plain simple stealing--and there was a command against that"
"2893"	"in the Bible. So they inwardly resolved that so long as they remained in"
"2894"	"the business, their piracies should not again be sullied with the"
"2895"	"crime of stealing. Then conscience granted a truce, and these curiously"
"2896"	"inconsistent pirates fell peacefully to sleep."
"2897"	"CHAPTER XIV"
"2898"	"WHEN Tom awoke in the morning, he wondered where he was. He sat up and"
"2899"	"rubbed his eyes and looked around. Then he comprehended. It was the cool"
"2900"	"gray dawn, and there was a delicious sense of repose and peace in the"
"2901"	"deep pervading calm and silence of the woods. Not a leaf stirred; not"
"2902"	"a sound obtruded upon great Nature’s meditation. Beaded dewdrops stood"
"2903"	"upon the leaves and grasses. A white layer of ashes covered the fire,"
"2904"	"and a thin blue breath of smoke rose straight into the air. Joe and Huck"
"2905"	"still slept."
"2906"	"Now, far away in the woods a bird called; another answered; presently"
"2907"	"the hammering of a woodpecker was heard. Gradually the cool dim gray"
"2908"	"of the morning whitened, and as gradually sounds multiplied and life"
"2909"	"manifested itself. The marvel of Nature shaking off sleep and going"
"2910"	"to work unfolded itself to the musing boy. A little green worm came"
"2911"	"crawling over a dewy leaf, lifting two-thirds of his body into the air"
"2912"	"from time to time and “sniffing around,” then proceeding again--for he"
"2913"	"was measuring, Tom said; and when the worm approached him, of its own"
"2914"	"accord, he sat as still as a stone, with his hopes rising and falling,"
"2915"	"by turns, as the creature still came toward him or seemed inclined to"
"2916"	"go elsewhere; and when at last it considered a painful moment with its"
"2917"	"curved body in the air and then came decisively down upon Tom’s leg and"
"2918"	"began a journey over him, his whole heart was glad--for that meant that"
"2919"	"he was going to have a new suit of clothes--without the shadow of a"
"2920"	"doubt a gaudy piratical uniform. Now a procession of ants appeared,"
"2921"	"from nowhere in particular, and went about their labors; one struggled"
"2922"	"manfully by with a dead spider five times as big as itself in its arms,"
"2923"	"and lugged it straight up a tree-trunk. A brown spotted lady-bug climbed"
"2924"	"the dizzy height of a grass blade, and Tom bent down close to it and"
"2925"	"said, “Lady-bug, lady-bug, fly away home, your house is on fire, your"
"2926"	"children’s alone,” and she took wing and went off to see about it--which"
"2927"	"did not surprise the boy, for he knew of old that this insect was"
"2928"	"credulous about conflagrations, and he had practised upon its simplicity"
"2929"	"more than once. A tumblebug came next, heaving sturdily at its ball, and"
"2930"	"Tom touched the creature, to see it shut its legs against its body"
"2931"	"and pretend to be dead. The birds were fairly rioting by this time. A"
"2932"	"catbird, the Northern mocker, lit in a tree over Tom’s head, and trilled"
"2933"	"out her imitations of her neighbors in a rapture of enjoyment; then"
"2934"	"a shrill jay swept down, a flash of blue flame, and stopped on a twig"
"2935"	"almost within the boy’s reach, cocked his head to one side and eyed the"
"2936"	"strangers with a consuming curiosity; a gray squirrel and a big fellow"
"2937"	"of the “fox” kind came skurrying along, sitting up at intervals to"
"2938"	"inspect and chatter at the boys, for the wild things had probably never"
"2939"	"seen a human being before and scarcely knew whether to be afraid or not."
"2940"	"All Nature was wide awake and stirring, now; long lances of sunlight"
"2941"	"pierced down through the dense foliage far and near, and a few"
"2942"	"butterflies came fluttering upon the scene."
"2943"	"Tom stirred up the other pirates and they all clattered away with"
"2944"	"a shout, and in a minute or two were stripped and chasing after and"
"2945"	"tumbling over each other in the shallow limpid water of the white"
"2946"	"sandbar. They felt no longing for the little village sleeping in the"
"2947"	"distance beyond the majestic waste of water. A vagrant current or a"
"2948"	"slight rise in the river had carried off their raft, but this only"
"2949"	"gratified them, since its going was something like burning the bridge"
"2950"	"between them and civilization."
"2951"	"They came back to camp wonderfully refreshed, glad-hearted, and"
"2952"	"ravenous; and they soon had the camp-fire blazing up again. Huck found a"
"2953"	"spring of clear cold water close by, and the boys made cups of broad oak"
"2954"	"or hickory leaves, and felt that water, sweetened with such a wildwood"
"2955"	"charm as that, would be a good enough substitute for coffee. While Joe"
"2956"	"was slicing bacon for breakfast, Tom and Huck asked him to hold on a"
"2957"	"minute; they stepped to a promising nook in the river-bank and threw in"
"2958"	"their lines; almost immediately they had reward. Joe had not had time"
"2959"	"to get impatient before they were back again with some handsome bass,"
"2960"	"a couple of sun-perch and a small catfish--provisions enough for quite a"
"2961"	"family. They fried the fish with the bacon, and were astonished; for"
"2962"	"no fish had ever seemed so delicious before. They did not know that the"
"2963"	"quicker a fresh-water fish is on the fire after he is caught the better"
"2964"	"he is; and they reflected little upon what a sauce open-air sleeping,"
"2965"	"open-air exercise, bathing, and a large ingredient of hunger make, too."
"2966"	"They lay around in the shade, after breakfast, while Huck had a smoke,"
"2967"	"and then went off through the woods on an exploring expedition. They"
"2968"	"tramped gayly along, over decaying logs, through tangled underbrush,"
"2969"	"among solemn monarchs of the forest, hung from their crowns to the"
"2970"	"ground with a drooping regalia of grape-vines. Now and then they came"
"2971"	"upon snug nooks carpeted with grass and jeweled with flowers."
"2972"	"They found plenty of things to be delighted with, but nothing to be"
"2973"	"astonished at. They discovered that the island was about three miles"
"2974"	"long and a quarter of a mile wide, and that the shore it lay closest to"
"2975"	"was only separated from it by a narrow channel hardly two hundred yards"
"2976"	"wide. They took a swim about every hour, so it was close upon the middle"
"2977"	"of the afternoon when they got back to camp. They were too hungry to"
"2978"	"stop to fish, but they fared sumptuously upon cold ham, and then threw"
"2979"	"themselves down in the shade to talk. But the talk soon began to drag,"
"2980"	"and then died. The stillness, the solemnity that brooded in the woods,"
"2981"	"and the sense of loneliness, began to tell upon the spirits of the boys."
"2982"	"They fell to thinking. A sort of undefined longing crept upon them. This"
"2983"	"took dim shape, presently--it was budding homesickness. Even Finn the"
"2984"	"Red-Handed was dreaming of his doorsteps and empty hogsheads. But they"
"2985"	"were all ashamed of their weakness, and none was brave enough to speak"
"2986"	"his thought."
"2987"	"For some time, now, the boys had been dully conscious of a peculiar"
"2988"	"sound in the distance, just as one sometimes is of the ticking of a"
"2989"	"clock which he takes no distinct note of. But now this mysterious sound"
"2990"	"became more pronounced, and forced a recognition. The boys started,"
"2991"	"glanced at each other, and then each assumed a listening attitude. There"
"2992"	"was a long silence, profound and unbroken; then a deep, sullen boom came"
"2993"	"floating down out of the distance."
"2994"	"“What is it!” exclaimed Joe, under his breath."
"2995"	"“I wonder,” said Tom in a whisper."
"2996"	"“‘Tain’t thunder,” said Huckleberry, in an awed tone, “becuz thunder--”"
"2997"	"“Hark!” said Tom. “Listen--don’t talk.”"
"2998"	"They waited a time that seemed an age, and then the same muffled boom"
"2999"	"troubled the solemn hush."
"3000"	"“Let’s go and see.”"
"3001"	"They sprang to their feet and hurried to the shore toward the town. They"
"3002"	"parted the bushes on the bank and peered out over the water. The little"
"3003"	"steam ferry-boat was about a mile below the village, drifting with the"
"3004"	"current. Her broad deck seemed crowded with people. There were a great"
"3005"	"many skiffs rowing about or floating with the stream in the neighborhood"
"3006"	"of the ferryboat, but the boys could not determine what the men in"
"3007"	"them were doing. Presently a great jet of white smoke burst from the"
"3008"	"ferryboat’s side, and as it expanded and rose in a lazy cloud, that same"
"3009"	"dull throb of sound was borne to the listeners again."
"3010"	"“I know now!” exclaimed Tom; “somebody’s drownded!”"
"3011"	"“That’s it!” said Huck; “they done that last summer, when Bill Turner"
"3012"	"got drownded; they shoot a cannon over the water, and that makes"
"3013"	"him come up to the top. Yes, and they take loaves of bread and put"
"3014"	"quicksilver in ‘em and set ‘em afloat, and wherever there’s anybody"
"3015"	"that’s drownded, they’ll float right there and stop.”"
"3016"	"“Yes, I’ve heard about that,” said Joe. “I wonder what makes the bread"
"3017"	"do that.”"
"3018"	"“Oh, it ain’t the bread, so much,” said Tom; “I reckon it’s mostly what"
"3019"	"they _say_ over it before they start it out.”"
"3020"	"“But they don’t say anything over it,” said Huck. “I’ve seen ‘em and"
"3021"	"they don’t.”"
"3022"	"“Well, that’s funny,” said Tom. “But maybe they say it to themselves. Of"
"3023"	"_course_ they do. Anybody might know that.”"
"3024"	"The other boys agreed that there was reason in what Tom said, because"
"3025"	"an ignorant lump of bread, uninstructed by an incantation, could not"
"3026"	"be expected to act very intelligently when set upon an errand of such"
"3027"	"gravity."
"3028"	"“By jings, I wish I was over there, now,” said Joe."
"3029"	"“I do too” said Huck “I’d give heaps to know who it is.”"
"3030"	"The boys still listened and watched. Presently a revealing thought"
"3031"	"flashed through Tom’s mind, and he exclaimed:"
"3032"	"“Boys, I know who’s drownded--it’s us!”"
"3033"	"They felt like heroes in an instant. Here was a gorgeous triumph; they"
"3034"	"were missed; they were mourned; hearts were breaking on their account;"
"3035"	"tears were being shed; accusing memories of unkindness to these poor"
"3036"	"lost lads were rising up, and unavailing regrets and remorse were being"
"3037"	"indulged; and best of all, the departed were the talk of the whole town,"
"3038"	"and the envy of all the boys, as far as this dazzling notoriety was"
"3039"	"concerned. This was fine. It was worth while to be a pirate, after all."
"3040"	"As twilight drew on, the ferryboat went back to her accustomed business"
"3041"	"and the skiffs disappeared. The pirates returned to camp. They were"
"3042"	"jubilant with vanity over their new grandeur and the illustrious trouble"
"3043"	"they were making. They caught fish, cooked supper and ate it, and then"
"3044"	"fell to guessing at what the village was thinking and saying about them;"
"3045"	"and the pictures they drew of the public distress on their account were"
"3046"	"gratifying to look upon--from their point of view. But when the shadows"
"3047"	"of night closed them in, they gradually ceased to talk, and sat gazing"
"3048"	"into the fire, with their minds evidently wandering elsewhere. The"
"3049"	"excitement was gone, now, and Tom and Joe could not keep back thoughts"
"3050"	"of certain persons at home who were not enjoying this fine frolic as"
"3051"	"much as they were. Misgivings came; they grew troubled and unhappy; a"
"3052"	"sigh or two escaped, unawares. By and by Joe timidly ventured upon a"
"3053"	"roundabout “feeler” as to how the others might look upon a return to"
"3054"	"civilization--not right now, but--"
"3055"	"Tom withered him with derision! Huck, being uncommitted as yet, joined"
"3056"	"in with Tom, and the waverer quickly “explained,” and was glad to get"
"3057"	"out of the scrape with as little taint of chicken-hearted home-sickness"
"3058"	"clinging to his garments as he could. Mutiny was effectually laid to"
"3059"	"rest for the moment."
"3060"	"As the night deepened, Huck began to nod, and presently to snore."
"3061"	"Joe followed next. Tom lay upon his elbow motionless, for some time,"
"3062"	"watching the two intently. At last he got up cautiously, on his knees,"
"3063"	"and went searching among the grass and the flickering reflections flung"
"3064"	"by the campfire. He picked up and inspected several large semi-cylinders"
"3065"	"of the thin white bark of a sycamore, and finally chose two which seemed"
"3066"	"to suit him. Then he knelt by the fire and painfully wrote something"
"3067"	"upon each of these with his “red keel”; one he rolled up and put in his"
"3068"	"jacket pocket, and the other he put in Joe’s hat and removed it to a"
"3069"	"little distance from the owner. And he also put into the hat certain"
"3070"	"schoolboy treasures of almost inestimable value--among them a lump of"
"3071"	"chalk, an India-rubber ball, three fishhooks, and one of that kind"
"3072"	"of marbles known as a “sure ‘nough crystal.” Then he tiptoed his way"
"3073"	"cautiously among the trees till he felt that he was out of hearing, and"
"3074"	"straightway broke into a keen run in the direction of the sandbar."
"3075"	"CHAPTER XV"
"3076"	"A few minutes later Tom was in the shoal water of the bar, wading toward"
"3077"	"the Illinois shore. Before the depth reached his middle he was halfway"
"3078"	"over; the current would permit no more wading, now, so he struck out"
"3079"	"confidently to swim the remaining hundred yards. He swam quartering"
"3080"	"upstream, but still was swept downward rather faster than he had"
"3081"	"expected. However, he reached the shore finally, and drifted along till"
"3082"	"he found a low place and drew himself out. He put his hand on his jacket"
"3083"	"pocket, found his piece of bark safe, and then struck through the woods,"
"3084"	"following the shore, with streaming garments. Shortly before ten"
"3085"	"o’clock he came out into an open place opposite the village, and saw the"
"3086"	"ferryboat lying in the shadow of the trees and the high bank. Everything"
"3087"	"was quiet under the blinking stars. He crept down the bank, watching"
"3088"	"with all his eyes, slipped into the water, swam three or four strokes"
"3089"	"and climbed into the skiff that did “yawl” duty at the boat’s stern. He"
"3090"	"laid himself down under the thwarts and waited, panting."
"3091"	"Presently the cracked bell tapped and a voice gave the order to “cast"
"3092"	"off.” A minute or two later the skiff’s head was standing high up,"
"3093"	"against the boat’s swell, and the voyage was begun. Tom felt happy in"
"3094"	"his success, for he knew it was the boat’s last trip for the night. At"
"3095"	"the end of a long twelve or fifteen minutes the wheels stopped, and"
"3096"	"Tom slipped overboard and swam ashore in the dusk, landing fifty yards"
"3097"	"downstream, out of danger of possible stragglers."
"3098"	"He flew along unfrequented alleys, and shortly found himself at his"
"3099"	"aunt’s back fence. He climbed over, approached the “ell,” and looked"
"3100"	"in at the sitting-room window, for a light was burning there. There"
"3101"	"sat Aunt Polly, Sid, Mary, and Joe Harper’s mother, grouped together,"
"3102"	"talking. They were by the bed, and the bed was between them and the"
"3103"	"door. Tom went to the door and began to softly lift the latch; then"
"3104"	"he pressed gently and the door yielded a crack; he continued pushing"
"3105"	"cautiously, and quaking every time it creaked, till he judged he might"
"3106"	"squeeze through on his knees; so he put his head through and began,"
"3107"	"warily."
"3108"	"“What makes the candle blow so?” said Aunt Polly. Tom hurried up. “Why,"
"3109"	"that door’s open, I believe. Why, of course it is. No end of strange"
"3110"	"things now. Go ‘long and shut it, Sid.”"
"3111"	"Tom disappeared under the bed just in time. He lay and “breathed”"
"3112"	" himself for a time, and then crept to where he could almost touch his"
"3113"	"aunt’s foot."
"3114"	"“But as I was saying,” said Aunt Polly, “he warn’t _bad_, so to say--only"
"3115"	"misch_ee_vous. Only just giddy, and harum-scarum, you know. He warn’t"
"3116"	"any more responsible than a colt. _He_ never meant any harm, and he was"
"3117"	"the best-hearted boy that ever was”--and she began to cry."
"3118"	"“It was just so with my Joe--always full of his devilment, and up to"
"3119"	"every kind of mischief, but he was just as unselfish and kind as he"
"3120"	"could be--and laws bless me, to think I went and whipped him for taking"
"3121"	"that cream, never once recollecting that I throwed it out myself because"
"3122"	"it was sour, and I never to see him again in this world, never, never,"
"3123"	"never, poor abused boy!” And Mrs. Harper sobbed as if her heart would"
"3124"	"break."
"3125"	"“I hope Tom’s better off where he is,” said Sid, “but if he’d been"
"3126"	"better in some ways--”"
"3127"	"“_Sid!_” Tom felt the glare of the old lady’s eye, though he could not"
"3128"	"see it. “Not a word against my Tom, now that he’s gone! God’ll take care"
"3129"	"of _him_--never you trouble _your_self, sir! Oh, Mrs. Harper, I don’t"
"3130"	"know how to give him up! I don’t know how to give him up! He was such a"
"3131"	"comfort to me, although he tormented my old heart out of me, ‘most.”"
"3132"	"“The Lord giveth and the Lord hath taken away--Blessed be the name of"
"3133"	"the Lord! But it’s so hard--Oh, it’s so hard! Only last Saturday my Joe"
"3134"	"busted a firecracker right under my nose and I knocked him sprawling."
"3135"	"Little did I know then, how soon--Oh, if it was to do over again I’d hug"
"3136"	"him and bless him for it.”"
"3137"	"“Yes, yes, yes, I know just how you feel, Mrs. Harper, I know just"
"3138"	"exactly how you feel. No longer ago than yesterday noon, my Tom took"
"3139"	"and filled the cat full of Pain-killer, and I did think the cretur would"
"3140"	"tear the house down. And God forgive me, I cracked Tom’s head with my"
"3141"	"thimble, poor boy, poor dead boy. But he’s out of all his troubles now."
"3142"	"And the last words I ever heard him say was to reproach--”"
"3143"	"But this memory was too much for the old lady, and she broke entirely"
"3144"	"down. Tom was snuffling, now, himself--and more in pity of himself than"
"3145"	"anybody else. He could hear Mary crying, and putting in a kindly word"
"3146"	"for him from time to time. He began to have a nobler opinion of himself"
"3147"	"than ever before. Still, he was sufficiently touched by his aunt’s grief"
"3148"	"to long to rush out from under the bed and overwhelm her with joy--and"
"3149"	"the theatrical gorgeousness of the thing appealed strongly to his"
"3150"	"nature, too, but he resisted and lay still."
"3151"	"He went on listening, and gathered by odds and ends that it was"
"3152"	"conjectured at first that the boys had got drowned while taking a swim;"
"3153"	"then the small raft had been missed; next, certain boys said the missing"
"3154"	"lads had promised that the village should “hear something” soon; the"
"3155"	"wise-heads had “put this and that together” and decided that the lads"
"3156"	"had gone off on that raft and would turn up at the next town below,"
"3157"	"presently; but toward noon the raft had been found, lodged against the"
"3158"	"Missouri shore some five or six miles below the village--and then hope"
"3159"	"perished; they must be drowned, else hunger would have driven them home"
"3160"	"by nightfall if not sooner. It was believed that the search for the"
"3161"	"bodies had been a fruitless effort merely because the drowning must"
"3162"	"have occurred in mid-channel, since the boys, being good swimmers, would"
"3163"	"otherwise have escaped to shore. This was Wednesday night. If the bodies"
"3164"	"continued missing until Sunday, all hope would be given over, and the"
"3165"	"funerals would be preached on that morning. Tom shuddered."
"3166"	"Mrs. Harper gave a sobbing goodnight and turned to go. Then with a"
"3167"	"mutual impulse the two bereaved women flung themselves into each other’s"
"3168"	"arms and had a good, consoling cry, and then parted. Aunt Polly was"
"3169"	"tender far beyond her wont, in her goodnight to Sid and Mary. Sid"
"3170"	"snuffled a bit and Mary went off crying with all her heart."
"3171"	"Aunt Polly knelt down and prayed for Tom so touchingly, so appealingly,"
"3172"	"and with such measureless love in her words and her old trembling voice,"
"3173"	"that he was weltering in tears again, long before she was through."
"3174"	"He had to keep still long after she went to bed, for she kept making"
"3175"	"broken-hearted ejaculations from time to time, tossing unrestfully, and"
"3176"	"turning over. But at last she was still, only moaning a little in her"
"3177"	"sleep. Now the boy stole out, rose gradually by the bedside, shaded the"
"3178"	"candle-light with his hand, and stood regarding her. His heart was full"
"3179"	"of pity for her. He took out his sycamore scroll and placed it by the"
"3180"	"candle. But something occurred to him, and he lingered considering."
"3181"	"His face lighted with a happy solution of his thought; he put the bark"
"3182"	"hastily in his pocket. Then he bent over and kissed the faded lips, and"
"3183"	"straightway made his stealthy exit, latching the door behind him."
"3184"	"He threaded his way back to the ferry landing, found nobody at large"
"3185"	"there, and walked boldly on board the boat, for he knew she was"
"3186"	"tenantless except that there was a watchman, who always turned in and"
"3187"	"slept like a graven image. He untied the skiff at the stern, slipped"
"3188"	"into it, and was soon rowing cautiously upstream. When he had pulled a"
"3189"	"mile above the village, he started quartering across and bent himself"
"3190"	"stoutly to his work. He hit the landing on the other side neatly, for"
"3191"	"this was a familiar bit of work to him. He was moved to capture"
"3192"	"the skiff, arguing that it might be considered a ship and therefore"
"3193"	"legitimate prey for a pirate, but he knew a thorough search would be"
"3194"	"made for it and that might end in revelations. So he stepped ashore and"
"3195"	"entered the woods."
"3196"	"He sat down and took a long rest, torturing himself meanwhile to keep"
"3197"	"awake, and then started warily down the home-stretch. The night was far"
"3198"	"spent. It was broad daylight before he found himself fairly abreast the"
"3199"	"island bar. He rested again until the sun was well up and gilding the"
"3200"	"great river with its splendor, and then he plunged into the stream. A"
"3201"	"little later he paused, dripping, upon the threshold of the camp, and"
"3202"	"heard Joe say:"
"3203"	"“No, Tom’s true-blue, Huck, and he’ll come back. He won’t desert. He"
"3204"	"knows that would be a disgrace to a pirate, and Tom’s too proud for that"
"3205"	"sort of thing. He’s up to something or other. Now I wonder what?”"
"3206"	"“Well, the things is ours, anyway, ain’t they?”"
"3207"	"“Pretty near, but not yet, Huck. The writing says they are if he ain’t"
"3208"	"back here to breakfast.”"
"3209"	"“Which he is!” exclaimed Tom, with fine dramatic effect, stepping"
"3210"	"grandly into camp."
"3211"	"A sumptuous breakfast of bacon and fish was shortly provided, and as the"
"3212"	"boys set to work upon it, Tom recounted (and adorned) his adventures."
"3213"	"They were a vain and boastful company of heroes when the tale was done."
"3214"	"Then Tom hid himself away in a shady nook to sleep till noon, and the"
"3215"	"other pirates got ready to fish and explore."
"3216"	"CHAPTER XVI"
"3217"	"AFTER dinner all the gang turned out to hunt for turtle eggs on the bar."
"3218"	"They went about poking sticks into the sand, and when they found a soft"
"3219"	"place they went down on their knees and dug with their hands. Sometimes"
"3220"	"they would take fifty or sixty eggs out of one hole. They were perfectly"
"3221"	"round white things a trifle smaller than an English walnut. They had a"
"3222"	"famous fried-egg feast that night, and another on Friday morning."
"3223"	"After breakfast they went whooping and prancing out on the bar, and"
"3224"	"chased each other round and round, shedding clothes as they went, until"
"3225"	"they were naked, and then continued the frolic far away up the shoal"
"3226"	"water of the bar, against the stiff current, which latter tripped their"
"3227"	"legs from under them from time to time and greatly increased the fun."
"3228"	"And now and then they stooped in a group and splashed water in each"
"3229"	"other’s faces with their palms, gradually approaching each other, with"
"3230"	"averted faces to avoid the strangling sprays, and finally gripping and"
"3231"	"struggling till the best man ducked his neighbor, and then they all"
"3232"	"went under in a tangle of white legs and arms and came up blowing,"
"3233"	"sputtering, laughing, and gasping for breath at one and the same time."
"3234"	"When they were well exhausted, they would run out and sprawl on the dry,"
"3235"	"hot sand, and lie there and cover themselves up with it, and by and by"
"3236"	"break for the water again and go through the original performance once"
"3237"	"more. Finally it occurred to them that their naked skin represented"
"3238"	"flesh-colored “tights” very fairly; so they drew a ring in the sand and"
"3239"	"had a circus--with three clowns in it, for none would yield this proudest"
"3240"	"post to his neighbor."
"3241"	"Next they got their marbles and played “knucks” and “ringtaw” and"
"3242"	"“keeps” till that amusement grew stale. Then Joe and Huck had another"
"3243"	"swim, but Tom would not venture, because he found that in kicking off"
"3244"	"his trousers he had kicked his string of rattlesnake rattles off his"
"3245"	"ankle, and he wondered how he had escaped cramp so long without the"
"3246"	"protection of this mysterious charm. He did not venture again until he"
"3247"	"had found it, and by that time the other boys were tired and ready to"
"3248"	"rest. They gradually wandered apart, dropped into the “dumps,” and"
"3249"	"fell to gazing longingly across the wide river to where the village lay"
"3250"	"drowsing in the sun. Tom found himself writing “BECKY” in the sand with"
"3251"	"his big toe; he scratched it out, and was angry with himself for his"
"3252"	"weakness. But he wrote it again, nevertheless; he could not help it. He"
"3253"	"erased it once more and then took himself out of temptation by driving"
"3254"	"the other boys together and joining them."
"3255"	"But Joe’s spirits had gone down almost beyond resurrection. He was so"
"3256"	"homesick that he could hardly endure the misery of it. The tears lay"
"3257"	"very near the surface. Huck was melancholy, too. Tom was downhearted,"
"3258"	"but tried hard not to show it. He had a secret which he was not ready"
"3259"	"to tell, yet, but if this mutinous depression was not broken up soon, he"
"3260"	"would have to bring it out. He said, with a great show of cheerfulness:"
"3261"	"“I bet there’s been pirates on this island before, boys. We’ll explore"
"3262"	"it again. They’ve hid treasures here somewhere. How’d you feel to light"
"3263"	"on a rotten chest full of gold and silver--hey?”"
"3264"	"But it roused only faint enthusiasm, which faded out, with no reply."
"3265"	"Tom tried one or two other seductions; but they failed, too. It was"
"3266"	"discouraging work. Joe sat poking up the sand with a stick and looking"
"3267"	"very gloomy. Finally he said:"
"3268"	"“Oh, boys, let’s give it up. I want to go home. It’s so lonesome.”"
"3269"	"“Oh no, Joe, you’ll feel better by and by,” said Tom. “Just think of the"
"3270"	"fishing that’s here.”"
"3271"	"“I don’t care for fishing. I want to go home.”"
"3272"	"“But, Joe, there ain’t such another swimming-place anywhere.”"
"3273"	"“Swimming’s no good. I don’t seem to care for it, somehow, when there"
"3274"	"ain’t anybody to say I sha’n’t go in. I mean to go home.”"
"3275"	"“Oh, shucks! Baby! You want to see your mother, I reckon.”"
"3276"	"“Yes, I _do_ want to see my mother--and you would, too, if you had one. I"
"3277"	"ain’t any more baby than you are.” And Joe snuffled a little."
"3278"	"“Well, we’ll let the crybaby go home to his mother, won’t we, Huck? Poor"
"3279"	"thing--does it want to see its mother? And so it shall. You like it here,"
"3280"	"don’t you, Huck? We’ll stay, won’t we?”"
"3281"	"Huck said, “Y-e-s”--without any heart in it."
"3282"	"“I’ll never speak to you again as long as I live,” said Joe, rising."
"3283"	"“There now!” And he moved moodily away and began to dress himself."
"3284"	"“Who cares!” said Tom. “Nobody wants you to. Go ‘long home and get"
"3285"	"laughed at. Oh, you’re a nice pirate. Huck and me ain’t crybabies. We’ll"
"3286"	"stay, won’t we, Huck? Let him go if he wants to. I reckon we can get"
"3287"	"along without him, per’aps.”"
"3288"	"But Tom was uneasy, nevertheless, and was alarmed to see Joe go sullenly"
"3289"	"on with his dressing. And then it was discomforting to see Huck eying"
"3290"	"Joe’s preparations so wistfully, and keeping up such an ominous silence."
"3291"	"Presently, without a parting word, Joe began to wade off toward the"
"3292"	"Illinois shore. Tom’s heart began to sink. He glanced at Huck. Huck"
"3293"	"could not bear the look, and dropped his eyes. Then he said:"
"3294"	"“I want to go, too, Tom. It was getting so lonesome anyway, and now"
"3295"	"it’ll be worse. Let’s us go, too, Tom.”"
"3296"	"“I won’t! You can all go, if you want to. I mean to stay.”"
"3297"	"“Tom, I better go.”"
"3298"	"“Well, go ‘long--who’s hendering you.”"
"3299"	"Huck began to pick up his scattered clothes. He said:"
"3300"	"“Tom, I wisht you’d come, too. Now you think it over. We’ll wait for you"
"3301"	"when we get to shore.”"
"3302"	"“Well, you’ll wait a blame long time, that’s all.”"
"3303"	"Huck started sorrowfully away, and Tom stood looking after him, with a"
"3304"	"strong desire tugging at his heart to yield his pride and go along"
"3305"	"too. He hoped the boys would stop, but they still waded slowly on. It"
"3306"	"suddenly dawned on Tom that it was become very lonely and still. He made"
"3307"	"one final struggle with his pride, and then darted after his comrades,"
"3308"	"yelling:"
"3309"	"“Wait! Wait! I want to tell you something!”"
"3310"	"They presently stopped and turned around. When he got to where they"
"3311"	"were, he began unfolding his secret, and they listened moodily till"
"3312"	"at last they saw the “point” he was driving at, and then they set up a"
"3313"	"warwhoop of applause and said it was “splendid!” and said if he had"
"3314"	"told them at first, they wouldn’t have started away. He made a plausible"
"3315"	"excuse; but his real reason had been the fear that not even the secret"
"3316"	"would keep them with him any very great length of time, and so he had"
"3317"	"meant to hold it in reserve as a last seduction."
"3318"	"The lads came gayly back and went at their sports again with a will,"
"3319"	"chattering all the time about Tom’s stupendous plan and admiring the"
"3320"	"genius of it. After a dainty egg and fish dinner, Tom said he wanted to"
"3321"	"learn to smoke, now. Joe caught at the idea and said he would like to"
"3322"	"try, too. So Huck made pipes and filled them. These novices had never"
"3323"	"smoked anything before but cigars made of grapevine, and they “bit” the"
"3324"	"tongue, and were not considered manly anyway."
"3325"	"Now they stretched themselves out on their elbows and began to puff,"
"3326"	"charily, and with slender confidence. The smoke had an unpleasant taste,"
"3327"	"and they gagged a little, but Tom said:"
"3328"	"“Why, it’s just as easy! If I’d a knowed this was all, I’d a learnt long"
"3329"	"ago.”"
"3330"	"“So would I,” said Joe. “It’s just nothing.”"
"3331"	"“Why, many a time I’ve looked at people smoking, and thought well I wish"
"3332"	"I could do that; but I never thought I could,” said Tom."
"3333"	"“That’s just the way with me, hain’t it, Huck? You’ve heard me talk just"
"3334"	"that way--haven’t you, Huck? I’ll leave it to Huck if I haven’t.”"
"3335"	"“Yes--heaps of times,” said Huck."
"3336"	"“Well, I have too,” said Tom; “oh, hundreds of times. Once down by the"
"3337"	"slaughter-house. Don’t you remember, Huck? Bob Tanner was there, and"
"3338"	"Johnny Miller, and Jeff Thatcher, when I said it. Don’t you remember,"
"3339"	"Huck, ‘bout me saying that?”"
"3340"	"“Yes, that’s so,” said Huck. “That was the day after I lost a white"
"3341"	"alley. No, ‘twas the day before.”"
"3342"	"“There--I told you so,” said Tom. “Huck recollects it.”"
"3343"	"“I bleeve I could smoke this pipe all day,” said Joe. “I don’t feel"
"3344"	"sick.”"
"3345"	"“Neither do I,” said Tom. “I could smoke it all day. But I bet you Jeff"
"3346"	"Thatcher couldn’t.”"
"3347"	"“Jeff Thatcher! Why, he’d keel over just with two draws. Just let him"
"3348"	"try it once. _He’d_ see!”"
"3349"	"“I bet he would. And Johnny Miller--I wish could see Johnny Miller tackle"
"3350"	"it once.”"
"3351"	"“Oh, don’t I!” said Joe. “Why, I bet you Johnny Miller couldn’t any more"
"3352"	"do this than nothing. Just one little snifter would fetch _him_.”"
"3353"	"“‘Deed it would, Joe. Say--I wish the boys could see us now.”"
"3354"	"“So do I.”"
"3355"	"“Say--boys, don’t say anything about it, and some time when they’re"
"3356"	"around, I’ll come up to you and say, ‘Joe, got a pipe? I want a smoke.’"
"3357"	"And you’ll say, kind of careless like, as if it warn’t anything, you’ll"
"3358"	"say, ‘Yes, I got my _old_ pipe, and another one, but my tobacker ain’t"
"3359"	"very good.’ And I’ll say, ‘Oh, that’s all right, if it’s _strong_"
"3360"	"enough.’ And then you’ll out with the pipes, and we’ll light up just as"
"3361"	"ca’m, and then just see ‘em look!”"
"3362"	"“By jings, that’ll be gay, Tom! I wish it was _now_!”"
"3363"	"“So do I! And when we tell ‘em we learned when we was off pirating,"
"3364"	"won’t they wish they’d been along?”"
"3365"	"“Oh, I reckon not! I’ll just _bet_ they will!”"
"3366"	"So the talk ran on. But presently it began to flag a trifle, and"
"3367"	"grow disjointed. The silences widened; the expectoration marvellously"
"3368"	"increased. Every pore inside the boys’ cheeks became a spouting"
"3369"	"fountain; they could scarcely bail out the cellars under their tongues"
"3370"	"fast enough to prevent an inundation; little overflowings down their"
"3371"	"throats occurred in spite of all they could do, and sudden retchings"
"3372"	"followed every time. Both boys were looking very pale and miserable,"
"3373"	"now. Joe’s pipe dropped from his nerveless fingers. Tom’s followed. Both"
"3374"	"fountains were going furiously and both pumps bailing with might and"
"3375"	"main. Joe said feebly:"
"3376"	"“I’ve lost my knife. I reckon I better go and find it.”"
"3377"	"Tom said, with quivering lips and halting utterance:"
"3378"	"“I’ll help you. You go over that way and I’ll hunt around by the spring."
"3379"	"No, you needn’t come, Huck--we can find it.”"
"3380"	"So Huck sat down again, and waited an hour. Then he found it lonesome,"
"3381"	"and went to find his comrades. They were wide apart in the woods, both"
"3382"	"very pale, both fast asleep. But something informed him that if they had"
"3383"	"had any trouble they had got rid of it."
"3384"	"They were not talkative at supper that night. They had a humble look,"
"3385"	"and when Huck prepared his pipe after the meal and was going to prepare"
"3386"	"theirs, they said no, they were not feeling very well--something they ate"
"3387"	"at dinner had disagreed with them."
"3388"	"About midnight Joe awoke, and called the boys. There was a brooding"
"3389"	"oppressiveness in the air that seemed to bode something. The boys"
"3390"	"huddled themselves together and sought the friendly companionship of"
"3391"	"the fire, though the dull dead heat of the breathless atmosphere was"
"3392"	"stifling. They sat still, intent and waiting. The solemn hush continued."
"3393"	"Beyond the light of the fire everything was swallowed up in the"
"3394"	"blackness of darkness. Presently there came a quivering glow that"
"3395"	"vaguely revealed the foliage for a moment and then vanished. By and by"
"3396"	"another came, a little stronger. Then another. Then a faint moan came"
"3397"	"sighing through the branches of the forest and the boys felt a fleeting"
"3398"	"breath upon their cheeks, and shuddered with the fancy that the Spirit"
"3399"	"of the Night had gone by. There was a pause. Now a weird flash turned"
"3400"	"night into day and showed every little grassblade, separate and"
"3401"	"distinct, that grew about their feet. And it showed three white,"
"3402"	"startled faces, too. A deep peal of thunder went rolling and tumbling"
"3403"	"down the heavens and lost itself in sullen rumblings in the distance. A"
"3404"	"sweep of chilly air passed by, rustling all the leaves and snowing the"
"3405"	"flaky ashes broadcast about the fire. Another fierce glare lit up the"
"3406"	"forest and an instant crash followed that seemed to rend the treetops"
"3407"	"right over the boys’ heads. They clung together in terror, in the thick"
"3408"	"gloom that followed. A few big raindrops fell pattering upon the leaves."
"3409"	"“Quick! boys, go for the tent!” exclaimed Tom."
"3410"	"They sprang away, stumbling over roots and among vines in the dark, no"
"3411"	"two plunging in the same direction. A furious blast roared through"
"3412"	"the trees, making everything sing as it went. One blinding flash after"
"3413"	"another came, and peal on peal of deafening thunder. And now a drenching"
"3414"	"rain poured down and the rising hurricane drove it in sheets along the"
"3415"	"ground. The boys cried out to each other, but the roaring wind and the"
"3416"	"booming thunderblasts drowned their voices utterly. However, one by one"
"3417"	"they straggled in at last and took shelter under the tent, cold, scared,"
"3418"	"and streaming with water; but to have company in misery seemed something"
"3419"	"to be grateful for. They could not talk, the old sail flapped so"
"3420"	"furiously, even if the other noises would have allowed them. The tempest"
"3421"	"rose higher and higher, and presently the sail tore loose from its"
"3422"	"fastenings and went winging away on the blast. The boys seized each"
"3423"	"others’ hands and fled, with many tumblings and bruises, to the shelter"
"3424"	"of a great oak that stood upon the riverbank. Now the battle was at its"
"3425"	"highest. Under the ceaseless conflagration of lightning that flamed"
"3426"	"in the skies, everything below stood out in cleancut and shadowless"
"3427"	"distinctness: the bending trees, the billowy river, white with foam, the"
"3428"	"driving spray of spumeflakes, the dim outlines of the high bluffs on"
"3429"	"the other side, glimpsed through the drifting cloudrack and the slanting"
"3430"	"veil of rain. Every little while some giant tree yielded the fight"
"3431"	"and fell crashing through the younger growth; and the unflagging"
"3432"	"thunderpeals came now in ear-splitting explosive bursts, keen and sharp,"
"3433"	"and unspeakably appalling. The storm culminated in one matchless effort"
"3434"	"that seemed likely to tear the island to pieces, burn it up, drown it to"
"3435"	"the treetops, blow it away, and deafen every creature in it, all at one"
"3436"	"and the same moment. It was a wild night for homeless young heads to be"
"3437"	"out in."
"3438"	"But at last the battle was done, and the forces retired with weaker and"
"3439"	"weaker threatenings and grumblings, and peace resumed her sway. The"
"3440"	"boys went back to camp, a good deal awed; but they found there was still"
"3441"	"something to be thankful for, because the great sycamore, the shelter"
"3442"	"of their beds, was a ruin, now, blasted by the lightnings, and they were"
"3443"	"not under it when the catastrophe happened."
"3444"	"Everything in camp was drenched, the campfire as well; for they were but"
"3445"	"heedless lads, like their generation, and had made no provision against"
"3446"	"rain. Here was matter for dismay, for they were soaked through and"
"3447"	"chilled. They were eloquent in their distress; but they presently"
"3448"	"discovered that the fire had eaten so far up under the great log it had"
"3449"	"been built against (where it curved upward and separated itself from"
"3450"	"the ground), that a handbreadth or so of it had escaped wetting; so they"
"3451"	"patiently wrought until, with shreds and bark gathered from the under"
"3452"	"sides of sheltered logs, they coaxed the fire to burn again. Then they"
"3453"	"piled on great dead boughs till they had a roaring furnace, and were"
"3454"	"gladhearted once more. They dried their boiled ham and had a feast,"
"3455"	"and after that they sat by the fire and expanded and glorified their"
"3456"	"midnight adventure until morning, for there was not a dry spot to sleep"
"3457"	"on, anywhere around."
"3458"	"As the sun began to steal in upon the boys, drowsiness came over"
"3459"	"them, and they went out on the sandbar and lay down to sleep. They got"
"3460"	"scorched out by and by, and drearily set about getting breakfast. After"
"3461"	"the meal they felt rusty, and stiff-jointed, and a little homesick once"
"3462"	"more. Tom saw the signs, and fell to cheering up the pirates as well as"
"3463"	"he could. But they cared nothing for marbles, or circus, or swimming, or"
"3464"	"anything. He reminded them of the imposing secret, and raised a ray of"
"3465"	"cheer. While it lasted, he got them interested in a new device. This was"
"3466"	"to knock off being pirates, for a while, and be Indians for a change."
"3467"	"They were attracted by this idea; so it was not long before they were"
"3468"	"stripped, and striped from head to heel with black mud, like so many"
"3469"	"zebras--all of them chiefs, of course--and then they went tearing through"
"3470"	"the woods to attack an English settlement."
"3471"	"By and by they separated into three hostile tribes, and darted upon each"
"3472"	"other from ambush with dreadful warwhoops, and killed and scalped each"
"3473"	"other by thousands. It was a gory day. Consequently it was an extremely"
"3474"	"satisfactory one."
"3475"	"They assembled in camp toward suppertime, hungry and happy; but now"
"3476"	"a difficulty arose--hostile Indians could not break the bread of"
"3477"	"hospitality together without first making peace, and this was a simple"
"3478"	"impossibility without smoking a pipe of peace. There was no other"
"3479"	"process that ever they had heard of. Two of the savages almost wished"
"3480"	"they had remained pirates. However, there was no other way; so with such"
"3481"	"show of cheerfulness as they could muster they called for the pipe and"
"3482"	"took their whiff as it passed, in due form."
"3483"	"And behold, they were glad they had gone into savagery, for they had"
"3484"	"gained something; they found that they could now smoke a little without"
"3485"	"having to go and hunt for a lost knife; they did not get sick enough to"
"3486"	"be seriously uncomfortable. They were not likely to fool away this high"
"3487"	"promise for lack of effort. No, they practised cautiously, after supper,"
"3488"	"with right fair success, and so they spent a jubilant evening. They were"
"3489"	"prouder and happier in their new acquirement than they would have been"
"3490"	"in the scalping and skinning of the Six Nations. We will leave them to"
"3491"	"smoke and chatter and brag, since we have no further use for them at"
"3492"	"present."
"3493"	"CHAPTER XVII"
"3494"	"BUT there was no hilarity in the little town that same tranquil Saturday"
"3495"	"afternoon. The Harpers, and Aunt Polly’s family, were being put into"
"3496"	"mourning, with great grief and many tears. An unusual quiet possessed"
"3497"	"the village, although it was ordinarily quiet enough, in all conscience."
"3498"	"The villagers conducted their concerns with an absent air, and talked"
"3499"	"little; but they sighed often. The Saturday holiday seemed a burden to"
"3500"	"the children. They had no heart in their sports, and gradually gave them"
"3501"	"up."
"3502"	"In the afternoon Becky Thatcher found herself moping about the deserted"
"3503"	"schoolhouse yard, and feeling very melancholy. But she found nothing"
"3504"	"there to comfort her. She soliloquized:"
"3505"	"“Oh, if I only had a brass andiron-knob again! But I haven’t got"
"3506"	"anything now to remember him by.” And she choked back a little sob."
"3507"	"Presently she stopped, and said to herself:"
"3508"	"“It was right here. Oh, if it was to do over again, I wouldn’t say"
"3509"	"that--I wouldn’t say it for the whole world. But he’s gone now; I’ll"
"3510"	"never, never, never see him any more.”"
"3511"	"This thought broke her down, and she wandered away, with tears rolling"
"3512"	"down her cheeks. Then quite a group of boys and girls--playmates of Tom’s"
"3513"	"and Joe’s--came by, and stood looking over the paling fence and talking"
"3514"	"in reverent tones of how Tom did so-and-so the last time they saw"
"3515"	"him, and how Joe said this and that small trifle (pregnant with awful"
"3516"	"prophecy, as they could easily see now!)--and each speaker pointed out"
"3517"	"the exact spot where the lost lads stood at the time, and then added"
"3518"	"something like “and I was a-standing just so--just as I am now, and as if"
"3519"	"you was him--I was as close as that--and he smiled, just this way--and then"
"3520"	"something seemed to go all over me, like--awful, you know--and I never"
"3521"	"thought what it meant, of course, but I can see now!”"
"3522"	"Then there was a dispute about who saw the dead boys last in life, and"
"3523"	"many claimed that dismal distinction, and offered evidences, more or"
"3524"	"less tampered with by the witness; and when it was ultimately decided"
"3525"	"who _did_ see the departed last, and exchanged the last words with them,"
"3526"	"the lucky parties took upon themselves a sort of sacred importance,"
"3527"	"and were gaped at and envied by all the rest. One poor chap, who had"
"3528"	"no other grandeur to offer, said with tolerably manifest pride in the"
"3529"	"remembrance:"
"3530"	"“Well, Tom Sawyer he licked me once.”"
"3531"	"But that bid for glory was a failure. Most of the boys could say that,"
"3532"	"and so that cheapened the distinction too much. The group loitered away,"
"3533"	"still recalling memories of the lost heroes, in awed voices."
"3534"	"When the Sunday-school hour was finished, the next morning, the bell"
"3535"	"began to toll, instead of ringing in the usual way. It was a very still"
"3536"	"Sabbath, and the mournful sound seemed in keeping with the musing hush"
"3537"	"that lay upon nature. The villagers began to gather, loitering a moment"
"3538"	"in the vestibule to converse in whispers about the sad event. But there"
"3539"	"was no whispering in the house; only the funereal rustling of dresses"
"3540"	"as the women gathered to their seats disturbed the silence there. None"
"3541"	"could remember when the little church had been so full before. There"
"3542"	"was finally a waiting pause, an expectant dumbness, and then Aunt Polly"
"3543"	"entered, followed by Sid and Mary, and they by the Harper family, all in"
"3544"	"deep black, and the whole congregation, the old minister as well, rose"
"3545"	"reverently and stood until the mourners were seated in the front pew."
"3546"	"There was another communing silence, broken at intervals by muffled"
"3547"	"sobs, and then the minister spread his hands abroad and prayed. A moving"
"3548"	"hymn was sung, and the text followed: “I am the Resurrection and the"
"3549"	"Life.”"
"3550"	"As the service proceeded, the clergyman drew such pictures of the"
"3551"	"graces, the winning ways, and the rare promise of the lost lads that"
"3552"	"every soul there, thinking he recognized these pictures, felt a pang"
"3553"	"in remembering that he had persistently blinded himself to them always"
"3554"	"before, and had as persistently seen only faults and flaws in the poor"
"3555"	"boys. The minister related many a touching incident in the lives of the"
"3556"	"departed, too, which illustrated their sweet, generous natures, and the"
"3557"	"people could easily see, now, how noble and beautiful those episodes"
"3558"	"were, and remembered with grief that at the time they occurred they had"
"3559"	"seemed rank rascalities, well deserving of the cowhide. The congregation"
"3560"	"became more and more moved, as the pathetic tale went on, till at last"
"3561"	"the whole company broke down and joined the weeping mourners in a chorus"
"3562"	"of anguished sobs, the preacher himself giving way to his feelings, and"
"3563"	"crying in the pulpit."
"3564"	"There was a rustle in the gallery, which nobody noticed; a moment later"
"3565"	"the church door creaked; the minister raised his streaming eyes above"
"3566"	"his handkerchief, and stood transfixed! First one and then another pair"
"3567"	"of eyes followed the minister’s, and then almost with one impulse the"
"3568"	"congregation rose and stared while the three dead boys came marching up"
"3569"	"the aisle, Tom in the lead, Joe next, and Huck, a ruin of drooping rags,"
"3570"	"sneaking sheepishly in the rear! They had been hid in the unused gallery"
"3571"	"listening to their own funeral sermon!"
"3572"	"Aunt Polly, Mary, and the Harpers threw themselves upon their restored"
"3573"	"ones, smothered them with kisses and poured out thanksgivings, while"
"3574"	"poor Huck stood abashed and uncomfortable, not knowing exactly what"
"3575"	"to do or where to hide from so many unwelcoming eyes. He wavered, and"
"3576"	"started to slink away, but Tom seized him and said:"
"3577"	"“Aunt Polly, it ain’t fair. Somebody’s got to be glad to see Huck.”"
"3578"	"“And so they shall. I’m glad to see him, poor motherless thing!” And"
"3579"	"the loving attentions Aunt Polly lavished upon him were the one thing"
"3580"	"capable of making him more uncomfortable than he was before."
"3581"	"Suddenly the minister shouted at the top of his voice: “Praise God from"
"3582"	"whom all blessings flow--_sing_!--and put your hearts in it!”"
"3583"	"And they did. Old Hundred swelled up with a triumphant burst, and"
"3584"	"while it shook the rafters Tom Sawyer the Pirate looked around upon the"
"3585"	"envying juveniles about him and confessed in his heart that this was the"
"3586"	"proudest moment of his life."
"3587"	"As the “sold” congregation trooped out they said they would almost be"
"3588"	"willing to be made ridiculous again to hear Old Hundred sung like that"
"3589"	"once more."
"3590"	"Tom got more cuffs and kisses that day--according to Aunt Polly’s varying"
"3591"	"moods--than he had earned before in a year; and he hardly knew which"
"3592"	"expressed the most gratefulness to God and affection for himself."
"3593"	"CHAPTER XVIII"
"3594"	"THAT was Tom’s great secret--the scheme to return home with his brother"
"3595"	"pirates and attend their own funerals. They had paddled over to the"
"3596"	"Missouri shore on a log, at dusk on Saturday, landing five or six miles"
"3597"	"below the village; they had slept in the woods at the edge of the town"
"3598"	"till nearly daylight, and had then crept through back lanes and alleys"
"3599"	"and finished their sleep in the gallery of the church among a chaos of"
"3600"	"invalided benches."
"3601"	"At breakfast, Monday morning, Aunt Polly and Mary were very loving to"
"3602"	"Tom, and very attentive to his wants. There was an unusual amount of"
"3603"	"talk. In the course of it Aunt Polly said:"
"3604"	"“Well, I don’t say it wasn’t a fine joke, Tom, to keep everybody"
"3605"	"suffering ‘most a week so you boys had a good time, but it is a pity you"
"3606"	"could be so hard-hearted as to let me suffer so. If you could come over"
"3607"	"on a log to go to your funeral, you could have come over and give me a"
"3608"	"hint some way that you warn’t dead, but only run off.”"
"3609"	"“Yes, you could have done that, Tom,” said Mary; “and I believe you"
"3610"	"would if you had thought of it.”"
"3611"	"“Would you, Tom?” said Aunt Polly, her face lighting wistfully. “Say,"
"3612"	"now, would you, if you’d thought of it?”"
"3613"	"“I--well, I don’t know. ‘Twould ‘a’ spoiled everything.”"
"3614"	"“Tom, I hoped you loved me that much,” said Aunt Polly, with a grieved"
"3615"	"tone that discomforted the boy. “It would have been something if you’d"
"3616"	"cared enough to _think_ of it, even if you didn’t _do_ it.”"
"3617"	"“Now, auntie, that ain’t any harm,” pleaded Mary; “it’s only Tom’s giddy"
"3618"	"way--he is always in such a rush that he never thinks of anything.”"
"3619"	"“More’s the pity. Sid would have thought. And Sid would have come and"
"3620"	"_done_ it, too. Tom, you’ll look back, some day, when it’s too late,"
"3621"	"and wish you’d cared a little more for me when it would have cost you so"
"3622"	"little.”"
"3623"	"“Now, auntie, you know I do care for you,” said Tom."
"3624"	"“I’d know it better if you acted more like it.”"
"3625"	"“I wish now I’d thought,” said Tom, with a repentant tone; “but I dreamt"
"3626"	"about you, anyway. That’s something, ain’t it?”"
"3627"	"“It ain’t much--a cat does that much--but it’s better than nothing. What"
"3628"	"did you dream?”"
"3629"	"“Why, Wednesday night I dreamt that you was sitting over there by the"
"3630"	"bed, and Sid was sitting by the woodbox, and Mary next to him.”"
"3631"	"“Well, so we did. So we always do. I’m glad your dreams could take even"
"3632"	"that much trouble about us.”"
"3633"	"“And I dreamt that Joe Harper’s mother was here.”"
"3634"	"“Why, she was here! Did you dream any more?”"
"3635"	"“Oh, lots. But it’s so dim, now.”"
"3636"	"“Well, try to recollect--can’t you?”"
"3637"	"“Somehow it seems to me that the wind--the wind blowed the--the--”"
"3638"	"“Try harder, Tom! The wind did blow something. Come!”"
"3639"	"Tom pressed his fingers on his forehead an anxious minute, and then"
"3640"	"said:"
"3641"	"“I’ve got it now! I’ve got it now! It blowed the candle!”"
"3642"	"“Mercy on us! Go on, Tom--go on!”"
"3643"	"“And it seems to me that you said, ‘Why, I believe that that door--’”"
"3644"	"“Go _on_, Tom!”"
"3645"	"“Just let me study a moment--just a moment. Oh, yes--you said you believed"
"3646"	"the door was open.”"
"3647"	"“As I’m sitting here, I did! Didn’t I, Mary! Go on!”"
"3648"	"“And then--and then--well I won’t be certain, but it seems like as if you"
"3649"	"made Sid go and--and--”"
"3650"	"“Well? Well? What did I make him do, Tom? What did I make him do?”"
"3651"	"“You made him--you--Oh, you made him shut it.”"
"3652"	"“Well, for the land’s sake! I never heard the beat of that in all my"
"3653"	"days! Don’t tell _me_ there ain’t anything in dreams, any more. Sereny"
"3654"	"Harper shall know of this before I’m an hour older. I’d like to see her"
"3655"	"get around _this_ with her rubbage ‘bout superstition. Go on, Tom!”"
"3656"	"“Oh, it’s all getting just as bright as day, now. Next you said I warn’t"
"3657"	"_bad_, only mischeevous and harum-scarum, and not any more responsible"
"3658"	"than--than--I think it was a colt, or something.”"
"3659"	"“And so it was! Well, goodness gracious! Go on, Tom!”"
"3660"	"“And then you began to cry.”"
"3661"	"“So I did. So I did. Not the first time, neither. And then--”"
"3662"	"“Then Mrs. Harper she began to cry, and said Joe was just the same, and"
"3663"	"she wished she hadn’t whipped him for taking cream when she’d throwed it"
"3664"	"out her own self--”"
"3665"	"“Tom! The sperrit was upon you! You was a prophesying--that’s what you"
"3666"	"was doing! Land alive, go on, Tom!”"
"3667"	"“Then Sid he said--he said--”"
"3668"	"“I don’t think I said anything,” said Sid."
"3669"	"“Yes you did, Sid,” said Mary."
"3670"	"“Shut your heads and let Tom go on! What did he say, Tom?”"
"3671"	"“He said--I _think_ he said he hoped I was better off where I was gone"
"3672"	"to, but if I’d been better sometimes--”"
"3673"	"“_There_, d’you hear that! It was his very words!”"
"3674"	"“And you shut him up sharp.”"
"3675"	"“I lay I did! There must ‘a’ been an angel there. There _was_ an angel"
"3676"	"there, somewheres!”"
"3677"	"“And Mrs. Harper told about Joe scaring her with a firecracker, and you"
"3678"	"told about Peter and the Pain-killer--”"
"3679"	"“Just as true as I live!”"
"3680"	"“And then there was a whole lot of talk ‘bout dragging the river for us,"
"3681"	"and ‘bout having the funeral Sunday, and then you and old Miss Harper"
"3682"	"hugged and cried, and she went.”"
"3683"	"“It happened just so! It happened just so, as sure as I’m a-sitting in"
"3684"	"these very tracks. Tom, you couldn’t told it more like if you’d ‘a’ seen"
"3685"	"it! And then what? Go on, Tom!”"
"3686"	"“Then I thought you prayed for me--and I could see you and hear every"
"3687"	"word you said. And you went to bed, and I was so sorry that I took and"
"3688"	"wrote on a piece of sycamore bark, ‘We ain’t dead--we are only off being"
"3689"	"pirates,’ and put it on the table by the candle; and then you looked"
"3690"	"so good, laying there asleep, that I thought I went and leaned over and"
"3691"	"kissed you on the lips.”"
"3692"	"“Did you, Tom, _did_ you! I just forgive you everything for that!” And"
"3693"	"she seized the boy in a crushing embrace that made him feel like the"
"3694"	"guiltiest of villains."
"3695"	"“It was very kind, even though it was only a--dream,” Sid soliloquized"
"3696"	"just audibly."
"3697"	"“Shut up, Sid! A body does just the same in a dream as he’d do if he was"
"3698"	"awake. Here’s a big Milum apple I’ve been saving for you, Tom, if you"
