"3699"	"was ever found again--now go ‘long to school. I’m thankful to the good"
"3700"	"God and Father of us all I’ve got you back, that’s long-suffering and"
"3701"	"merciful to them that believe on Him and keep His word, though goodness"
"3702"	"knows I’m unworthy of it, but if only the worthy ones got His blessings"
"3703"	"and had His hand to help them over the rough places, there’s few enough"
"3704"	"would smile here or ever enter into His rest when the long night comes."
"3705"	"Go ‘long Sid, Mary, Tom--take yourselves off--you’ve hendered me long"
"3706"	"enough.”"
"3707"	"The children left for school, and the old lady to call on Mrs. Harper"
"3708"	"and vanquish her realism with Tom’s marvellous dream. Sid had better"
"3709"	"judgment than to utter the thought that was in his mind as he left the"
"3710"	"house. It was this: “Pretty thin--as long a dream as that, without any"
"3711"	"mistakes in it!”"
"3712"	"What a hero Tom was become, now! He did not go skipping and prancing,"
"3713"	"but moved with a dignified swagger as became a pirate who felt that the"
"3714"	"public eye was on him. And indeed it was; he tried not to seem to see"
"3715"	"the looks or hear the remarks as he passed along, but they were food and"
"3716"	"drink to him. Smaller boys than himself flocked at his heels, as proud"
"3717"	"to be seen with him, and tolerated by him, as if he had been the drummer"
"3718"	"at the head of a procession or the elephant leading a menagerie into"
"3719"	"town. Boys of his own size pretended not to know he had been away at"
"3720"	"all; but they were consuming with envy, nevertheless. They would have"
"3721"	"given anything to have that swarthy sun-tanned skin of his, and his"
"3722"	"glittering notoriety; and Tom would not have parted with either for a"
"3723"	"circus."
"3724"	"At school the children made so much of him and of Joe, and delivered"
"3725"	"such eloquent admiration from their eyes, that the two heroes were"
"3726"	"not long in becoming insufferably “stuck-up.” They began to tell their"
"3727"	"adventures to hungry listeners--but they only began; it was not a"
"3728"	"thing likely to have an end, with imaginations like theirs to furnish"
"3729"	"material. And finally, when they got out their pipes and went serenely"
"3730"	"puffing around, the very summit of glory was reached."
"3731"	"Tom decided that he could be independent of Becky Thatcher now. Glory"
"3732"	"was sufficient. He would live for glory. Now that he was distinguished,"
"3733"	"maybe she would be wanting to “make up.” Well, let her--she should see"
"3734"	"that he could be as indifferent as some other people. Presently she"
"3735"	"arrived. Tom pretended not to see her. He moved away and joined a group"
"3736"	"of boys and girls and began to talk. Soon he observed that she was"
"3737"	"tripping gayly back and forth with flushed face and dancing eyes,"
"3738"	"pretending to be busy chasing schoolmates, and screaming with laughter"
"3739"	"when she made a capture; but he noticed that she always made her"
"3740"	"captures in his vicinity, and that she seemed to cast a conscious eye"
"3741"	"in his direction at such times, too. It gratified all the vicious vanity"
"3742"	"that was in him; and so, instead of winning him, it only “set him up”"
"3743"	" the more and made him the more diligent to avoid betraying that he"
"3744"	"knew she was about. Presently she gave over skylarking, and moved"
"3745"	"irresolutely about, sighing once or twice and glancing furtively and"
"3746"	"wistfully toward Tom. Then she observed that now Tom was talking more"
"3747"	"particularly to Amy Lawrence than to any one else. She felt a sharp pang"
"3748"	"and grew disturbed and uneasy at once. She tried to go away, but her"
"3749"	"feet were treacherous, and carried her to the group instead. She said to"
"3750"	"a girl almost at Tom’s elbow--with sham vivacity:"
"3751"	"“Why, Mary Austin! you bad girl, why didn’t you come to Sunday-school?”"
"3752"	"“I did come--didn’t you see me?”"
"3753"	"“Why, no! Did you? Where did you sit?”"
"3754"	"“I was in Miss Peters’ class, where I always go. I saw _you_.”"
"3755"	"“Did you? Why, it’s funny I didn’t see you. I wanted to tell you about"
"3756"	"the picnic.”"
"3757"	"“Oh, that’s jolly. Who’s going to give it?”"
"3758"	"“My ma’s going to let me have one.”"
"3759"	"“Oh, goody; I hope she’ll let _me_ come.”"
"3760"	"“Well, she will. The picnic’s for me. She’ll let anybody come that I"
"3761"	"want, and I want you.”"
"3762"	"“That’s ever so nice. When is it going to be?”"
"3763"	"“By and by. Maybe about vacation.”"
"3764"	"“Oh, won’t it be fun! You going to have all the girls and boys?”"
"3765"	"“Yes, every one that’s friends to me--or wants to be”; and she glanced"
"3766"	"ever so furtively at Tom, but he talked right along to Amy Lawrence"
"3767"	"about the terrible storm on the island, and how the lightning tore the"
"3768"	"great sycamore tree “all to flinders” while he was “standing within"
"3769"	"three feet of it.”"
"3770"	"“Oh, may I come?” said Grace Miller."
"3771"	"“Yes.”"
"3772"	"“And me?” said Sally Rogers."
"3773"	"“Yes.”"
"3774"	"“And me, too?” said Susy Harper. “And Joe?”"
"3775"	"“Yes.”"
"3776"	"And so on, with clapping of joyful hands till all the group had begged"
"3777"	"for invitations but Tom and Amy. Then Tom turned coolly away, still"
"3778"	"talking, and took Amy with him. Becky’s lips trembled and the tears"
"3779"	"came to her eyes; she hid these signs with a forced gayety and went on"
"3780"	"chattering, but the life had gone out of the picnic, now, and out of"
"3781"	"everything else; she got away as soon as she could and hid herself and"
"3782"	"had what her sex call “a good cry.” Then she sat moody, with wounded"
"3783"	"pride, till the bell rang. She roused up, now, with a vindictive cast"
"3784"	"in her eye, and gave her plaited tails a shake and said she knew what"
"3785"	"_she’d_ do."
"3786"	"At recess Tom continued his flirtation with Amy with jubilant"
"3787"	"self-satisfaction. And he kept drifting about to find Becky and lacerate"
"3788"	"her with the performance. At last he spied her, but there was a sudden"
"3789"	"falling of his mercury. She was sitting cosily on a little bench behind"
"3790"	"the schoolhouse looking at a picture-book with Alfred Temple--and so"
"3791"	"absorbed were they, and their heads so close together over the book,"
"3792"	"that they did not seem to be conscious of anything in the world besides."
"3793"	"Jealousy ran red-hot through Tom’s veins. He began to hate himself for"
"3794"	"throwing away the chance Becky had offered for a reconciliation. He"
"3795"	"called himself a fool, and all the hard names he could think of. He"
"3796"	"wanted to cry with vexation. Amy chatted happily along, as they walked,"
"3797"	"for her heart was singing, but Tom’s tongue had lost its function. He"
"3798"	"did not hear what Amy was saying, and whenever she paused expectantly"
"3799"	"he could only stammer an awkward assent, which was as often misplaced"
"3800"	"as otherwise. He kept drifting to the rear of the schoolhouse, again and"
"3801"	"again, to sear his eyeballs with the hateful spectacle there. He could"
"3802"	"not help it. And it maddened him to see, as he thought he saw, that"
"3803"	"Becky Thatcher never once suspected that he was even in the land of the"
"3804"	"living. But she did see, nevertheless; and she knew she was winning her"
"3805"	"fight, too, and was glad to see him suffer as she had suffered."
"3806"	"Amy’s happy prattle became intolerable. Tom hinted at things he had"
"3807"	"to attend to; things that must be done; and time was fleeting. But in"
"3808"	"vain--the girl chirped on. Tom thought, “Oh, hang her, ain’t I ever going"
"3809"	"to get rid of her?” At last he must be attending to those things--and she"
"3810"	"said artlessly that she would be “around” when school let out. And he"
"3811"	"hastened away, hating her for it."
"3812"	"“Any other boy!” Tom thought, grating his teeth. “Any boy in the whole"
"3813"	"town but that Saint Louis smarty that thinks he dresses so fine and is"
"3814"	"aristocracy! Oh, all right, I licked you the first day you ever saw this"
"3815"	"town, mister, and I’ll lick you again! You just wait till I catch you"
"3816"	"out! I’ll just take and--”"
"3817"	"And he went through the motions of thrashing an imaginary boy--pummelling"
"3818"	"the air, and kicking and gouging. “Oh, you do, do you? You holler"
"3819"	"‘nough, do you? Now, then, let that learn you!” And so the imaginary"
"3820"	"flogging was finished to his satisfaction."
"3821"	"Tom fled home at noon. His conscience could not endure any more of Amy’s"
"3822"	"grateful happiness, and his jealousy could bear no more of the other"
"3823"	"distress. Becky resumed her picture inspections with Alfred, but as the"
"3824"	"minutes dragged along and no Tom came to suffer, her triumph began to"
"3825"	"cloud and she lost interest; gravity and absentmindedness followed,"
"3826"	"and then melancholy; two or three times she pricked up her ear at"
"3827"	"a footstep, but it was a false hope; no Tom came. At last she grew"
"3828"	"entirely miserable and wished she hadn’t carried it so far. When"
"3829"	"poor Alfred, seeing that he was losing her, he did not know how, kept"
"3830"	"exclaiming: “Oh, here’s a jolly one! look at this!” she lost patience at"
"3831"	"last, and said, “Oh, don’t bother me! I don’t care for them!” and burst"
"3832"	"into tears, and got up and walked away."
"3833"	"Alfred dropped alongside and was going to try to comfort her, but she"
"3834"	"said:"
"3835"	"“Go away and leave me alone, can’t you! I hate you!”"
"3836"	"So the boy halted, wondering what he could have done--for she had said"
"3837"	"she would look at pictures all through the nooning--and she walked on,"
"3838"	"crying. Then Alfred went musing into the deserted schoolhouse. He was"
"3839"	"humiliated and angry. He easily guessed his way to the truth--the girl"
"3840"	"had simply made a convenience of him to vent her spite upon Tom Sawyer."
"3841"	"He was far from hating Tom the less when this thought occurred to him."
"3842"	"He wished there was some way to get that boy into trouble without much"
"3843"	"risk to himself. Tom’s spelling-book fell under his eye. Here was his"
"3844"	"opportunity. He gratefully opened to the lesson for the afternoon and"
"3845"	"poured ink upon the page."
"3846"	"Becky, glancing in at a window behind him at the moment, saw the act,"
"3847"	"and moved on, without discovering herself. She started homeward, now,"
"3848"	"intending to find Tom and tell him; Tom would be thankful and their"
"3849"	"troubles would be healed. Before she was half way home, however, she"
"3850"	"had changed her mind. The thought of Tom’s treatment of her when she was"
"3851"	"talking about her picnic came scorching back and filled her with shame."
"3852"	"She resolved to let him get whipped on the damaged spelling-book’s"
"3853"	"account, and to hate him forever, into the bargain."
"3854"	"CHAPTER XIX"
"3855"	"TOM arrived at home in a dreary mood, and the first thing his aunt said"
"3856"	"to him showed him that he had brought his sorrows to an unpromising"
"3857"	"market:"
"3858"	"“Tom, I’ve a notion to skin you alive!”"
"3859"	"“Auntie, what have I done?”"
"3860"	"“Well, you’ve done enough. Here I go over to Sereny Harper, like an old"
"3861"	"softy, expecting I’m going to make her believe all that rubbage about"
"3862"	"that dream, when lo and behold you she’d found out from Joe that you was"
"3863"	"over here and heard all the talk we had that night. Tom, I don’t know"
"3864"	"what is to become of a boy that will act like that. It makes me feel so"
"3865"	"bad to think you could let me go to Sereny Harper and make such a fool"
"3866"	"of myself and never say a word.”"
"3867"	"This was a new aspect of the thing. His smartness of the morning had"
"3868"	"seemed to Tom a good joke before, and very ingenious. It merely looked"
"3869"	"mean and shabby now. He hung his head and could not think of anything to"
"3870"	"say for a moment. Then he said:"
"3871"	"“Auntie, I wish I hadn’t done it--but I didn’t think.”"
"3872"	"“Oh, child, you never think. You never think of anything but your"
"3873"	"own selfishness. You could think to come all the way over here from"
"3874"	"Jackson’s Island in the night to laugh at our troubles, and you could"
"3875"	"think to fool me with a lie about a dream; but you couldn’t ever think"
"3876"	"to pity us and save us from sorrow.”"
"3877"	"“Auntie, I know now it was mean, but I didn’t mean to be mean. I didn’t,"
"3878"	"honest. And besides, I didn’t come over here to laugh at you that"
"3879"	"night.”"
"3880"	"“What did you come for, then?”"
"3881"	"“It was to tell you not to be uneasy about us, because we hadn’t got"
"3882"	"drownded.”"
"3883"	"“Tom, Tom, I would be the thankfullest soul in this world if I could"
"3884"	"believe you ever had as good a thought as that, but you know you never"
"3885"	"did--and I know it, Tom.”"
"3886"	"“Indeed and ‘deed I did, auntie--I wish I may never stir if I didn’t.”"
"3887"	"“Oh, Tom, don’t lie--don’t do it. It only makes things a hundred times"
"3888"	"worse.”"
"3889"	"“It ain’t a lie, auntie; it’s the truth. I wanted to keep you from"
"3890"	"grieving--that was all that made me come.”"
"3891"	"“I’d give the whole world to believe that--it would cover up a power"
"3892"	"of sins, Tom. I’d ‘most be glad you’d run off and acted so bad. But it"
"3893"	"ain’t reasonable; because, why didn’t you tell me, child?”"
"3894"	"“Why, you see, when you got to talking about the funeral, I just got all"
"3895"	"full of the idea of our coming and hiding in the church, and I couldn’t"
"3896"	"somehow bear to spoil it. So I just put the bark back in my pocket and"
"3897"	"kept mum.”"
"3898"	"“What bark?”"
"3899"	"“The bark I had wrote on to tell you we’d gone pirating. I wish, now,"
"3900"	"you’d waked up when I kissed you--I do, honest.”"
"3901"	"The hard lines in his aunt’s face relaxed and a sudden tenderness dawned"
"3902"	"in her eyes."
"3903"	"“_Did_ you kiss me, Tom?”"
"3904"	"“Why, yes, I did.”"
"3905"	"“Are you sure you did, Tom?”"
"3906"	"“Why, yes, I did, auntie--certain sure.”"
"3907"	"“What did you kiss me for, Tom?”"
"3908"	"“Because I loved you so, and you laid there moaning and I was so sorry.”"
"3909"	"The words sounded like truth. The old lady could not hide a tremor in"
"3910"	"her voice when she said:"
"3911"	"“Kiss me again, Tom!--and be off with you to school, now, and don’t"
"3912"	"bother me any more.”"
"3913"	"The moment he was gone, she ran to a closet and got out the ruin of a"
"3914"	"jacket which Tom had gone pirating in. Then she stopped, with it in her"
"3915"	"hand, and said to herself:"
"3916"	"“No, I don’t dare. Poor boy, I reckon he’s lied about it--but it’s a"
"3917"	"blessed, blessed lie, there’s such a comfort come from it. I hope"
"3918"	"the Lord--I _know_ the Lord will forgive him, because it was such"
"3919"	"good-heartedness in him to tell it. But I don’t want to find out it’s a"
"3920"	"lie. I won’t look.”"
"3921"	"She put the jacket away, and stood by musing a minute. Twice she put out"
"3922"	"her hand to take the garment again, and twice she refrained. Once more"
"3923"	"she ventured, and this time she fortified herself with the thought:"
"3924"	"“It’s a good lie--it’s a good lie--I won’t let it grieve me.” So she"
"3925"	"sought the jacket pocket. A moment later she was reading Tom’s piece of"
"3926"	"bark through flowing tears and saying: “I could forgive the boy, now, if"
"3927"	"he’d committed a million sins!”"
"3928"	"CHAPTER XX"
"3929"	"THERE was something about Aunt Polly’s manner, when she kissed Tom, that"
"3930"	"swept away his low spirits and made him lighthearted and happy again. He"
"3931"	"started to school and had the luck of coming upon Becky Thatcher at the"
"3932"	"head of Meadow Lane. His mood always determined his manner. Without a"
"3933"	"moment’s hesitation he ran to her and said:"
"3934"	"“I acted mighty mean today, Becky, and I’m so sorry. I won’t ever, ever"
"3935"	"do that way again, as long as ever I live--please make up, won’t you?”"
"3936"	"The girl stopped and looked him scornfully in the face:"
"3937"	"“I’ll thank you to keep yourself _to_ yourself, Mr. Thomas Sawyer. I’ll"
"3938"	"never speak to you again.”"
"3939"	"She tossed her head and passed on. Tom was so stunned that he had not"
"3940"	"even presence of mind enough to say “Who cares, Miss Smarty?” until the"
"3941"	"right time to say it had gone by. So he said nothing. But he was in a"
"3942"	"fine rage, nevertheless. He moped into the schoolyard wishing she were"
"3943"	"a boy, and imagining how he would trounce her if she were. He presently"
"3944"	"encountered her and delivered a stinging remark as he passed. She hurled"
"3945"	"one in return, and the angry breach was complete. It seemed to Becky, in"
"3946"	"her hot resentment, that she could hardly wait for school to “take in,”"
"3947"	" she was so impatient to see Tom flogged for the injured spelling-book."
"3948"	"If she had had any lingering notion of exposing Alfred Temple, Tom’s"
"3949"	"offensive fling had driven it entirely away."
"3950"	"Poor girl, she did not know how fast she was nearing trouble herself."
"3951"	"The master, Mr. Dobbins, had reached middle age with an unsatisfied"
"3952"	"ambition. The darling of his desires was, to be a doctor, but"
"3953"	"poverty had decreed that he should be nothing higher than a village"
"3954"	"schoolmaster. Every day he took a mysterious book out of his desk and"
"3955"	"absorbed himself in it at times when no classes were reciting. He kept"
"3956"	"that book under lock and key. There was not an urchin in school but was"
"3957"	"perishing to have a glimpse of it, but the chance never came. Every boy"
"3958"	"and girl had a theory about the nature of that book; but no two theories"
"3959"	"were alike, and there was no way of getting at the facts in the case."
"3960"	"Now, as Becky was passing by the desk, which stood near the door, she"
"3961"	"noticed that the key was in the lock! It was a precious moment. She"
"3962"	"glanced around; found herself alone, and the next instant she had the"
"3963"	"book in her hands. The titlepage--Professor Somebody’s _Anatomy_--carried"
"3964"	"no information to her mind; so she began to turn the leaves. She came at"
"3965"	"once upon a handsomely engraved and colored frontispiece--a human figure,"
"3966"	"stark naked. At that moment a shadow fell on the page and Tom Sawyer"
"3967"	"stepped in at the door and caught a glimpse of the picture. Becky"
"3968"	"snatched at the book to close it, and had the hard luck to tear the"
"3969"	"pictured page half down the middle. She thrust the volume into the desk,"
"3970"	"turned the key, and burst out crying with shame and vexation."
"3971"	"“Tom Sawyer, you are just as mean as you can be, to sneak up on a person"
"3972"	"and look at what they’re looking at.”"
"3973"	"“How could I know you was looking at anything?”"
"3974"	"“You ought to be ashamed of yourself, Tom Sawyer; you know you’re"
"3975"	"going to tell on me, and oh, what shall I do, what shall I do! I’ll be"
"3976"	"whipped, and I never was whipped in school.”"
"3977"	"Then she stamped her little foot and said:"
"3978"	"“_Be_ so mean if you want to! I know something that’s going to happen."
"3979"	"You just wait and you’ll see! Hateful, hateful, hateful!”--and she flung"
"3980"	"out of the house with a new explosion of crying."
"3981"	"Tom stood still, rather flustered by this onslaught. Presently he said"
"3982"	"to himself:"
"3983"	"“What a curious kind of a fool a girl is! Never been licked in"
"3984"	"school! Shucks! What’s a licking! That’s just like a girl--they’re so"
"3985"	"thin-skinned and chicken-hearted. Well, of course I ain’t going to tell"
"3986"	"old Dobbins on this little fool, because there’s other ways of getting"
"3987"	"even on her, that ain’t so mean; but what of it? Old Dobbins will ask"
"3988"	"who it was tore his book. Nobody’ll answer. Then he’ll do just the way"
"3989"	"he always does--ask first one and then t’other, and when he comes to the"
"3990"	"right girl he’ll know it, without any telling. Girls’ faces always tell"
"3991"	"on them. They ain’t got any backbone. She’ll get licked. Well, it’s a"
"3992"	"kind of a tight place for Becky Thatcher, because there ain’t any way"
"3993"	"out of it.” Tom conned the thing a moment longer, and then added: “All"
"3994"	"right, though; she’d like to see me in just such a fix--let her sweat it"
"3995"	"out!”"
"3996"	"Tom joined the mob of skylarking scholars outside. In a few moments the"
"3997"	"master arrived and school “took in.” Tom did not feel a strong interest"
"3998"	"in his studies. Every time he stole a glance at the girls’ side of the"
"3999"	"room Becky’s face troubled him. Considering all things, he did not want"
"4000"	"to pity her, and yet it was all he could do to help it. He could get"
"4001"	"up no exultation that was really worthy the name. Presently the"
"4002"	"spelling-book discovery was made, and Tom’s mind was entirely full"
"4003"	"of his own matters for a while after that. Becky roused up from her"
"4004"	"lethargy of distress and showed good interest in the proceedings. She"
"4005"	"did not expect that Tom could get out of his trouble by denying that he"
"4006"	"spilt the ink on the book himself; and she was right. The denial only"
"4007"	"seemed to make the thing worse for Tom. Becky supposed she would be glad"
"4008"	"of that, and she tried to believe she was glad of it, but she found she"
"4009"	"was not certain. When the worst came to the worst, she had an impulse"
"4010"	"to get up and tell on Alfred Temple, but she made an effort and forced"
"4011"	"herself to keep still--because, said she to herself, “he’ll tell about me"
"4012"	"tearing the picture sure. I wouldn’t say a word, not to save his life!”"
"4013"	"Tom took his whipping and went back to his seat not at all"
"4014"	"broken-hearted, for he thought it was possible that he had unknowingly"
"4015"	"upset the ink on the spelling-book himself, in some skylarking bout--he"
"4016"	"had denied it for form’s sake and because it was custom, and had stuck"
"4017"	"to the denial from principle."
"4018"	"A whole hour drifted by, the master sat nodding in his throne, the air"
"4019"	"was drowsy with the hum of study. By and by, Mr. Dobbins straightened"
"4020"	"himself up, yawned, then unlocked his desk, and reached for his book,"
"4021"	"but seemed undecided whether to take it out or leave it. Most of the"
"4022"	"pupils glanced up languidly, but there were two among them that watched"
"4023"	"his movements with intent eyes. Mr. Dobbins fingered his book absently"
"4024"	"for a while, then took it out and settled himself in his chair to read!"
"4025"	"Tom shot a glance at Becky. He had seen a hunted and helpless rabbit"
"4026"	"look as she did, with a gun levelled at its head. Instantly he forgot"
"4027"	"his quarrel with her. Quick--something must be done! done in a flash,"
"4028"	"too! But the very imminence of the emergency paralyzed his invention."
"4029"	"Good!--he had an inspiration! He would run and snatch the book, spring"
"4030"	"through the door and fly. But his resolution shook for one little"
"4031"	"instant, and the chance was lost--the master opened the volume. If Tom"
"4032"	"only had the wasted opportunity back again! Too late. There was no help"
"4033"	"for Becky now, he said. The next moment the master faced the school."
"4034"	"Every eye sank under his gaze. There was that in it which smote even"
"4035"	"the innocent with fear. There was silence while one might count ten--the"
"4036"	"master was gathering his wrath. Then he spoke: “Who tore this book?”"
"4037"	"There was not a sound. One could have heard a pin drop. The stillness"
"4038"	"continued; the master searched face after face for signs of guilt."
"4039"	"“Benjamin Rogers, did you tear this book?”"
"4040"	"A denial. Another pause."
"4041"	"“Joseph Harper, did you?”"
"4042"	"Another denial. Tom’s uneasiness grew more and more intense under the"
"4043"	"slow torture of these proceedings. The master scanned the ranks of"
"4044"	"boys--considered a while, then turned to the girls:"
"4045"	"“Amy Lawrence?”"
"4046"	"A shake of the head."
"4047"	"“Gracie Miller?”"
"4048"	"The same sign."
"4049"	"“Susan Harper, did you do this?”"
"4050"	"Another negative. The next girl was Becky Thatcher. Tom was trembling"
"4051"	"from head to foot with excitement and a sense of the hopelessness of the"
"4052"	"situation."
"4053"	"“Rebecca Thatcher” [Tom glanced at her face--it was white with"
"4054"	"terror]--“did you tear--no, look me in the face” [her hands rose in"
"4055"	"appeal]--“did you tear this book?”"
"4056"	"A thought shot like lightning through Tom’s brain. He sprang to his feet"
"4057"	"and shouted--“I done it!”"
"4058"	"The school stared in perplexity at this incredible folly. Tom stood a"
"4059"	"moment, to gather his dismembered faculties; and when he stepped forward"
"4060"	"to go to his punishment the surprise, the gratitude, the adoration that"
"4061"	"shone upon him out of poor Becky’s eyes seemed pay enough for a hundred"
"4062"	"floggings. Inspired by the splendor of his own act, he took without"
"4063"	"an outcry the most merciless flaying that even Mr. Dobbins had ever"
"4064"	"administered; and also received with indifference the added cruelty of a"
"4065"	"command to remain two hours after school should be dismissed--for he"
"4066"	"knew who would wait for him outside till his captivity was done, and not"
"4067"	"count the tedious time as loss, either."
"4068"	"Tom went to bed that night planning vengeance against Alfred Temple; for"
"4069"	"with shame and repentance Becky had told him all, not forgetting her own"
"4070"	"treachery; but even the longing for vengeance had to give way, soon, to"
"4071"	"pleasanter musings, and he fell asleep at last with Becky’s latest words"
"4072"	"lingering dreamily in his ear--"
"4073"	"“Tom, how _could_ you be so noble!”"
"4074"	"CHAPTER XXI"
"4075"	"VACATION was approaching. The schoolmaster, always severe, grew severer"
"4076"	"and more exacting than ever, for he wanted the school to make a good"
"4077"	"showing on “Examination” day. His rod and his ferule were seldom idle"
"4078"	"now--at least among the smaller pupils. Only the biggest boys, and young"
"4079"	"ladies of eighteen and twenty, escaped lashing. Mr. Dobbins’ lashings"
"4080"	"were very vigorous ones, too; for although he carried, under his wig, a"
"4081"	"perfectly bald and shiny head, he had only reached middle age, and there"
"4082"	"was no sign of feebleness in his muscle. As the great day approached,"
"4083"	"all the tyranny that was in him came to the surface; he seemed to take a"
"4084"	"vindictive pleasure in punishing the least shortcomings. The consequence"
"4085"	"was, that the smaller boys spent their days in terror and suffering and"
"4086"	"their nights in plotting revenge. They threw away no opportunity to do"
"4087"	"the master a mischief. But he kept ahead all the time. The retribution"
"4088"	"that followed every vengeful success was so sweeping and majestic that"
"4089"	"the boys always retired from the field badly worsted. At last they"
"4090"	"conspired together and hit upon a plan that promised a dazzling victory."
"4091"	"They swore in the signpainter’s boy, told him the scheme, and asked his"
"4092"	"help. He had his own reasons for being delighted, for the master boarded"
"4093"	"in his father’s family and had given the boy ample cause to hate him."
"4094"	"The master’s wife would go on a visit to the country in a few days, and"
"4095"	"there would be nothing to interfere with the plan; the master always"
"4096"	"prepared himself for great occasions by getting pretty well fuddled, and"
"4097"	"the signpainter’s boy said that when the dominie had reached the proper"
"4098"	"condition on Examination Evening he would “manage the thing” while he"
"4099"	"napped in his chair; then he would have him awakened at the right time"
"4100"	"and hurried away to school."
"4101"	"In the fulness of time the interesting occasion arrived. At eight in"
"4102"	"the evening the schoolhouse was brilliantly lighted, and adorned with"
"4103"	"wreaths and festoons of foliage and flowers. The master sat throned in"
"4104"	"his great chair upon a raised platform, with his blackboard behind him."
"4105"	"He was looking tolerably mellow. Three rows of benches on each side and"
"4106"	"six rows in front of him were occupied by the dignitaries of the town"
"4107"	"and by the parents of the pupils. To his left, back of the rows of"
"4108"	"citizens, was a spacious temporary platform upon which were seated the"
"4109"	"scholars who were to take part in the exercises of the evening; rows of"
"4110"	"small boys, washed and dressed to an intolerable state of discomfort;"
"4111"	"rows of gawky big boys; snowbanks of girls and young ladies clad in"
"4112"	"lawn and muslin and conspicuously conscious of their bare arms, their"
"4113"	"grandmothers’ ancient trinkets, their bits of pink and blue ribbon and"
"4114"	"the flowers in their hair. All the rest of the house was filled with"
"4115"	"non-participating scholars."
"4116"	"The exercises began. A very little boy stood up and sheepishly recited,"
"4117"	"“You’d scarce expect one of my age to speak in public on the stage,”"
"4118"	" etc.--accompanying himself with the painfully exact and spasmodic"
"4119"	"gestures which a machine might have used--supposing the machine to be a"
"4120"	"trifle out of order. But he got through safely, though cruelly scared,"
"4121"	"and got a fine round of applause when he made his manufactured bow and"
"4122"	"retired."
"4123"	"A little shamefaced girl lisped, “Mary had a little lamb,” etc.,"
"4124"	"performed a compassion-inspiring curtsy, got her meed of applause, and"
"4125"	"sat down flushed and happy."
"4126"	"Tom Sawyer stepped forward with conceited confidence and soared into"
"4127"	"the unquenchable and indestructible “Give me liberty or give me death”"
"4128"	" speech, with fine fury and frantic gesticulation, and broke down in the"
"4129"	"middle of it. A ghastly stage-fright seized him, his legs quaked under"
"4130"	"him and he was like to choke. True, he had the manifest sympathy of the"
"4131"	"house but he had the house’s silence, too, which was even worse than"
"4132"	"its sympathy. The master frowned, and this completed the disaster. Tom"
"4133"	"struggled awhile and then retired, utterly defeated. There was a weak"
"4134"	"attempt at applause, but it died early."
"4135"	"“The Boy Stood on the Burning Deck” followed; also “The Assyrian Came"
"4136"	"Down,” and other declamatory gems. Then there were reading exercises,"
"4137"	"and a spelling fight. The meagre Latin class recited with honor. The"
"4138"	"prime feature of the evening was in order, now--original “compositions”"
"4139"	" by the young ladies. Each in her turn stepped forward to the edge of the"
"4140"	"platform, cleared her throat, held up her manuscript (tied with dainty"
"4141"	"ribbon), and proceeded to read, with labored attention to “expression”"
"4142"	" and punctuation. The themes were the same that had been illuminated upon"
"4143"	"similar occasions by their mothers before them, their grandmothers,"
"4144"	"and doubtless all their ancestors in the female line clear back to the"
"4145"	"Crusades. “Friendship” was one; “Memories of Other Days”; “Religion in"
"4146"	"History”; “Dream Land”; “The Advantages of Culture”; “Forms of Political"
"4147"	"Government Compared and Contrasted”; “Melancholy”; “Filial Love”; “Heart"
"4148"	"Longings,” etc., etc."
"4149"	"A prevalent feature in these compositions was a nursed and petted"
"4150"	"melancholy; another was a wasteful and opulent gush of “fine language”;"
"4151"	"another was a tendency to lug in by the ears particularly prized words"
"4152"	"and phrases until they were worn entirely out; and a peculiarity that"
"4153"	"conspicuously marked and marred them was the inveterate and intolerable"
"4154"	"sermon that wagged its crippled tail at the end of each and every one"
"4155"	"of them. No matter what the subject might be, a brainracking effort was"
"4156"	"made to squirm it into some aspect or other that the moral and religious"
"4157"	"mind could contemplate with edification. The glaring insincerity of"
"4158"	"these sermons was not sufficient to compass the banishment of the"
"4159"	"fashion from the schools, and it is not sufficient today; it never will"
"4160"	"be sufficient while the world stands, perhaps. There is no school in"
"4161"	"all our land where the young ladies do not feel obliged to close their"
"4162"	"compositions with a sermon; and you will find that the sermon of the"
"4163"	"most frivolous and the least religious girl in the school is always"
"4164"	"the longest and the most relentlessly pious. But enough of this. Homely"
"4165"	"truth is unpalatable."
"4166"	"Let us return to the “Examination.” The first composition that was read"
"4167"	"was one entitled “Is this, then, Life?” Perhaps the reader can endure an"
"4168"	"extract from it:"
"4169"	"“In the common walks of life, with what delightful emotions does the"
"4170"	"youthful mind look forward to some anticipated scene of festivity!"
"4171"	"Imagination is busy sketching rose-tinted pictures of joy. In fancy, the"
"4172"	"voluptuous votary of fashion sees herself amid the festive throng, ‘the"
"4173"	"observed of all observers.’ Her graceful form, arrayed in snowy robes,"
"4174"	"is whirling through the mazes of the joyous dance; her eye is brightest,"
"4175"	"her step is lightest in the gay assembly."
"4176"	"“In such delicious fancies time quickly glides by, and the welcome hour"
"4177"	"arrives for her entrance into the Elysian world, of which she has"
"4178"	"had such bright dreams. How fairy-like does everything appear to her"
"4179"	"enchanted vision! Each new scene is more charming than the last. But"
"4180"	"after a while she finds that beneath this goodly exterior, all is"
"4181"	"vanity, the flattery which once charmed her soul, now grates harshly"
"4182"	"upon her ear; the ballroom has lost its charms; and with wasted health"
"4183"	"and imbittered heart, she turns away with the conviction that earthly"
"4184"	"pleasures cannot satisfy the longings of the soul!”"
"4185"	"And so forth and so on. There was a buzz of gratification from time to"
"4186"	"time during the reading, accompanied by whispered ejaculations of “How"
"4187"	"sweet!” “How eloquent!” “So true!” etc., and after the thing had closed"
"4188"	"with a peculiarly afflicting sermon the applause was enthusiastic."
"4189"	"Then arose a slim, melancholy girl, whose face had the “interesting”"
"4190"	" paleness that comes of pills and indigestion, and read a “poem.” Two"
"4191"	"stanzas of it will do:"
"4192"	"“A MISSOURI MAIDEN’S FAREWELL TO ALABAMA"
"4193"	"“Alabama, goodbye! I love thee well! But yet for a while do I leave thee"
"4194"	"now! Sad, yes, sad thoughts of thee my heart doth swell, And burning"
"4195"	"recollections throng my brow! For I have wandered through thy flowery"
"4196"	"woods; Have roamed and read near Tallapoosa’s stream; Have listened to"
"4197"	"Tallassee’s warring floods, And wooed on Coosa’s side Aurora’s beam."
"4198"	"“Yet shame I not to bear an o’erfull heart, Nor blush to turn behind"
"4199"	"my tearful eyes; ‘Tis from no stranger land I now must part, ‘Tis to no"
"4200"	"strangers left I yield these sighs. Welcome and home were mine within"
"4201"	"this State, Whose vales I leave--whose spires fade fast from me And cold"
"4202"	"must be mine eyes, and heart, and tete, When, dear Alabama! they turn"
"4203"	"cold on thee!” There were very few there who knew what “tete” meant, but"
"4204"	"the poem was very satisfactory, nevertheless."
"4205"	"Next appeared a dark-complexioned, black-eyed, black-haired young lady,"
"4206"	"who paused an impressive moment, assumed a tragic expression, and began"
"4207"	"to read in a measured, solemn tone:"
"4208"	"“A VISION"
"4209"	"“Dark and tempestuous was night. Around the throne on high not a single"
"4210"	"star quivered; but the deep intonations of the heavy thunder constantly"
"4211"	"vibrated upon the ear; whilst the terrific lightning revelled in angry"
"4212"	"mood through the cloudy chambers of heaven, seeming to scorn the power"
"4213"	"exerted over its terror by the illustrious Franklin! Even the boisterous"
"4214"	"winds unanimously came forth from their mystic homes, and blustered"
"4215"	"about as if to enhance by their aid the wildness of the scene."
"4216"	"“At such a time, so dark, so dreary, for human sympathy my very spirit"
"4217"	"sighed; but instead thereof,"
"4218"	"“‘My dearest friend, my counsellor, my comforter and guide--My joy in"
"4219"	"grief, my second bliss in joy,’ came to my side. She moved like one of"
"4220"	"those bright beings pictured in the sunny walks of fancy’s Eden by"
"4221"	"the romantic and young, a queen of beauty unadorned save by her own"
"4222"	"transcendent loveliness. So soft was her step, it failed to make even a"
"4223"	"sound, and but for the magical thrill imparted by her genial touch,"
"4224"	"as other unobtrusive beauties, she would have glided away"
"4225"	"unperceived--unsought. A strange sadness rested upon her features, like"
"4226"	"icy tears upon the robe of December, as she pointed to the contending"
"4227"	"elements without, and bade me contemplate the two beings presented.”"
"4228"	"This nightmare occupied some ten pages of manuscript and wound up with a"
"4229"	"sermon so destructive of all hope to non-Presbyterians that it took"
"4230"	"the first prize. This composition was considered to be the very finest"
"4231"	"effort of the evening. The mayor of the village, in delivering the prize"
"4232"	"to the author of it, made a warm speech in which he said that it was by"
"4233"	"far the most “eloquent” thing he had ever listened to, and that Daniel"
"4234"	"Webster himself might well be proud of it."
"4235"	"It may be remarked, in passing, that the number of compositions in which"
"4236"	"the word “beauteous” was over-fondled, and human experience referred to"
"4237"	"as “life’s page,” was up to the usual average."
"4238"	"Now the master, mellow almost to the verge of geniality, put his chair"
"4239"	"aside, turned his back to the audience, and began to draw a map of"
"4240"	"America on the blackboard, to exercise the geography class upon. But he"
"4241"	"made a sad business of it with his unsteady hand, and a smothered titter"
"4242"	"rippled over the house. He knew what the matter was, and set himself to"
"4243"	"right it. He sponged out lines and remade them; but he only distorted"
"4244"	"them more than ever, and the tittering was more pronounced. He threw his"
"4245"	"entire attention upon his work, now, as if determined not to be put down"
"4246"	"by the mirth. He felt that all eyes were fastened upon him; he imagined"
"4247"	"he was succeeding, and yet the tittering continued; it even manifestly"
"4248"	"increased. And well it might. There was a garret above, pierced with"
"4249"	"a scuttle over his head; and down through this scuttle came a cat,"
"4250"	"suspended around the haunches by a string; she had a rag tied about"
"4251"	"her head and jaws to keep her from mewing; as she slowly descended she"
"4252"	"curved upward and clawed at the string, she swung downward and clawed"
"4253"	"at the intangible air. The tittering rose higher and higher--the cat was"
"4254"	"within six inches of the absorbed teacher’s head--down, down, a little"
"4255"	"lower, and she grabbed his wig with her desperate claws, clung to it,"
"4256"	"and was snatched up into the garret in an instant with her trophy still"
"4257"	"in her possession! And how the light did blaze abroad from the master’s"
"4258"	"bald pate--for the signpainter’s boy had _gilded_ it!"
"4259"	"That broke up the meeting. The boys were avenged. Vacation had come."
"4260"	"NOTE:--The pretended “compositions” quoted in this chapter are taken"
"4261"	"without alteration from a volume entitled “Prose and Poetry, by a"
"4262"	"Western Lady”--but they are exactly and precisely after the schoolgirl"
"4263"	"pattern, and hence are much happier than any mere imitations could be."
"4264"	"CHAPTER XXII"
"4265"	"TOM joined the new order of Cadets of Temperance, being attracted by the"
"4266"	"showy character of their “regalia.” He promised to abstain from smoking,"
"4267"	"chewing, and profanity as long as he remained a member. Now he found out"
"4268"	"a new thing--namely, that to promise not to do a thing is the surest way"
"4269"	"in the world to make a body want to go and do that very thing. Tom soon"
"4270"	"found himself tormented with a desire to drink and swear; the desire"
"4271"	"grew to be so intense that nothing but the hope of a chance to display"
"4272"	"himself in his red sash kept him from withdrawing from the order. Fourth"
"4273"	"of July was coming; but he soon gave that up--gave it up before he had"
"4274"	"worn his shackles over forty-eight hours--and fixed his hopes upon old"
"4275"	"Judge Frazer, justice of the peace, who was apparently on his deathbed"
"4276"	"and would have a big public funeral, since he was so high an official."
"4277"	"During three days Tom was deeply concerned about the Judge’s condition"
"4278"	"and hungry for news of it. Sometimes his hopes ran high--so high that"
"4279"	"he would venture to get out his regalia and practise before the"
"4280"	"looking-glass. But the Judge had a most discouraging way of fluctuating."
"4281"	"At last he was pronounced upon the mend--and then convalescent. Tom was"
"4282"	"disgusted; and felt a sense of injury, too. He handed in his resignation"
"4283"	"at once--and that night the Judge suffered a relapse and died. Tom"
"4284"	"resolved that he would never trust a man like that again."
"4285"	"The funeral was a fine thing. The Cadets paraded in a style calculated"
"4286"	"to kill the late member with envy. Tom was a free boy again,"
"4287"	"however--there was something in that. He could drink and swear, now--but"
"4288"	"found to his surprise that he did not want to. The simple fact that he"
"4289"	"could, took the desire away, and the charm of it."
"4290"	"Tom presently wondered to find that his coveted vacation was beginning"
"4291"	"to hang a little heavily on his hands."
"4292"	"He attempted a diary--but nothing happened during three days, and so he"
"4293"	"abandoned it."
"4294"	"The first of all the negro minstrel shows came to town, and made a"
"4295"	"sensation. Tom and Joe Harper got up a band of performers and were happy"
"4296"	"for two days."
"4297"	"Even the Glorious Fourth was in some sense a failure, for it rained"
"4298"	"hard, there was no procession in consequence, and the greatest man"
"4299"	"in the world (as Tom supposed), Mr. Benton, an actual United States"
"4300"	"Senator, proved an overwhelming disappointment--for he was not"
"4301"	"twenty-five feet high, nor even anywhere in the neighborhood of it."
"4302"	"A circus came. The boys played circus for three days afterward in tents"
"4303"	"made of rag carpeting--admission, three pins for boys, two for girls--and"
"4304"	"then circusing was abandoned."
"4305"	"A phrenologist and a mesmerizer came--and went again and left the village"
"4306"	"duller and drearier than ever."
"4307"	"There were some boys-and-girls’ parties, but they were so few and so"
"4308"	"delightful that they only made the aching voids between ache the harder."
"4309"	"Becky Thatcher was gone to her Constantinople home to stay with her"
"4310"	"parents during vacation--so there was no bright side to life anywhere."
"4311"	"The dreadful secret of the murder was a chronic misery. It was a very"
"4312"	"cancer for permanency and pain."
"4313"	"Then came the measles."
"4314"	"During two long weeks Tom lay a prisoner, dead to the world and its"
"4315"	"happenings. He was very ill, he was interested in nothing. When he got"
"4316"	"upon his feet at last and moved feebly downtown, a melancholy change had"
"4317"	"come over everything and every creature. There had been a “revival,” and"
"4318"	"everybody had “got religion,” not only the adults, but even the boys and"
"4319"	"girls. Tom went about, hoping against hope for the sight of one blessed"
"4320"	"sinful face, but disappointment crossed him everywhere. He found Joe"
"4321"	"Harper studying a Testament, and turned sadly away from the depressing"
"4322"	"spectacle. He sought Ben Rogers, and found him visiting the poor with a"
"4323"	"basket of tracts. He hunted up Jim Hollis, who called his attention to"
"4324"	"the precious blessing of his late measles as a warning. Every boy"
"4325"	"he encountered added another ton to his depression; and when, in"
"4326"	"desperation, he flew for refuge at last to the bosom of Huckleberry Finn"
"4327"	"and was received with a Scriptural quotation, his heart broke and he"
"4328"	"crept home and to bed realizing that he alone of all the town was lost,"
"4329"	"forever and forever."
"4330"	"And that night there came on a terrific storm, with driving rain, awful"
"4331"	"claps of thunder and blinding sheets of lightning. He covered his head"
"4332"	"with the bedclothes and waited in a horror of suspense for his doom; for"
"4333"	"he had not the shadow of a doubt that all this hubbub was about him."
"4334"	"He believed he had taxed the forbearance of the powers above to the"
"4335"	"extremity of endurance and that this was the result. It might have"
"4336"	"seemed to him a waste of pomp and ammunition to kill a bug with a"
"4337"	"battery of artillery, but there seemed nothing incongruous about the"
"4338"	"getting up such an expensive thunderstorm as this to knock the turf from"
"4339"	"under an insect like himself."
"4340"	"By and by the tempest spent itself and died without accomplishing its"
"4341"	"object. The boy’s first impulse was to be grateful, and reform. His"
"4342"	"second was to wait--for there might not be any more storms."
"4343"	"The next day the doctors were back; Tom had relapsed. The three weeks he"
"4344"	"spent on his back this time seemed an entire age. When he got abroad"
"4345"	"at last he was hardly grateful that he had been spared, remembering how"
"4346"	"lonely was his estate, how companionless and forlorn he was. He drifted"
"4347"	"listlessly down the street and found Jim Hollis acting as judge in a"
"4348"	"juvenile court that was trying a cat for murder, in the presence of her"
"4349"	"victim, a bird. He found Joe Harper and Huck Finn up an alley eating a"
"4350"	"stolen melon. Poor lads! they--like Tom--had suffered a relapse."
"4351"	"CHAPTER XXIII"
"4352"	"AT last the sleepy atmosphere was stirred--and vigorously: the murder"
"4353"	"trial came on in the court. It became the absorbing topic of village"
"4354"	"talk immediately. Tom could not get away from it. Every reference to"
"4355"	"the murder sent a shudder to his heart, for his troubled conscience"
"4356"	"and fears almost persuaded him that these remarks were put forth in"
"4357"	"his hearing as “feelers”; he did not see how he could be suspected of"
"4358"	"knowing anything about the murder, but still he could not be comfortable"
"4359"	"in the midst of this gossip. It kept him in a cold shiver all the time."
"4360"	"He took Huck to a lonely place to have a talk with him. It would be some"
"4361"	"relief to unseal his tongue for a little while; to divide his burden of"
"4362"	"distress with another sufferer. Moreover, he wanted to assure himself"
"4363"	"that Huck had remained discreet."
"4364"	"“Huck, have you ever told anybody about--that?”"
"4365"	"“‘Bout what?”"
"4366"	"“You know what.”"
"4367"	"“Oh--‘course I haven’t.”"
"4368"	"“Never a word?”"
"4369"	"“Never a solitary word, so help me. What makes you ask?”"
"4370"	"“Well, I was afeard.”"
"4371"	"“Why, Tom Sawyer, we wouldn’t be alive two days if that got found out."
"4372"	"_You_ know that.”"
"4373"	"Tom felt more comfortable. After a pause:"
"4374"	"“Huck, they couldn’t anybody get you to tell, could they?”"
"4375"	"“Get me to tell? Why, if I wanted that halfbreed devil to drownd me they"
"4376"	"could get me to tell. They ain’t no different way.”"
"4377"	"“Well, that’s all right, then. I reckon we’re safe as long as we keep"
"4378"	"mum. But let’s swear again, anyway. It’s more surer.”"
"4379"	"“I’m agreed.”"
"4380"	"So they swore again with dread solemnities."
"4381"	"“What is the talk around, Huck? I’ve heard a power of it.”"
"4382"	"“Talk? Well, it’s just Muff Potter, Muff Potter, Muff Potter all the"
"4383"	"time. It keeps me in a sweat, constant, so’s I want to hide som’ers.”"
"4384"	"“That’s just the same way they go on round me. I reckon he’s a goner."
"4385"	"Don’t you feel sorry for him, sometimes?”"
"4386"	"“Most always--most always. He ain’t no account; but then he hain’t ever"
"4387"	"done anything to hurt anybody. Just fishes a little, to get money to"
"4388"	"get drunk on--and loafs around considerable; but lord, we all do"
"4389"	"that--leastways most of us--preachers and such like. But he’s kind of"
"4390"	"good--he give me half a fish, once, when there warn’t enough for two; and"
"4391"	"lots of times he’s kind of stood by me when I was out of luck.”"
"4392"	"“Well, he’s mended kites for me, Huck, and knitted hooks on to my line."
"4393"	"I wish we could get him out of there.”"
"4394"	"“My! we couldn’t get him out, Tom. And besides, ‘twouldn’t do any good;"
"4395"	"they’d ketch him again.”"
"4396"	"“Yes--so they would. But I hate to hear ‘em abuse him so like the dickens"
"4397"	"when he never done--that.”"
"4398"	"“I do too, Tom. Lord, I hear ‘em say he’s the bloodiest looking villain"
"4399"	"in this country, and they wonder he wasn’t ever hung before.”"
"4400"	"“Yes, they talk like that, all the time. I’ve heard ‘em say that if he"
"4401"	"was to get free they’d lynch him.”"
"4402"	"“And they’d do it, too.”"
"4403"	"The boys had a long talk, but it brought them little comfort. As the"
"4404"	"twilight drew on, they found themselves hanging about the neighborhood"
"4405"	"of the little isolated jail, perhaps with an undefined hope that"
"4406"	"something would happen that might clear away their difficulties. But"
"4407"	"nothing happened; there seemed to be no angels or fairies interested in"
"4408"	"this luckless captive."
"4409"	"The boys did as they had often done before--went to the cell grating and"
"4410"	"gave Potter some tobacco and matches. He was on the ground floor and"
"4411"	"there were no guards."
"4412"	"His gratitude for their gifts had always smote their consciences"
"4413"	"before--it cut deeper than ever, this time. They felt cowardly and"
"4414"	"treacherous to the last degree when Potter said:"
"4415"	"“You’ve been mighty good to me, boys--better’n anybody else in this town."
"4416"	"And I don’t forget it, I don’t. Often I says to myself, says I, ‘I used"
"4417"	"to mend all the boys’ kites and things, and show ‘em where the good"
"4418"	"fishin’ places was, and befriend ‘em what I could, and now they’ve"
"4419"	"all forgot old Muff when he’s in trouble; but Tom don’t, and Huck"
"4420"	"don’t--_they_ don’t forget him, says I, ‘and I don’t forget them.’ Well,"
"4421"	"boys, I done an awful thing--drunk and crazy at the time--that’s the only"
"4422"	"way I account for it--and now I got to swing for it, and it’s right."
"4423"	"Right, and _best_, too, I reckon--hope so, anyway. Well, we won’t talk"
"4424"	"about that. I don’t want to make _you_ feel bad; you’ve befriended me."
"4425"	"But what I want to say, is, don’t _you_ ever get drunk--then you won’t"
"4426"	"ever get here. Stand a litter furder west--so--that’s it; it’s a prime"
"4427"	"comfort to see faces that’s friendly when a body’s in such a muck"
"4428"	"of trouble, and there don’t none come here but yourn. Good friendly"
"4429"	"faces--good friendly faces. Git up on one another’s backs and let me"
"4430"	"touch ‘em. That’s it. Shake hands--yourn’ll come through the bars, but"
"4431"	"mine’s too big. Little hands, and weak--but they’ve helped Muff Potter a"
"4432"	"power, and they’d help him more if they could.”"
"4433"	"Tom went home miserable, and his dreams that night were full of horrors."
"4434"	"The next day and the day after, he hung about the courtroom, drawn by an"
"4435"	"almost irresistible impulse to go in, but forcing himself to stay out."
"4436"	"Huck was having the same experience. They studiously avoided each other."
"4437"	"Each wandered away, from time to time, but the same dismal fascination"
"4438"	"always brought them back presently. Tom kept his ears open when idlers"
"4439"	"sauntered out of the courtroom, but invariably heard distressing"
"4440"	"news--the toils were closing more and more relentlessly around poor"
"4441"	"Potter. At the end of the second day the village talk was to the effect"
"4442"	"that Injun Joe’s evidence stood firm and unshaken, and that there was"
"4443"	"not the slightest question as to what the jury’s verdict would be."
"4444"	"Tom was out late, that night, and came to bed through the window. He"
"4445"	"was in a tremendous state of excitement. It was hours before he got to"
"4446"	"sleep. All the village flocked to the courthouse the next morning, for"
"4447"	"this was to be the great day. Both sexes were about equally represented"
"4448"	"in the packed audience. After a long wait the jury filed in and took"
"4449"	"their places; shortly afterward, Potter, pale and haggard, timid and"
"4450"	"hopeless, was brought in, with chains upon him, and seated where all"
"4451"	"the curious eyes could stare at him; no less conspicuous was Injun Joe,"
"4452"	"stolid as ever. There was another pause, and then the judge arrived and"
"4453"	"the sheriff proclaimed the opening of the court. The usual whisperings"
"4454"	"among the lawyers and gathering together of papers followed. These"
"4455"	"details and accompanying delays worked up an atmosphere of preparation"
"4456"	"that was as impressive as it was fascinating."
"4457"	"Now a witness was called who testified that he found Muff Potter washing"
"4458"	"in the brook, at an early hour of the morning that the murder was"
"4459"	"discovered, and that he immediately sneaked away. After some further"
"4460"	"questioning, counsel for the prosecution said:"
"4461"	"“Take the witness.”"
"4462"	"The prisoner raised his eyes for a moment, but dropped them again when"
"4463"	"his own counsel said:"
"4464"	"“I have no questions to ask him.”"
"4465"	"The next witness proved the finding of the knife near the corpse."
"4466"	"Counsel for the prosecution said:"
"4467"	"“Take the witness.”"
"4468"	"“I have no questions to ask him,” Potter’s lawyer replied."
"4469"	"A third witness swore he had often seen the knife in Potter’s"
"4470"	"possession."
"4471"	"“Take the witness.”"
"4472"	"Counsel for Potter declined to question him. The faces of the audience"
"4473"	"began to betray annoyance. Did this attorney mean to throw away his"
"4474"	"client’s life without an effort?"
"4475"	"Several witnesses deposed concerning Potter’s guilty behavior when"
"4476"	"brought to the scene of the murder. They were allowed to leave the stand"
"4477"	"without being cross-questioned."
"4478"	"Every detail of the damaging circumstances that occurred in the"
"4479"	"graveyard upon that morning which all present remembered so well was"
"4480"	"brought out by credible witnesses, but none of them were cross-examined"
"4481"	"by Potter’s lawyer. The perplexity and dissatisfaction of the house"
"4482"	"expressed itself in murmurs and provoked a reproof from the bench."
"4483"	"Counsel for the prosecution now said:"
"4484"	"“By the oaths of citizens whose simple word is above suspicion, we have"
"4485"	"fastened this awful crime, beyond all possibility of question, upon the"
"4486"	"unhappy prisoner at the bar. We rest our case here.”"
"4487"	"A groan escaped from poor Potter, and he put his face in his hands and"
"4488"	"rocked his body softly to and fro, while a painful silence reigned"
"4489"	"in the courtroom. Many men were moved, and many women’s compassion"
"4490"	"testified itself in tears. Counsel for the defence rose and said:"
"4491"	"“Your honor, in our remarks at the opening of this trial, we"
"4492"	"foreshadowed our purpose to prove that our client did this fearful deed"
"4493"	"while under the influence of a blind and irresponsible delirium produced"
"4494"	"by drink. We have changed our mind. We shall not offer that plea.” [Then"
"4495"	"to the clerk:] “Call Thomas Sawyer!”"
"4496"	"A puzzled amazement awoke in every face in the house, not even excepting"
"4497"	"Potter’s. Every eye fastened itself with wondering interest upon Tom as"
"4498"	"he rose and took his place upon the stand. The boy looked wild enough,"
"4499"	"for he was badly scared. The oath was administered."
"4500"	"“Thomas Sawyer, where were you on the seventeenth of June, about the"
"4501"	"hour of midnight?”"
"4502"	"Tom glanced at Injun Joe’s iron face and his tongue failed him. The"
"4503"	"audience listened breathless, but the words refused to come. After a few"
"4504"	"moments, however, the boy got a little of his strength back, and managed"
"4505"	"to put enough of it into his voice to make part of the house hear:"
"4506"	"“In the graveyard!”"
"4507"	"“A little bit louder, please. Don’t be afraid. You were--”"
"4508"	"“In the graveyard.”"
"4509"	"A contemptuous smile flitted across Injun Joe’s face."
"4510"	"“Were you anywhere near Horse Williams’ grave?”"
"4511"	"“Yes, sir.”"
"4512"	"“Speak up--just a trifle louder. How near were you?”"
"4513"	"“Near as I am to you.”"
"4514"	"“Were you hidden, or not?”"
"4515"	"“I was hid.”"
"4516"	"“Where?”"
"4517"	"“Behind the elms that’s on the edge of the grave.”"
"4518"	"Injun Joe gave a barely perceptible start."
"4519"	"“Any one with you?”"
"4520"	"“Yes, sir. I went there with--”"
"4521"	"“Wait--wait a moment. Never mind mentioning your companion’s name. We"
"4522"	"will produce him at the proper time. Did you carry anything there with"
"4523"	"you.”"
"4524"	"Tom hesitated and looked confused."
"4525"	"“Speak out, my boy--don’t be diffident. The truth is always respectable."
"4526"	"What did you take there?”"
"4527"	"“Only a--a--dead cat.”"
"4528"	"There was a ripple of mirth, which the court checked."
"4529"	"“We will produce the skeleton of that cat. Now, my boy, tell us"
"4530"	"everything that occurred--tell it in your own way--don’t skip anything,"
"4531"	"and don’t be afraid.”"
"4532"	"Tom began--hesitatingly at first, but as he warmed to his subject his"
"4533"	"words flowed more and more easily; in a little while every sound ceased"
"4534"	"but his own voice; every eye fixed itself upon him; with parted lips and"
"4535"	"bated breath the audience hung upon his words, taking no note of time,"
"4536"	"rapt in the ghastly fascinations of the tale. The strain upon pent"
"4537"	"emotion reached its climax when the boy said:"
"4538"	"“--and as the doctor fetched the board around and Muff Potter fell, Injun"
"4539"	"Joe jumped with the knife and--”"
"4540"	"Crash! Quick as lightning the halfbreed sprang for a window, tore his"
"4541"	"way through all opposers, and was gone!"
"4542"	"CHAPTER XXIV"
"4543"	"TOM was a glittering hero once more--the pet of the old, the envy of the"
"4544"	"young. His name even went into immortal print, for the village paper"
"4545"	"magnified him. There were some that believed he would be President, yet,"
"4546"	"if he escaped hanging."
"4547"	"As usual, the fickle, unreasoning world took Muff Potter to its bosom"
"4548"	"and fondled him as lavishly as it had abused him before. But that sort"
"4549"	"of conduct is to the world’s credit; therefore it is not well to find"
"4550"	"fault with it."
"4551"	"Tom’s days were days of splendor and exultation to him, but his nights"
"4552"	"were seasons of horror. Injun Joe infested all his dreams, and always"
"4553"	"with doom in his eye. Hardly any temptation could persuade the boy"
"4554"	"to stir abroad after nightfall. Poor Huck was in the same state of"
"4555"	"wretchedness and terror, for Tom had told the whole story to the lawyer"
"4556"	"the night before the great day of the trial, and Huck was sore afraid"
"4557"	"that his share in the business might leak out, yet, notwithstanding"
"4558"	"Injun Joe’s flight had saved him the suffering of testifying in court."
"4559"	"The poor fellow had got the attorney to promise secrecy, but what of"
"4560"	"that? Since Tom’s harassed conscience had managed to drive him to the"
"4561"	"lawyer’s house by night and wring a dread tale from lips that had"
"4562"	"been sealed with the dismalest and most formidable of oaths, Huck’s"
"4563"	"confidence in the human race was wellnigh obliterated."
"4564"	"Daily Muff Potter’s gratitude made Tom glad he had spoken; but nightly"
"4565"	"he wished he had sealed up his tongue."
"4566"	"Half the time Tom was afraid Injun Joe would never be captured; the"
"4567"	"other half he was afraid he would be. He felt sure he never could draw a"
"4568"	"safe breath again until that man was dead and he had seen the corpse."
"4569"	"Rewards had been offered, the country had been scoured, but no Injun"
"4570"	"Joe was found. One of those omniscient and aweinspiring marvels, a"
"4571"	"detective, came up from St. Louis, moused around, shook his head, looked"
"4572"	"wise, and made that sort of astounding success which members of that"
"4573"	"craft usually achieve. That is to say, he “found a clew.” But you can’t"
"4574"	"hang a “clew” for murder, and so after that detective had got through"
"4575"	"and gone home, Tom felt just as insecure as he was before."
"4576"	"The slow days drifted on, and each left behind it a slightly lightened"
"4577"	"weight of apprehension."
"4578"	"CHAPTER XXV"
"4579"	"THERE comes a time in every rightly-constructed boy’s life when he has"
"4580"	"a raging desire to go somewhere and dig for hidden treasure. This desire"
"4581"	"suddenly came upon Tom one day. He sallied out to find Joe Harper,"
"4582"	"but failed of success. Next he sought Ben Rogers; he had gone fishing."
"4583"	"Presently he stumbled upon Huck Finn the Red-Handed. Huck would"
"4584"	"answer. Tom took him to a private place and opened the matter to him"
"4585"	"confidentially. Huck was willing. Huck was always willing to take a hand"
"4586"	"in any enterprise that offered entertainment and required no capital,"
"4587"	"for he had a troublesome superabundance of that sort of time which is"
"4588"	"not money. “Where’ll we dig?” said Huck."
"4589"	"“Oh, most anywhere.”"
"4590"	"“Why, is it hid all around?”"
"4591"	"“No, indeed it ain’t. It’s hid in mighty particular places,"
"4592"	"Huck--sometimes on islands, sometimes in rotten chests under the end of"
"4593"	"a limb of an old dead tree, just where the shadow falls at midnight; but"
"4594"	"mostly under the floor in ha’nted houses.”"
"4595"	"“Who hides it?”"
"4596"	"“Why, robbers, of course--who’d you reckon? Sunday-school"
"4597"	"sup’rintendents?”"
"4598"	"“I don’t know. If ‘twas mine I wouldn’t hide it; I’d spend it and have a"
"4599"	"good time.”"
"4600"	"“So would I. But robbers don’t do that way. They always hide it and"
"4601"	"leave it there.”"
"4602"	"“Don’t they come after it any more?”"
"4603"	"“No, they think they will, but they generally forget the marks, or else"
"4604"	"they die. Anyway, it lays there a long time and gets rusty; and by and"
"4605"	"by somebody finds an old yellow paper that tells how to find the marks--a"
"4606"	"paper that’s got to be ciphered over about a week because it’s mostly"
"4607"	"signs and hy’roglyphics.”"
"4608"	"“Hyro--which?”"
"4609"	"“Hy’roglyphics--pictures and things, you know, that don’t seem to mean"
"4610"	"anything.”"
"4611"	"“Have you got one of them papers, Tom?”"
"4612"	"“No.”"
"4613"	"“Well then, how you going to find the marks?”"
"4614"	"“I don’t want any marks. They always bury it under a ha’nted house or on"
"4615"	"an island, or under a dead tree that’s got one limb sticking out. Well,"
"4616"	"we’ve tried Jackson’s Island a little, and we can try it again some"
"4617"	"time; and there’s the old ha’nted house up the Still-House branch, and"
"4618"	"there’s lots of dead-limb trees--dead loads of ‘em.”"
"4619"	"“Is it under all of them?”"
"4620"	"“How you talk! No!”"
"4621"	"“Then how you going to know which one to go for?”"
"4622"	"“Go for all of ‘em!”"
"4623"	"“Why, Tom, it’ll take all summer.”"
"4624"	"“Well, what of that? Suppose you find a brass pot with a hundred dollars"
"4625"	"in it, all rusty and gray, or rotten chest full of di’monds. How’s"
"4626"	"that?”"
"4627"	"Huck’s eyes glowed."
"4628"	"“That’s bully. Plenty bully enough for me. Just you gimme the hundred"
"4629"	"dollars and I don’t want no di’monds.”"
"4630"	"“All right. But I bet you I ain’t going to throw off on di’monds. Some"
"4631"	"of ‘em’s worth twenty dollars apiece--there ain’t any, hardly, but’s"
"4632"	"worth six bits or a dollar.”"
"4633"	"“No! Is that so?”"
"4634"	"“Cert’nly--anybody’ll tell you so. Hain’t you ever seen one, Huck?”"
"4635"	"“Not as I remember.”"
"4636"	"“Oh, kings have slathers of them.”"
"4637"	"“Well, I don’ know no kings, Tom.”"
"4638"	"“I reckon you don’t. But if you was to go to Europe you’d see a raft of"
"4639"	"‘em hopping around.”"
"4640"	"“Do they hop?”"
"4641"	"“Hop?--your granny! No!”"
"4642"	"“Well, what did you say they did, for?”"
"4643"	"“Shucks, I only meant you’d _see_ ‘em--not hopping, of course--what do"
"4644"	"they want to hop for?--but I mean you’d just see ‘em--scattered around,"
"4645"	"you know, in a kind of a general way. Like that old humpbacked Richard.”"
"4646"	"“Richard? What’s his other name?”"
"4647"	"“He didn’t have any other name. Kings don’t have any but a given name.”"
"4648"	"“No?”"
"4649"	"“But they don’t.”"
"4650"	"“Well, if they like it, Tom, all right; but I don’t want to be a king"
"4651"	"and have only just a given name, like a nigger. But say--where you going"
"4652"	"to dig first?”"
"4653"	"“Well, I don’t know. S’pose we tackle that old dead-limb tree on the"
"4654"	"hill t’other side of Still-House branch?”"
"4655"	"“I’m agreed.”"
"4656"	"So they got a crippled pick and a shovel, and set out on their"
"4657"	"three-mile tramp. They arrived hot and panting, and threw themselves"
"4658"	"down in the shade of a neighboring elm to rest and have a smoke."
"4659"	"“I like this,” said Tom."
"4660"	"“So do I.”"
"4661"	"“Say, Huck, if we find a treasure here, what you going to do with your"
"4662"	"share?”"
"4663"	"“Well, I’ll have pie and a glass of soda every day, and I’ll go to every"
"4664"	"circus that comes along. I bet I’ll have a gay time.”"
"4665"	"“Well, ain’t you going to save any of it?”"
"4666"	"“Save it? What for?”"
"4667"	"“Why, so as to have something to live on, by and by.”"
"4668"	"“Oh, that ain’t any use. Pap would come back to thish-yer town some day"
"4669"	"and get his claws on it if I didn’t hurry up, and I tell you he’d clean"
"4670"	"it out pretty quick. What you going to do with yourn, Tom?”"
"4671"	"“I’m going to buy a new drum, and a sure’nough sword, and a red necktie"
"4672"	"and a bull pup, and get married.”"
"4673"	"“Married!”"
"4674"	"“That’s it.”"
"4675"	"“Tom, you--why, you ain’t in your right mind.”"
"4676"	"“Wait--you’ll see.”"
"4677"	"“Well, that’s the foolishest thing you could do. Look at pap and my"
"4678"	"mother. Fight! Why, they used to fight all the time. I remember, mighty"
"4679"	"well.”"
"4680"	"“That ain’t anything. The girl I’m going to marry won’t fight.”"
"4681"	"“Tom, I reckon they’re all alike. They’ll all comb a body. Now you"
"4682"	"better think ‘bout this awhile. I tell you you better. What’s the name"
"4683"	"of the gal?”"
"4684"	"“It ain’t a gal at all--it’s a girl.”"
"4685"	"“It’s all the same, I reckon; some says gal, some says girl--both’s"
"4686"	"right, like enough. Anyway, what’s her name, Tom?”"
"4687"	"“I’ll tell you some time--not now.”"
"4688"	"“All right--that’ll do. Only if you get married I’ll be more lonesomer"
"4689"	"than ever.”"
"4690"	"“No you won’t. You’ll come and live with me. Now stir out of this and"
"4691"	"we’ll go to digging.”"
"4692"	"They worked and sweated for half an hour. No result. They toiled another"
"4693"	"halfhour. Still no result. Huck said:"
"4694"	"“Do they always bury it as deep as this?”"
"4695"	"“Sometimes--not always. Not generally. I reckon we haven’t got the right"
"4696"	"place.”"
"4697"	"So they chose a new spot and began again. The labor dragged a little,"
"4698"	"but still they made progress. They pegged away in silence for some time."
"4699"	"Finally Huck leaned on his shovel, swabbed the beaded drops from his"
"4700"	"brow with his sleeve, and said:"
"4701"	"“Where you going to dig next, after we get this one?”"
"4702"	"“I reckon maybe we’ll tackle the old tree that’s over yonder on Cardiff"
"4703"	"Hill back of the widow’s.”"
"4704"	"“I reckon that’ll be a good one. But won’t the widow take it away from"
"4705"	"us, Tom? It’s on her land.”"
"4706"	"“_She_ take it away! Maybe she’d like to try it once. Whoever finds one"
"4707"	"of these hid treasures, it belongs to him. It don’t make any difference"
"4708"	"whose land it’s on.”"
"4709"	"That was satisfactory. The work went on. By and by Huck said:"
"4710"	"“Blame it, we must be in the wrong place again. What do you think?”"
"4711"	"“It is mighty curious, Huck. I don’t understand it. Sometimes witches"
"4712"	"interfere. I reckon maybe that’s what’s the trouble now.”"
"4713"	"“Shucks! Witches ain’t got no power in the daytime.”"
"4714"	"“Well, that’s so. I didn’t think of that. Oh, I know what the matter is!"
"4715"	"What a blamed lot of fools we are! You got to find out where the shadow"
"4716"	"of the limb falls at midnight, and that’s where you dig!”"
"4717"	"“Then consound it, we’ve fooled away all this work for nothing. Now hang"
"4718"	"it all, we got to come back in the night. It’s an awful long way. Can"
"4719"	"you get out?”"
"4720"	"“I bet I will. We’ve got to do it tonight, too, because if somebody sees"
"4721"	"these holes they’ll know in a minute what’s here and they’ll go for it.”"
"4722"	"“Well, I’ll come around and maow tonight.”"
"4723"	"“All right. Let’s hide the tools in the bushes.”"
"4724"	"The boys were there that night, about the appointed time. They sat in"
"4725"	"the shadow waiting. It was a lonely place, and an hour made solemn by"
"4726"	"old traditions. Spirits whispered in the rustling leaves, ghosts lurked"
"4727"	"in the murky nooks, the deep baying of a hound floated up out of the"
"4728"	"distance, an owl answered with his sepulchral note. The boys were"
"4729"	"subdued by these solemnities, and talked little. By and by they judged"
"4730"	"that twelve had come; they marked where the shadow fell, and began to"
"4731"	"dig. Their hopes commenced to rise. Their interest grew stronger, and"
"4732"	"their industry kept pace with it. The hole deepened and still deepened,"
"4733"	"but every time their hearts jumped to hear the pick strike upon"
"4734"	"something, they only suffered a new disappointment. It was only a stone"
"4735"	"or a chunk. At last Tom said:"
"4736"	"“It ain’t any use, Huck, we’re wrong again.”"
"4737"	"“Well, but we _can’t_ be wrong. We spotted the shadder to a dot.”"
"4738"	"“I know it, but then there’s another thing.”"
"4739"	"“What’s that?”."
"4740"	"“Why, we only guessed at the time. Like enough it was too late or too"
"4741"	"early.”"
"4742"	"Huck dropped his shovel."
"4743"	"“That’s it,” said he. “That’s the very trouble. We got to give this one"
"4744"	"up. We can’t ever tell the right time, and besides this kind of thing’s"
"4745"	"too awful, here this time of night with witches and ghosts a-fluttering"
"4746"	"around so. I feel as if something’s behind me all the time;  and I’m"
"4747"	"afeard to turn around, becuz maybe there’s others in front a-waiting for"
"4748"	"a chance. I been creeping all over, ever since I got here.”"
"4749"	"“Well, I’ve been pretty much so, too, Huck. They most always put in a"
"4750"	"dead man when they bury a treasure under a tree, to look out for it.”"
"4751"	"“Lordy!”"
"4752"	"“Yes, they do. I’ve always heard that.”"
"4753"	"“Tom, I don’t like to fool around much where there’s dead people. A"
"4754"	"body’s bound to get into trouble with ‘em, sure.”"
"4755"	"“I don’t like to stir ‘em up, either. S’pose this one here was to stick"
"4756"	"his skull out and say something!”"
"4757"	"“Don’t Tom! It’s awful.”"
"4758"	"“Well, it just is. Huck, I don’t feel comfortable a bit.”"
"4759"	"“Say, Tom, let’s give this place up, and try somewheres else.”"
"4760"	"“All right, I reckon we better.”"
"4761"	"“What’ll it be?”"
"4762"	"Tom considered awhile; and then said:"
"4763"	"“The ha’nted house. That’s it!”"
"4764"	"“Blame it, I don’t like ha’nted houses, Tom. Why, they’re a dern sight"
"4765"	"worse’n dead people. Dead people might talk, maybe, but they don’t come"
"4766"	"sliding around in a shroud, when you ain’t noticing, and peep over your"
"4767"	"shoulder all of a sudden and grit their teeth, the way a ghost does. I"
"4768"	"couldn’t stand such a thing as that, Tom--nobody could.”"
"4769"	"“Yes, but, Huck, ghosts don’t travel around only at night. They won’t"
"4770"	"hender us from digging there in the daytime.”"
"4771"	"“Well, that’s so. But you know mighty well people don’t go about that"
"4772"	"ha’nted house in the day nor the night.”"
"4773"	"“Well, that’s mostly because they don’t like to go where a man’s been"
"4774"	"murdered, anyway--but nothing’s ever been seen around that house except"
"4775"	"in the night--just some blue lights slipping by the windows--no regular"
"4776"	"ghosts.”"
"4777"	"“Well, where you see one of them blue lights flickering around, Tom,"
"4778"	"you can bet there’s a ghost mighty close behind it. It stands to reason."
"4779"	"Becuz you know that they don’t anybody but ghosts use ‘em.”"
"4780"	"“Yes, that’s so. But anyway they don’t come around in the daytime, so"
"4781"	"what’s the use of our being afeard?”"
"4782"	"“Well, all right. We’ll tackle the ha’nted house if you say so--but I"
"4783"	"reckon it’s taking chances.”"
"4784"	"They had started down the hill by this time. There in the middle of the"
"4785"	"moonlit valley below them stood the “ha’nted” house, utterly isolated,"
"4786"	"its fences gone long ago, rank weeds smothering the very doorsteps, the"
"4787"	"chimney crumbled to ruin, the window-sashes vacant, a corner of the roof"
"4788"	"caved in. The boys gazed awhile, half expecting to see a blue light flit"
"4789"	"past a window; then talking in a low tone, as befitted the time and the"
"4790"	"circumstances, they struck far off to the right, to give the haunted"
"4791"	"house a wide berth, and took their way homeward through the woods that"
"4792"	"adorned the rearward side of Cardiff Hill."
"4793"	"CHAPTER XVI"
"4794"	"ABOUT noon the next day the boys arrived at the dead tree; they had come"
"4795"	"for their tools. Tom was impatient to go to the haunted house; Huck was"
"4796"	"measurably so, also--but suddenly said:"
"4797"	"“Lookyhere, Tom, do you know what day it is?”"
"4798"	"Tom mentally ran over the days of the week, and then quickly lifted his"
"4799"	"eyes with a startled look in them--"
"4800"	"“My! I never once thought of it, Huck!”"
"4801"	"“Well, I didn’t neither, but all at once it popped onto me that it was"
"4802"	"Friday.”"
"4803"	"“Blame it, a body can’t be too careful, Huck. We might ‘a’ got into an"
"4804"	"awful scrape, tackling such a thing on a Friday.”"
"4805"	"“_Might_! Better say we _would_! There’s some lucky days, maybe, but"
"4806"	"Friday ain’t.”"
"4807"	"“Any fool knows that. I don’t reckon _you_ was the first that found it"
"4808"	"out, Huck.”"
"4809"	"“Well, I never said I was, did I? And Friday ain’t all, neither. I had a"
"4810"	"rotten bad dream last night--dreampt about rats.”"
"4811"	"“No! Sure sign of trouble. Did they fight?”"
"4812"	"“No.”"
"4813"	"“Well, that’s good, Huck. When they don’t fight it’s only a sign that"
"4814"	"there’s trouble around, you know. All we got to do is to look mighty"
"4815"	"sharp and keep out of it. We’ll drop this thing for today, and play. Do"
"4816"	"you know Robin Hood, Huck?”"
"4817"	"“No. Who’s Robin Hood?”"
"4818"	"“Why, he was one of the greatest men that was ever in England--and the"
"4819"	"best. He was a robber.”"
"4820"	"“Cracky, I wisht I was. Who did he rob?”"
"4821"	"“Only sheriffs and bishops and rich people and kings, and such like. But"
"4822"	"he never bothered the poor. He loved ‘em. He always divided up with ‘em"
"4823"	"perfectly square.”"
"4824"	"“Well, he must ‘a’ been a brick.”"
"4825"	"“I bet you he was, Huck. Oh, he was the noblest man that ever was."
"4826"	"They ain’t any such men now, I can tell you. He could lick any man in"
"4827"	"England, with one hand tied behind him; and he could take his yew bow"
"4828"	"and plug a ten-cent piece every time, a mile and a half.”"
"4829"	"“What’s a _yew_ bow?”"
"4830"	"“I don’t know. It’s some kind of a bow, of course. And if he hit that"
"4831"	"dime only on the edge he would set down and cry--and curse. But we’ll"
"4832"	"play Robin Hood--it’s nobby fun. I’ll learn you.”"
"4833"	"“I’m agreed.”"
"4834"	"So they played Robin Hood all the afternoon, now and then casting a"
"4835"	"yearning eye down upon the haunted house and passing a remark about the"
"4836"	"morrow’s prospects and possibilities there. As the sun began to sink"
"4837"	"into the west they took their way homeward athwart the long shadows"
"4838"	"of the trees and soon were buried from sight in the forests of Cardiff"
"4839"	"Hill."
"4840"	"On Saturday, shortly after noon, the boys were at the dead tree again."
"4841"	"They had a smoke and a chat in the shade, and then dug a little in their"
"4842"	"last hole, not with great hope, but merely because Tom said there were"
"4843"	"so many cases where people had given up a treasure after getting down"
"4844"	"within six inches of it, and then somebody else had come along and"
"4845"	"turned it up with a single thrust of a shovel. The thing failed this"
"4846"	"time, however, so the boys shouldered their tools and went away feeling"
"4847"	"that they had not trifled with fortune, but had fulfilled all the"
"4848"	"requirements that belong to the business of treasure-hunting."
"4849"	"When they reached the haunted house there was something so weird and"
"4850"	"grisly about the dead silence that reigned there under the baking sun,"
"4851"	"and something so depressing about the loneliness and desolation of the"
"4852"	"place, that they were afraid, for a moment, to venture in. Then they"
"4853"	"crept to the door and took a trembling peep. They saw a weedgrown,"
"4854"	"floorless room, unplastered, an ancient fireplace, vacant windows,"
"4855"	"a ruinous staircase; and here, there, and everywhere hung ragged and"
"4856"	"abandoned cobwebs. They presently entered, softly, with quickened"
"4857"	"pulses, talking in whispers, ears alert to catch the slightest sound,"
"4858"	"and muscles tense and ready for instant retreat."
"4859"	"In a little while familiarity modified their fears and they gave the"
"4860"	"place a critical and interested examination, rather admiring their own"
"4861"	"boldness, and wondering at it, too. Next they wanted to look upstairs."
"4862"	"This was something like cutting off retreat, but they got to daring"
"4863"	"each other, and of course there could be but one result--they threw their"
"4864"	"tools into a corner and made the ascent. Up there were the same signs of"
"4865"	"decay. In one corner they found a closet that promised mystery, but the"
