"4866"	"promise was a fraud--there was nothing in it. Their courage was up now"
"4867"	"and well in hand. They were about to go down and begin work when--"
"4868"	"“Sh!” said Tom."
"4869"	"“What is it?” whispered Huck, blanching with fright."
"4870"	"“Sh!... There!... Hear it?”"
"4871"	"“Yes!... Oh, my! Let’s run!”"
"4872"	"“Keep still! Don’t you budge! They’re coming right toward the door.”"
"4873"	"The boys stretched themselves upon the floor with their eyes to"
"4874"	"knotholes in the planking, and lay waiting, in a misery of fear."
"4875"	"“They’ve stopped.... No--coming.... Here they are. Don’t whisper another"
"4876"	"word, Huck. My goodness, I wish I was out of this!”"
"4877"	"Two men entered. Each boy said to himself: “There’s the old deaf and"
"4878"	"dumb Spaniard that’s been about town once or twice lately--never saw"
"4879"	"t’other man before.”"
"4880"	"“T’other” was a ragged, unkempt creature, with nothing very pleasant"
"4881"	"in his face. The Spaniard was wrapped in a serape; he had bushy white"
"4882"	"whiskers; long white hair flowed from under his sombrero, and he wore"
"4883"	"green goggles. When they came in, “t’other” was talking in a low voice;"
"4884"	"they sat down on the ground, facing the door, with their backs to the"
"4885"	"wall, and the speaker continued his remarks. His manner became less"
"4886"	"guarded and his words more distinct as he proceeded:"
"4887"	"“No,” said he, “I’ve thought it all over, and I don’t like it. It’s"
"4888"	"dangerous.”"
"4889"	"“Dangerous!” grunted the “deaf and dumb” Spaniard--to the vast surprise"
"4890"	"of the boys. “Milksop!”"
"4891"	"This voice made the boys gasp and quake. It was Injun Joe’s! There was"
"4892"	"silence for some time. Then Joe said:"
"4893"	"“What’s any more dangerous than that job up yonder--but nothing’s come of"
"4894"	"it.”"
"4895"	"“That’s different. Away up the river so, and not another house about."
"4896"	"‘Twon’t ever be known that we tried, anyway, long as we didn’t succeed.”"
"4897"	"“Well, what’s more dangerous than coming here in the daytime!--anybody"
"4898"	"would suspicion us that saw us.”"
"4899"	"“I know that. But there warn’t any other place as handy after that fool"
"4900"	"of a job. I want to quit this shanty. I wanted to yesterday, only it"
"4901"	"warn’t any use trying to stir out of here, with those infernal boys"
"4902"	"playing over there on the hill right in full view.”"
"4903"	"“Those infernal boys” quaked again under the inspiration of this remark,"
"4904"	"and thought how lucky it was that they had remembered it was Friday and"
"4905"	"concluded to wait a day. They wished in their hearts they had waited a"
"4906"	"year."
"4907"	"The two men got out some food and made a luncheon. After a long and"
"4908"	"thoughtful silence, Injun Joe said:"
"4909"	"“Look here, lad--you go back up the river where you belong. Wait there"
"4910"	"till you hear from me. I’ll take the chances on dropping into this town"
"4911"	"just once more, for a look. We’ll do that ‘dangerous’ job after I’ve"
"4912"	"spied around a little and think things look well for it. Then for Texas!"
"4913"	"We’ll leg it together!”"
"4914"	"This was satisfactory. Both men presently fell to yawning, and Injun Joe"
"4915"	"said:"
"4916"	"“I’m dead for sleep! It’s your turn to watch.”"
"4917"	"He curled down in the weeds and soon began to snore. His comrade stirred"
"4918"	"him once or twice and he became quiet. Presently the watcher began to"
"4919"	"nod; his head drooped lower and lower, both men began to snore now."
"4920"	"The boys drew a long, grateful breath. Tom whispered:"
"4921"	"“Now’s our chance--come!”"
"4922"	"Huck said:"
"4923"	"“I can’t--I’d die if they was to wake.”"
"4924"	"Tom urged--Huck held back. At last Tom rose slowly and softly, and"
"4925"	"started alone. But the first step he made wrung such a hideous creak"
"4926"	"from the crazy floor that he sank down almost dead with fright. He never"
"4927"	"made a second attempt. The boys lay there counting the dragging moments"
"4928"	"till it seemed to them that time must be done and eternity growing gray;"
"4929"	"and then they were grateful to note that at last the sun was setting."
"4930"	"Now one snore ceased. Injun Joe sat up, stared around--smiled grimly upon"
"4931"	"his comrade, whose head was drooping upon his knees--stirred him up with"
"4932"	"his foot and said:"
"4933"	"“Here! _You’re_ a watchman, ain’t you! All right, though--nothing’s"
"4934"	"happened.”"
"4935"	"“My! have I been asleep?”"
"4936"	"“Oh, partly, partly. Nearly time for us to be moving, pard. What’ll we"
"4937"	"do with what little swag we’ve got left?”"
"4938"	"“I don’t know--leave it here as we’ve always done, I reckon. No use to"
"4939"	"take it away till we start south. Six hundred and fifty in silver’s"
"4940"	"something to carry.”"
"4941"	"“Well--all right--it won’t matter to come here once more.”"
"4942"	"“No--but I’d say come in the night as we used to do--it’s better.”"
"4943"	"“Yes: but look here; it may be a good while before I get the right"
"4944"	"chance at that job; accidents might happen; ‘tain’t in such a very good"
"4945"	"place; we’ll just regularly bury it--and bury it deep.”"
"4946"	"“Good idea,” said the comrade, who walked across the room, knelt down,"
"4947"	"raised one of the rearward hearth-stones and took out a bag that jingled"
"4948"	"pleasantly. He subtracted from it twenty or thirty dollars for himself"
"4949"	"and as much for Injun Joe, and passed the bag to the latter, who was on"
"4950"	"his knees in the corner, now, digging with his bowie-knife."
"4951"	"The boys forgot all their fears, all their miseries in an instant. With"
"4952"	"gloating eyes they watched every movement. Luck!--the splendor of it was"
"4953"	"beyond all imagination! Six hundred dollars was money enough to make"
"4954"	"half a dozen boys rich! Here was treasure-hunting under the happiest"
"4955"	"auspices--there would not be any bothersome uncertainty as to where to"
"4956"	"dig. They nudged each other every moment--eloquent nudges and easily"
"4957"	"understood, for they simply meant--“Oh, but ain’t you glad _now_ we’re"
"4958"	"here!”"
"4959"	"Joe’s knife struck upon something."
"4960"	"“Hello!” said he."
"4961"	"“What is it?” said his comrade."
"4962"	"“Half-rotten plank--no, it’s a box, I believe. Here--bear a hand and we’ll"
"4963"	"see what it’s here for. Never mind, I’ve broke a hole.”"
"4964"	"He reached his hand in and drew it out--"
"4965"	"“Man, it’s money!”"
"4966"	"The two men examined the handful of coins. They were gold. The boys"
"4967"	"above were as excited as themselves, and as delighted."
"4968"	"Joe’s comrade said:"
"4969"	"“We’ll make quick work of this. There’s an old rusty pick over amongst"
"4970"	"the weeds in the corner the other side of the fireplace--I saw it a"
"4971"	"minute ago.”"
"4972"	"He ran and brought the boys’ pick and shovel. Injun Joe took the"
"4973"	"pick, looked it over critically, shook his head, muttered something to"
"4974"	"himself, and then began to use it. The box was soon unearthed. It was"
"4975"	"not very large; it was iron bound and had been very strong before the"
"4976"	"slow years had injured it. The men contemplated the treasure awhile in"
"4977"	"blissful silence."
"4978"	"“Pard, there’s thousands of dollars here,” said Injun Joe."
"4979"	"“‘Twas always said that Murrel’s gang used to be around here one"
"4980"	"summer,” the stranger observed."
"4981"	"“I know it,” said Injun Joe; “and this looks like it, I should say.”"
"4982"	"“Now you won’t need to do that job.”"
"4983"	"The halfbreed frowned. Said he:"
"4984"	"“You don’t know me. Least you don’t know all about that thing. ‘Tain’t"
"4985"	"robbery altogether--it’s _revenge_!” and a wicked light flamed in his"
"4986"	"eyes. “I’ll need your help in it. When it’s finished--then Texas. Go home"
"4987"	"to your Nance and your kids, and stand by till you hear from me.”"
"4988"	"“Well--if you say so; what’ll we do with this--bury it again?”"
"4989"	"“Yes. [Ravishing delight overhead.] _No_! by the great Sachem, no!"
"4990"	"[Profound distress overhead.] I’d nearly forgot. That pick had fresh"
"4991"	"earth on it! [The boys were sick with terror in a moment.] What business"
"4992"	"has a pick and a shovel here? What business with fresh earth on"
"4993"	"them? Who brought them here--and where are they gone? Have you heard"
"4994"	"anybody?--seen anybody? What! bury it again and leave them to come and"
"4995"	"see the ground disturbed? Not exactly--not exactly. We’ll take it to my"
"4996"	"den.”"
"4997"	"“Why, of course! Might have thought of that before. You mean Number"
"4998"	"One?”"
"4999"	"“No--Number Two--under the cross. The other place is bad--too common.”"
"5000"	"“All right. It’s nearly dark enough to start.”"
"5001"	"Injun Joe got up and went about from window to window cautiously peeping"
"5002"	"out. Presently he said:"
"5003"	"“Who could have brought those tools here? Do you reckon they can be"
"5004"	"upstairs?”"
"5005"	"The boys’ breath forsook them. Injun Joe put his hand on his knife,"
"5006"	"halted a moment, undecided, and then turned toward the stairway. The"
"5007"	"boys thought of the closet, but their strength was gone. The steps came"
"5008"	"creaking up the stairs--the intolerable distress of the situation woke"
"5009"	"the stricken resolution of the lads--they were about to spring for the"
"5010"	"closet, when there was a crash of rotten timbers and Injun Joe landed on"
"5011"	"the ground amid the debris of the ruined stairway. He gathered himself"
"5012"	"up cursing, and his comrade said:"
"5013"	"“Now what’s the use of all that? If it’s anybody, and they’re up there,"
"5014"	"let them _stay_ there--who cares? If they want to jump down, now, and get"
"5015"	"into trouble, who objects? It will be dark in fifteen minutes--and then"
"5016"	"let them follow us if they want to. I’m willing. In my opinion, whoever"
"5017"	"hove those things in here caught a sight of us and took us for ghosts or"
"5018"	"devils or something. I’ll bet they’re running yet.”"
"5019"	"Joe grumbled awhile; then he agreed with his friend that what daylight"
"5020"	"was left ought to be economized in getting things ready for leaving."
"5021"	"Shortly afterward they slipped out of the house in the deepening"
"5022"	"twilight, and moved toward the river with their precious box."
"5023"	"Tom and Huck rose up, weak but vastly relieved, and stared after them"
"5024"	"through the chinks between the logs of the house. Follow? Not they. They"
"5025"	"were content to reach ground again without broken necks, and take the"
"5026"	"townward track over the hill. They did not talk much. They were too much"
"5027"	"absorbed in hating themselves--hating the ill luck that made them take"
"5028"	"the spade and the pick there. But for that, Injun Joe never would have"
"5029"	"suspected. He would have hidden the silver with the gold to wait"
"5030"	"there till his “revenge” was satisfied, and then he would have had the"
"5031"	"misfortune to find that money turn up missing. Bitter, bitter luck that"
"5032"	"the tools were ever brought there!"
"5033"	"They resolved to keep a lookout for that Spaniard when he should come to"
"5034"	"town spying out for chances to do his revengeful job, and follow him to"
"5035"	"“Number Two,” wherever that might be. Then a ghastly thought occurred to"
"5036"	"Tom."
"5037"	"“Revenge? What if he means _us_, Huck!”"
"5038"	"“Oh, don’t!” said Huck, nearly fainting."
"5039"	"They talked it all over, and as they entered town they agreed to believe"
"5040"	"that he might possibly mean somebody else--at least that he might at"
"5041"	"least mean nobody but Tom, since only Tom had testified."
"5042"	"Very, very small comfort it was to Tom to be alone in danger! Company"
"5043"	"would be a palpable improvement, he thought."
"5044"	"CHAPTER XXVII"
"5045"	"THE adventure of the day mightily tormented Tom’s dreams that night."
"5046"	"Four times he had his hands on that rich treasure and four times"
"5047"	"it wasted to nothingness in his fingers as sleep forsook him and"
"5048"	"wakefulness brought back the hard reality of his misfortune. As he lay"
"5049"	"in the early morning recalling the incidents of his great adventure, he"
"5050"	"noticed that they seemed curiously subdued and far away--somewhat as if"
"5051"	"they had happened in another world, or in a time long gone by. Then it"
"5052"	"occurred to him that the great adventure itself must be a dream! There"
"5053"	"was one very strong argument in favor of this idea--namely, that the"
"5054"	"quantity of coin he had seen was too vast to be real. He had never seen"
"5055"	"as much as fifty dollars in one mass before, and he was like all boys of"
"5056"	"his age and station in life, in that he imagined that all references to"
"5057"	"“hundreds” and “thousands” were mere fanciful forms of speech, and that"
"5058"	"no such sums really existed in the world. He never had supposed for"
"5059"	"a moment that so large a sum as a hundred dollars was to be found in"
"5060"	"actual money in any one’s possession. If his notions of hidden treasure"
"5061"	"had been analyzed, they would have been found to consist of a handful of"
"5062"	"real dimes and a bushel of vague, splendid, ungraspable dollars."
"5063"	"But the incidents of his adventure grew sensibly sharper and clearer"
"5064"	"under the attrition of thinking them over, and so he presently found"
"5065"	"himself leaning to the impression that the thing might not have been a"
"5066"	"dream, after all. This uncertainty must be swept away. He would snatch a"
"5067"	"hurried breakfast and go and find Huck. Huck was sitting on the gunwale"
"5068"	"of a flatboat, listlessly dangling his feet in the water and looking"
"5069"	"very melancholy. Tom concluded to let Huck lead up to the subject. If"
"5070"	"he did not do it, then the adventure would be proved to have been only a"
"5071"	"dream."
"5072"	"“Hello, Huck!”"
"5073"	"“Hello, yourself.”"
"5074"	"Silence, for a minute."
"5075"	"“Tom, if we’d ‘a’ left the blame tools at the dead tree, we’d ‘a’ got"
"5076"	"the money. Oh, ain’t it awful!”"
"5077"	"“‘Tain’t a dream, then, ‘tain’t a dream! Somehow I most wish it was."
"5078"	"Dog’d if I don’t, Huck.”"
"5079"	"“What ain’t a dream?”"
"5080"	"“Oh, that thing yesterday. I been half thinking it was.”"
"5081"	"“Dream! If them stairs hadn’t broke down you’d ‘a’ seen how much dream"
"5082"	"it was! I’ve had dreams enough all night--with that patch-eyed Spanish"
"5083"	"devil going for me all through ‘em--rot him!”"
"5084"	"“No, not rot him. _Find_ him! Track the money!”"
"5085"	"“Tom, we’ll never find him. A feller don’t have only one chance for such"
"5086"	"a pile--and that one’s lost. I’d feel mighty shaky if I was to see him,"
"5087"	"anyway.”"
"5088"	"“Well, so’d I; but I’d like to see him, anyway--and track him out--to his"
"5089"	"Number Two.”"
"5090"	"“Number Two--yes, that’s it. I been thinking ‘bout that. But I can’t make"
"5091"	"nothing out of it. What do you reckon it is?”"
"5092"	"“I dono. It’s too deep. Say, Huck--maybe it’s the number of a house!”"
"5093"	"“Goody!... No, Tom, that ain’t it. If it is, it ain’t in this one-horse"
"5094"	"town. They ain’t no numbers here.”"
"5095"	"“Well, that’s so. Lemme think a minute. Here--it’s the number of a"
"5096"	"room--in a tavern, you know!”"
"5097"	"“Oh, that’s the trick! They ain’t only two taverns. We can find out"
"5098"	"quick.”"
"5099"	"“You stay here, Huck, till I come.”"
"5100"	"Tom was off at once. He did not care to have Huck’s company in public"
"5101"	"places. He was gone half an hour. He found that in the best tavern, No."
"5102"	"2 had long been occupied by a young lawyer, and was still so occupied."
"5103"	"In the less ostentatious house, No. 2 was a mystery. The tavern-keeper’s"
"5104"	"young son said it was kept locked all the time, and he never saw anybody"
"5105"	"go into it or come out of it except at night; he did not know any"
"5106"	"particular reason for this state of things; had had some little"
"5107"	"curiosity, but it was rather feeble; had made the most of the mystery"
"5108"	"by entertaining himself with the idea that that room was “ha’nted”; had"
"5109"	"noticed that there was a light in there the night before."
"5110"	"“That’s what I’ve found out, Huck. I reckon that’s the very No. 2 we’re"
"5111"	"after.”"
"5112"	"“I reckon it is, Tom. Now what you going to do?”"
"5113"	"“Lemme think.”"
"5114"	"Tom thought a long time. Then he said:"
"5115"	"“I’ll tell you. The back door of that No. 2 is the door that comes out"
"5116"	"into that little close alley between the tavern and the old rattle trap"
"5117"	"of a brick store. Now you get hold of all the doorkeys you can find, and"
"5118"	"I’ll nip all of auntie’s, and the first dark night we’ll go there and"
"5119"	"try ‘em. And mind you, keep a lookout for Injun Joe, because he said he"
"5120"	"was going to drop into town and spy around once more for a chance to get"
"5121"	"his revenge. If you see him, you just follow him; and if he don’t go to"
"5122"	"that No. 2, that ain’t the place.”"
"5123"	"“Lordy, I don’t want to foller him by myself!”"
"5124"	"“Why, it’ll be night, sure. He mightn’t ever see you--and if he did,"
"5125"	"maybe he’d never think anything.”"
"5126"	"“Well, if it’s pretty dark I reckon I’ll track him. I dono--I dono. I’ll"
"5127"	"try.”"
"5128"	"“You bet I’ll follow him, if it’s dark, Huck. Why, he might ‘a’ found"
"5129"	"out he couldn’t get his revenge, and be going right after that money.”"
"5130"	"“It’s so, Tom, it’s so. I’ll foller him; I will, by jingoes!”"
"5131"	"“Now you’re _talking_! Don’t you ever weaken, Huck, and I won’t.”"
"5132"	"CHAPTER XXVIII"
"5133"	"THAT night Tom and Huck were ready for their adventure. They hung about"
"5134"	"the neighborhood of the tavern until after nine, one watching the alley"
"5135"	"at a distance and the other the tavern door. Nobody entered the alley or"
"5136"	"left it; nobody resembling the Spaniard entered or left the tavern"
"5137"	"door. The night promised to be a fair one; so Tom went home with the"
"5138"	"understanding that if a considerable degree of darkness came on, Huck"
"5139"	"was to come and “maow,” whereupon he would slip out and try the keys."
"5140"	"But the night remained clear, and Huck closed his watch and retired to"
"5141"	"bed in an empty sugar hogshead about twelve."
"5142"	"Tuesday the boys had the same ill luck. Also Wednesday. But Thursday"
"5143"	"night promised better. Tom slipped out in good season with his aunt’s"
"5144"	"old tin lantern, and a large towel to blindfold it with. He hid the"
"5145"	"lantern in Huck’s sugar hogshead and the watch began. An hour before"
"5146"	"midnight the tavern closed up and its lights (the only ones thereabouts)"
"5147"	"were put out. No Spaniard had been seen. Nobody had entered or left the"
"5148"	"alley. Everything was auspicious. The blackness of darkness reigned,"
"5149"	"the perfect stillness was interrupted only by occasional mutterings of"
"5150"	"distant thunder."
"5151"	"Tom got his lantern, lit it in the hogshead, wrapped it closely in the"
"5152"	"towel, and the two adventurers crept in the gloom toward the tavern."
"5153"	"Huck stood sentry and Tom felt his way into the alley. Then there was"
"5154"	"a season of waiting anxiety that weighed upon Huck’s spirits like a"
"5155"	"mountain. He began to wish he could see a flash from the lantern--it"
"5156"	"would frighten him, but it would at least tell him that Tom was alive"
"5157"	"yet. It seemed hours since Tom had disappeared. Surely he must have"
"5158"	"fainted; maybe he was dead; maybe his heart had burst under terror and"
"5159"	"excitement. In his uneasiness Huck found himself drawing closer"
"5160"	"and closer to the alley; fearing all sorts of dreadful things, and"
"5161"	"momentarily expecting some catastrophe to happen that would take away"
"5162"	"his breath. There was not much to take away, for he seemed only able to"
"5163"	"inhale it by thimblefuls, and his heart would soon wear itself out, the"
"5164"	"way it was beating. Suddenly there was a flash of light and Tom came"
"5165"	"tearing by him: “Run!” said he; “run, for your life!”"
"5166"	"He needn’t have repeated it; once was enough; Huck was making thirty or"
"5167"	"forty miles an hour before the repetition was uttered. The boys never"
"5168"	"stopped till they reached the shed of a deserted slaughter-house at the"
"5169"	"lower end of the village. Just as they got within its shelter the storm"
"5170"	"burst and the rain poured down. As soon as Tom got his breath he said:"
"5171"	"“Huck, it was awful! I tried two of the keys, just as soft as I could;"
"5172"	"but they seemed to make such a power of racket that I couldn’t hardly"
"5173"	"get my breath I was so scared. They wouldn’t turn in the lock, either."
"5174"	"Well, without noticing what I was doing, I took hold of the knob, and"
"5175"	"open comes the door! It warn’t locked! I hopped in, and shook off the"
"5176"	"towel, and, _Great Caesar’s Ghost!_”"
"5177"	"“What!--what’d you see, Tom?”"
"5178"	"“Huck, I most stepped onto Injun Joe’s hand!”"
"5179"	"“No!”"
"5180"	"“Yes! He was lying there, sound asleep on the floor, with his old patch"
"5181"	"on his eye and his arms spread out.”"
"5182"	"“Lordy, what did you do? Did he wake up?”"
"5183"	"“No, never budged. Drunk, I reckon. I just grabbed that towel and"
"5184"	"started!”"
"5185"	"“I’d never ‘a’ thought of the towel, I bet!”"
"5186"	"“Well, I would. My aunt would make me mighty sick if I lost it.”"
"5187"	"“Say, Tom, did you see that box?”"
"5188"	"“Huck, I didn’t wait to look around. I didn’t see the box, I didn’t see"
"5189"	"the cross. I didn’t see anything but a bottle and a tin cup on the floor"
"5190"	"by Injun Joe; yes, I saw two barrels and lots more bottles in the room."
"5191"	"Don’t you see, now, what’s the matter with that ha’nted room?”"
"5192"	"“How?”"
"5193"	"“Why, it’s ha’nted with whiskey! Maybe _all_ the Temperance Taverns have"
"5194"	"got a ha’nted room, hey, Huck?”"
"5195"	"“Well, I reckon maybe that’s so. Who’d ‘a’ thought such a thing? But"
"5196"	"say, Tom, now’s a mighty good time to get that box, if Injun Joe’s"
"5197"	"drunk.”"
"5198"	"“It is, that! You try it!”"
"5199"	"Huck shuddered."
"5200"	"“Well, no--I reckon not.”"
"5201"	"“And I reckon not, Huck. Only one bottle alongside of Injun Joe ain’t"
"5202"	"enough. If there’d been three, he’d be drunk enough and I’d do it.”"
"5203"	"There was a long pause for reflection, and then Tom said:"
"5204"	"“Lookyhere, Huck, less not try that thing any more till we know Injun"
"5205"	"Joe’s not in there. It’s too scary. Now, if we watch every night, we’ll"
"5206"	"be dead sure to see him go out, some time or other, and then we’ll"
"5207"	"snatch that box quicker’n lightning.”"
"5208"	"“Well, I’m agreed. I’ll watch the whole night long, and I’ll do it every"
"5209"	"night, too, if you’ll do the other part of the job.”"
"5210"	"“All right, I will. All you got to do is to trot up Hooper Street a"
"5211"	"block and maow--and if I’m asleep, you throw some gravel at the window"
"5212"	"and that’ll fetch me.”"
"5213"	"“Agreed, and good as wheat!”"
"5214"	"“Now, Huck, the storm’s over, and I’ll go home. It’ll begin to be"
"5215"	"daylight in a couple of hours. You go back and watch that long, will"
"5216"	"you?”"
"5217"	"“I said I would, Tom, and I will. I’ll ha’nt that tavern every night for"
"5218"	"a year! I’ll sleep all day and I’ll stand watch all night.”"
"5219"	"“That’s all right. Now, where you going to sleep?”"
"5220"	"“In Ben Rogers’ hayloft. He lets me, and so does his pap’s nigger man,"
"5221"	"Uncle Jake. I tote water for Uncle Jake whenever he wants me to, and any"
"5222"	"time I ask him he gives me a little something to eat if he can spare it."
"5223"	"That’s a mighty good nigger, Tom. He likes me, becuz I don’t ever act as"
"5224"	"if I was above him. Sometime I’ve set right down and eat _with_ him. But"
"5225"	"you needn’t tell that. A body’s got to do things when he’s awful hungry"
"5226"	"he wouldn’t want to do as a steady thing.”"
"5227"	"“Well, if I don’t want you in the daytime, I’ll let you sleep. I won’t"
"5228"	"come bothering around. Any time you see something’s up, in the night,"
"5229"	"just skip right around and maow.”"
"5230"	"CHAPTER XXIX"
"5231"	"THE first thing Tom heard on Friday morning was a glad piece of"
"5232"	"news--Judge Thatcher’s family had come back to town the night before."
"5233"	"Both Injun Joe and the treasure sunk into secondary importance for a"
"5234"	"moment, and Becky took the chief place in the boy’s interest. He saw her"
"5235"	"and they had an exhausting good time playing “hispy” and “gully-keeper”"
"5236"	" with a crowd of their schoolmates. The day was completed and crowned in"
"5237"	"a peculiarly satisfactory way: Becky teased her mother to appoint"
"5238"	"the next day for the long-promised and long-delayed picnic, and she"
"5239"	"consented. The child’s delight was boundless; and Tom’s not more"
"5240"	"moderate. The invitations were sent out before sunset, and straightway"
"5241"	"the young folks of the village were thrown into a fever of preparation"
"5242"	"and pleasurable anticipation. Tom’s excitement enabled him to keep"
"5243"	"awake until a pretty late hour, and he had good hopes of hearing Huck’s"
"5244"	"“maow,” and of having his treasure to astonish Becky and the picnickers"
"5245"	"with, next day; but he was disappointed. No signal came that night."
"5246"	"Morning came, eventually, and by ten or eleven o’clock a giddy and"
"5247"	"rollicking company were gathered at Judge Thatcher’s, and everything was"
"5248"	"ready for a start. It was not the custom for elderly people to mar the"
"5249"	"picnics with their presence. The children were considered safe enough"
"5250"	"under the wings of a few young ladies of eighteen and a few young"
"5251"	"gentlemen of twenty-three or thereabouts. The old steam ferry-boat was"
"5252"	"chartered for the occasion; presently the gay throng filed up the main"
"5253"	"street laden with provision-baskets. Sid was sick and had to miss"
"5254"	"the fun; Mary remained at home to entertain him. The last thing Mrs."
"5255"	"Thatcher said to Becky, was:"
"5256"	"“You’ll not get back till late. Perhaps you’d better stay all night with"
"5257"	"some of the girls that live near the ferry-landing, child.”"
"5258"	"“Then I’ll stay with Susy Harper, mamma.”"
"5259"	"“Very well. And mind and behave yourself and don’t be any trouble.”"
"5260"	"Presently, as they tripped along, Tom said to Becky:"
"5261"	"“Say--I’ll tell you what we’ll do. ‘Stead of going to Joe Harper’s we’ll"
"5262"	"climb right up the hill and stop at the Widow Douglas’. She’ll have"
"5263"	"ice-cream! She has it most every day--dead loads of it. And she’ll be"
"5264"	"awful glad to have us.”"
"5265"	"“Oh, that will be fun!”"
"5266"	"Then Becky reflected a moment and said:"
"5267"	"“But what will mamma say?”"
"5268"	"“How’ll she ever know?”"
"5269"	"The girl turned the idea over in her mind, and said reluctantly:"
"5270"	"“I reckon it’s wrong--but--”"
"5271"	"“But shucks! Your mother won’t know, and so what’s the harm? All she"
"5272"	"wants is that you’ll be safe; and I bet you she’d ‘a’ said go there if"
"5273"	"she’d ‘a’ thought of it. I know she would!”"
"5274"	"The Widow Douglas’ splendid hospitality was a tempting bait. It and"
"5275"	"Tom’s persuasions presently carried the day. So it was decided to say"
"5276"	"nothing to anybody about the night’s programme. Presently it occurred to"
"5277"	"Tom that maybe Huck might come this very night and give the signal. The"
"5278"	"thought took a deal of the spirit out of his anticipations. Still he"
"5279"	"could not bear to give up the fun at Widow Douglas’. And why should he"
"5280"	"give it up, he reasoned--the signal did not come the night before, so"
"5281"	"why should it be any more likely to come tonight? The sure fun of the"
"5282"	"evening outweighed the uncertain treasure; and, boy-like, he determined"
"5283"	"to yield to the stronger inclination and not allow himself to think of"
"5284"	"the box of money another time that day."
"5285"	"Three miles below town the ferryboat stopped at the mouth of a woody"
"5286"	"hollow and tied up. The crowd swarmed ashore and soon the forest"
"5287"	"distances and craggy heights echoed far and near with shoutings and"
"5288"	"laughter. All the different ways of getting hot and tired were gone"
"5289"	"through with, and by-and-by the rovers straggled back to camp fortified"
"5290"	"with responsible appetites, and then the destruction of the good things"
"5291"	"began. After the feast there was a refreshing season of rest and chat in"
"5292"	"the shade of spreading oaks. By-and-by somebody shouted:"
"5293"	"“Who’s ready for the cave?”"
"5294"	"Everybody was. Bundles of candles were procured, and straightway there"
"5295"	"was a general scamper up the hill. The mouth of the cave was up the"
"5296"	"hillside--an opening shaped like a letter A. Its massive oaken door stood"
"5297"	"unbarred. Within was a small chamber, chilly as an icehouse, and walled"
"5298"	"by Nature with solid limestone that was dewy with a cold sweat. It was"
"5299"	"romantic and mysterious to stand here in the deep gloom and look out"
"5300"	"upon the green valley shining in the sun. But the impressiveness of the"
"5301"	"situation quickly wore off, and the romping began again. The moment"
"5302"	"a candle was lighted there was a general rush upon the owner of it; a"
"5303"	"struggle and a gallant defence followed, but the candle was soon knocked"
"5304"	"down or blown out, and then there was a glad clamor of laughter and a"
"5305"	"new chase. But all things have an end. By-and-by the procession went"
"5306"	"filing down the steep descent of the main avenue, the flickering rank of"
"5307"	"lights dimly revealing the lofty walls of rock almost to their point of"
"5308"	"junction sixty feet overhead. This main avenue was not more than"
"5309"	"eight or ten feet wide. Every few steps other lofty and still narrower"
"5310"	"crevices branched from it on either hand--for McDougal’s cave was but a"
"5311"	"vast labyrinth of crooked aisles that ran into each other and out again"
"5312"	"and led nowhere. It was said that one might wander days and nights"
"5313"	"together through its intricate tangle of rifts and chasms, and never"
"5314"	"find the end of the cave; and that he might go down, and down, and"
"5315"	"still down, into the earth, and it was just the same--labyrinth under"
"5316"	"labyrinth, and no end to any of them. No man “knew” the cave. That was"
"5317"	"an impossible thing. Most of the young men knew a portion of it, and it"
"5318"	"was not customary to venture much beyond this known portion. Tom Sawyer"
"5319"	"knew as much of the cave as any one."
"5320"	"The procession moved along the main avenue some three-quarters of"
"5321"	"a mile, and then groups and couples began to slip aside into branch"
"5322"	"avenues, fly along the dismal corridors, and take each other by surprise"
"5323"	"at points where the corridors joined again. Parties were able to elude"
"5324"	"each other for the space of half an hour without going beyond the"
"5325"	"“known” ground."
"5326"	"By-and-by, one group after another came straggling back to the mouth"
"5327"	"of the cave, panting, hilarious, smeared from head to foot with tallow"
"5328"	"drippings, daubed with clay, and entirely delighted with the success of"
"5329"	"the day. Then they were astonished to find that they had been taking"
"5330"	"no note of time and that night was about at hand. The clanging bell had"
"5331"	"been calling for half an hour. However, this sort of close to the day’s"
"5332"	"adventures was romantic and therefore satisfactory. When the ferryboat"
"5333"	"with her wild freight pushed into the stream, nobody cared sixpence for"
"5334"	"the wasted time but the captain of the craft."
"5335"	"Huck was already upon his watch when the ferryboat’s lights went"
"5336"	"glinting past the wharf. He heard no noise on board, for the young"
"5337"	"people were as subdued and still as people usually are who are nearly"
"5338"	"tired to death. He wondered what boat it was, and why she did not"
"5339"	"stop at the wharf--and then he dropped her out of his mind and put his"
"5340"	"attention upon his business. The night was growing cloudy and dark. Ten"
"5341"	"o’clock came, and the noise of vehicles ceased, scattered lights began"
"5342"	"to wink out, all straggling foot-passengers disappeared, the village"
"5343"	"betook itself to its slumbers and left the small watcher alone with the"
"5344"	"silence and the ghosts. Eleven o’clock came, and the tavern lights were"
"5345"	"put out; darkness everywhere, now. Huck waited what seemed a weary long"
"5346"	"time, but nothing happened. His faith was weakening. Was there any use?"
"5347"	"Was there really any use? Why not give it up and turn in?"
"5348"	"A noise fell upon his ear. He was all attention in an instant. The alley"
"5349"	"door closed softly. He sprang to the corner of the brick store. The next"
"5350"	"moment two men brushed by him, and one seemed to have something under"
"5351"	"his arm. It must be that box! So they were going to remove the treasure."
"5352"	"Why call Tom now? It would be absurd--the men would get away with the box"
"5353"	"and never be found again. No, he would stick to their wake and follow"
"5354"	"them; he would trust to the darkness for security from discovery. So"
"5355"	"communing with himself, Huck stepped out and glided along behind the"
"5356"	"men, cat-like, with bare feet, allowing them to keep just far enough"
"5357"	"ahead not to be invisible."
"5358"	"They moved up the river street three blocks, then turned to the left up"
"5359"	"a crossstreet. They went straight ahead, then, until they came to the"
"5360"	"path that led up Cardiff Hill; this they took. They passed by the old"
"5361"	"Welshman’s house, halfway up the hill, without hesitating, and still"
"5362"	"climbed upward. Good, thought Huck, they will bury it in the old quarry."
"5363"	"But they never stopped at the quarry. They passed on, up the summit."
"5364"	"They plunged into the narrow path between the tall sumach bushes, and"
"5365"	"were at once hidden in the gloom. Huck closed up and shortened his"
"5366"	"distance, now, for they would never be able to see him. He trotted along"
"5367"	"awhile; then slackened his pace, fearing he was gaining too fast; moved"
"5368"	"on a piece, then stopped altogether; listened; no sound; none, save that"
"5369"	"he seemed to hear the beating of his own heart. The hooting of an"
"5370"	"owl came over the hill--ominous sound! But no footsteps. Heavens, was"
"5371"	"everything lost! He was about to spring with winged feet, when a man"
"5372"	"cleared his throat not four feet from him! Huck’s heart shot into his"
"5373"	"throat, but he swallowed it again; and then he stood there shaking as"
"5374"	"if a dozen agues had taken charge of him at once, and so weak that he"
"5375"	"thought he must surely fall to the ground. He knew where he was. He"
"5376"	"knew he was within five steps of the stile leading into Widow Douglas’"
"5377"	"grounds. Very well, he thought, let them bury it there; it won’t be hard"
"5378"	"to find."
"5379"	"Now there was a voice--a very low voice--Injun Joe’s:"
"5380"	"“Damn her, maybe she’s got company--there’s lights, late as it is.”"
"5381"	"“I can’t see any.”"
"5382"	"This was that stranger’s voice--the stranger of the haunted house. A"
"5383"	"deadly chill went to Huck’s heart--this, then, was the “revenge” job! His"
"5384"	"thought was, to fly. Then he remembered that the Widow Douglas had been"
"5385"	"kind to him more than once, and maybe these men were going to murder"
"5386"	"her. He wished he dared venture to warn her; but he knew he didn’t"
"5387"	"dare--they might come and catch him. He thought all this and more in"
"5388"	"the moment that elapsed between the stranger’s remark and Injun Joe’s"
"5389"	"next--which was--"
"5390"	"“Because the bush is in your way. Now--this way--now you see, don’t you?”"
"5391"	"“Yes. Well, there _is_ company there, I reckon. Better give it up.”"
"5392"	"“Give it up, and I just leaving this country forever! Give it up and"
"5393"	"maybe never have another chance. I tell you again, as I’ve told you"
"5394"	"before, I don’t care for her swag--you may have it. But her husband was"
"5395"	"rough on me--many times he was rough on me--and mainly he was the justice"
"5396"	"of the peace that jugged me for a vagrant. And that ain’t all. It ain’t"
"5397"	"a millionth part of it! He had me _horsewhipped_!--horsewhipped in"
"5398"	"front of the jail, like a nigger!--with all the town looking on!"
"5399"	"_Horsewhipped_!--do you understand? He took advantage of me and died. But"
"5400"	"I’ll take it out of _her_.”"
"5401"	"“Oh, don’t kill her! Don’t do that!”"
"5402"	"“Kill? Who said anything about killing? I would kill _him_ if he was"
"5403"	"here; but not her. When you want to get revenge on a woman you don’t"
"5404"	"kill her--bosh! you go for her looks. You slit her nostrils--you notch her"
"5405"	"ears like a sow!”"
"5406"	"“By God, that’s--”"
"5407"	"“Keep your opinion to yourself! It will be safest for you. I’ll tie her"
"5408"	"to the bed. If she bleeds to death, is that my fault? I’ll not cry, if"
"5409"	"she does. My friend, you’ll help me in this thing--for _my_ sake--that’s"
"5410"	"why you’re here--I mightn’t be able alone. If you flinch, I’ll kill you."
"5411"	"Do you understand that? And if I have to kill you, I’ll kill her--and"
"5412"	"then I reckon nobody’ll ever know much about who done this business.”"
"5413"	"“Well, if it’s got to be done, let’s get at it. The quicker the"
"5414"	"better--I’m all in a shiver.”"
"5415"	"“Do it _now_? And company there? Look here--I’ll get suspicious of you,"
"5416"	"first thing you know. No--we’ll wait till the lights are out--there’s no"
"5417"	"hurry.”"
"5418"	"Huck felt that a silence was going to ensue--a thing still more awful"
"5419"	"than any amount of murderous talk; so he held his breath and stepped"
"5420"	"gingerly back; planted his foot carefully and firmly, after balancing,"
"5421"	"one-legged, in a precarious way and almost toppling over, first on one"
"5422"	"side and then on the other. He took another step back, with the same"
"5423"	"elaboration and the same risks; then another and another, and--a twig"
"5424"	"snapped under his foot! His breath stopped and he listened. There was no"
"5425"	"sound--the stillness was perfect. His gratitude was measureless. Now he"
"5426"	"turned in his tracks, between the walls of sumach bushes--turned"
"5427"	"himself as carefully as if he were a ship--and then stepped quickly but"
"5428"	"cautiously along. When he emerged at the quarry he felt secure, and"
"5429"	"so he picked up his nimble heels and flew. Down, down he sped, till he"
"5430"	"reached the Welshman’s. He banged at the door, and presently the heads"
"5431"	"of the old man and his two stalwart sons were thrust from windows."
"5432"	"“What’s the row there? Who’s banging? What do you want?”"
"5433"	"“Let me in--quick! I’ll tell everything.”"
"5434"	"“Why, who are you?”"
"5435"	"“Huckleberry Finn--quick, let me in!”"
"5436"	"“Huckleberry Finn, indeed! It ain’t a name to open many doors, I judge!"
"5437"	"But let him in, lads, and let’s see what’s the trouble.”"
"5438"	"“Please don’t ever tell I told you,” were Huck’s first words when he got"
"5439"	"in. “Please don’t--I’d be killed, sure--but the widow’s been good friends"
"5440"	"to me sometimes, and I want to tell--I _will_ tell if you’ll promise you"
"5441"	"won’t ever say it was me.”"
"5442"	"“By George, he _has_ got something to tell, or he wouldn’t act so!”"
"5443"	" exclaimed the old man; “out with it and nobody here’ll ever tell, lad.”"
"5444"	"Three minutes later the old man and his sons, well armed, were up the"
"5445"	"hill, and just entering the sumach path on tiptoe, their weapons in"
"5446"	"their hands. Huck accompanied them no further. He hid behind a great"
"5447"	"bowlder and fell to listening. There was a lagging, anxious silence, and"
"5448"	"then all of a sudden there was an explosion of firearms and a cry."
"5449"	"Huck waited for no particulars. He sprang away and sped down the hill as"
"5450"	"fast as his legs could carry him."
"5451"	"CHAPTER XXX"
"5452"	"AS the earliest suspicion of dawn appeared on Sunday morning, Huck came"
"5453"	"groping up the hill and rapped gently at the old Welshman’s door. The"
"5454"	"inmates were asleep, but it was a sleep that was set on a hair-trigger,"
"5455"	"on account of the exciting episode of the night. A call came from a"
"5456"	"window:"
"5457"	"“Who’s there!”"
"5458"	"Huck’s scared voice answered in a low tone:"
"5459"	"“Please let me in! It’s only Huck Finn!”"
"5460"	"“It’s a name that can open this door night or day, lad!--and welcome!”"
"5461"	"These were strange words to the vagabond boy’s ears, and the pleasantest"
"5462"	"he had ever heard. He could not recollect that the closing word had ever"
"5463"	"been applied in his case before. The door was quickly unlocked, and he"
"5464"	"entered. Huck was given a seat and the old man and his brace of tall"
"5465"	"sons speedily dressed themselves."
"5466"	"“Now, my boy, I hope you’re good and hungry, because breakfast will be"
"5467"	"ready as soon as the sun’s up, and we’ll have a piping hot one, too--make"
"5468"	"yourself easy about that! I and the boys hoped you’d turn up and stop"
"5469"	"here last night.”"
"5470"	"“I was awful scared,” said Huck, “and I run. I took out when the pistols"
"5471"	"went off, and I didn’t stop for three mile. I’ve come now becuz I wanted"
"5472"	"to know about it, you know; and I come before daylight becuz I didn’t"
"5473"	"want to run across them devils, even if they was dead.”"
"5474"	"“Well, poor chap, you do look as if you’d had a hard night of it--but"
"5475"	"there’s a bed here for you when you’ve had your breakfast. No, they"
"5476"	"ain’t dead, lad--we are sorry enough for that. You see we knew right"
"5477"	"where to put our hands on them, by your description; so we crept along"
"5478"	"on tiptoe till we got within fifteen feet of them--dark as a cellar that"
"5479"	"sumach path was--and just then I found I was going to sneeze. It was the"
"5480"	"meanest kind of luck! I tried to keep it back, but no use--‘twas bound to"
"5481"	"come, and it did come! I was in the lead with my pistol raised, and when"
"5482"	"the sneeze started those scoundrels a-rustling to get out of the path,"
"5483"	"I sung out, ‘Fire boys!’ and blazed away at the place where the rustling"
"5484"	"was. So did the boys. But they were off in a jiffy, those villains, and"
"5485"	"we after them, down through the woods. I judge we never touched them."
"5486"	"They fired a shot apiece as they started, but their bullets whizzed by"
"5487"	"and didn’t do us any harm. As soon as we lost the sound of their feet"
"5488"	"we quit chasing, and went down and stirred up the constables. They got a"
"5489"	"posse together, and went off to guard the river bank, and as soon as it"
"5490"	"is light the sheriff and a gang are going to beat up the woods. My boys"
"5491"	"will be with them presently. I wish we had some sort of description of"
"5492"	"those rascals--‘twould help a good deal. But you couldn’t see what they"
"5493"	"were like, in the dark, lad, I suppose?”"
"5494"	"“Oh yes; I saw them downtown and follered them.”"
"5495"	"“Splendid! Describe them--describe them, my boy!”"
"5496"	"“One’s the old deaf and dumb Spaniard that’s ben around here once or"
"5497"	"twice, and t’other’s a mean-looking, ragged--”"
"5498"	"“That’s enough, lad, we know the men! Happened on them in the woods back"
"5499"	"of the widow’s one day, and they slunk away. Off with you, boys, and"
"5500"	"tell the sheriff--get your breakfast tomorrow morning!”"
"5501"	"The Welshman’s sons departed at once. As they were leaving the room Huck"
"5502"	"sprang up and exclaimed:"
"5503"	"“Oh, please don’t tell _any_body it was me that blowed on them! Oh,"
"5504"	"please!”"
"5505"	"“All right if you say it, Huck, but you ought to have the credit of what"
"5506"	"you did.”"
"5507"	"“Oh no, no! Please don’t tell!”"
"5508"	"When the young men were gone, the old Welshman said:"
"5509"	"“They won’t tell--and I won’t. But why don’t you want it known?”"
"5510"	"Huck would not explain, further than to say that he already knew too"
"5511"	"much about one of those men and would not have the man know that he knew"
"5512"	"anything against him for the whole world--he would be killed for knowing"
"5513"	"it, sure."
"5514"	"The old man promised secrecy once more, and said:"
"5515"	"“How did you come to follow these fellows, lad? Were they looking"
"5516"	"suspicious?”"
"5517"	"Huck was silent while he framed a duly cautious reply. Then he said:"
"5518"	"“Well, you see, I’m a kind of a hard lot,--least everybody says so, and"
"5519"	"I don’t see nothing agin it--and sometimes I can’t sleep much, on account"
"5520"	"of thinking about it and sort of trying to strike out a new way of"
"5521"	"doing. That was the way of it last night. I couldn’t sleep, and so I"
"5522"	"come along upstreet ‘bout midnight, a-turning it all over, and when I"
"5523"	"got to that old shackly brick store by the Temperance Tavern, I backed"
"5524"	"up agin the wall to have another think. Well, just then along comes"
"5525"	"these two chaps slipping along close by me, with something under their"
"5526"	"arm, and I reckoned they’d stole it. One was a-smoking, and t’other one"
"5527"	"wanted a light; so they stopped right before me and the cigars lit up"
"5528"	"their faces and I see that the big one was the deaf and dumb Spaniard,"
"5529"	"by his white whiskers and the patch on his eye, and t’other one was a"
"5530"	"rusty, ragged-looking devil.”"
"5531"	"“Could you see the rags by the light of the cigars?”"
"5532"	"This staggered Huck for a moment. Then he said:"
"5533"	"“Well, I don’t know--but somehow it seems as if I did.”"
"5534"	"“Then they went on, and you--”"
"5535"	"“Follered ‘em--yes. That was it. I wanted to see what was up--they sneaked"
"5536"	"along so. I dogged ‘em to the widder’s stile, and stood in the dark and"
"5537"	"heard the ragged one beg for the widder, and the Spaniard swear he’d"
"5538"	"spile her looks just as I told you and your two--”"
"5539"	"“What! The _deaf and dumb_ man said all that!”"
"5540"	"Huck had made another terrible mistake! He was trying his best to keep"
"5541"	"the old man from getting the faintest hint of who the Spaniard might be,"
"5542"	"and yet his tongue seemed determined to get him into trouble in spite of"
"5543"	"all he could do. He made several efforts to creep out of his scrape,"
"5544"	"but the old man’s eye was upon him and he made blunder after blunder."
"5545"	"Presently the Welshman said:"
"5546"	"“My boy, don’t be afraid of me. I wouldn’t hurt a hair of your head for"
"5547"	"all the world. No--I’d protect you--I’d protect you. This Spaniard is"
"5548"	"not deaf and dumb; you’ve let that slip without intending it; you can’t"
"5549"	"cover that up now. You know something about that Spaniard that you want"
"5550"	"to keep dark. Now trust me--tell me what it is, and trust me--I won’t"
"5551"	"betray you.”"
"5552"	"Huck looked into the old man’s honest eyes a moment, then bent over and"
"5553"	"whispered in his ear:"
"5554"	"“‘Tain’t a Spaniard--it’s Injun Joe!”"
"5555"	"The Welshman almost jumped out of his chair. In a moment he said:"
"5556"	"“It’s all plain enough, now. When you talked about notching ears and"
"5557"	"slitting noses I judged that that was your own embellishment, because"
"5558"	"white men don’t take that sort of revenge. But an Injun! That’s a"
"5559"	"different matter altogether.”"
"5560"	"During breakfast the talk went on, and in the course of it the old man"
"5561"	"said that the last thing which he and his sons had done, before going"
"5562"	"to bed, was to get a lantern and examine the stile and its vicinity for"
"5563"	"marks of blood. They found none, but captured a bulky bundle of--"
"5564"	"“Of _what_?”"
"5565"	"If the words had been lightning they could not have leaped with a more"
"5566"	"stunning suddenness from Huck’s blanched lips. His eyes were staring"
"5567"	"wide, now, and his breath suspended--waiting for the answer. The Welshman"
"5568"	"started--stared in return--three seconds--five seconds--ten--then replied:"
"5569"	"“Of burglar’s tools. Why, what’s the _matter_ with you?”"
"5570"	"Huck sank back, panting gently, but deeply, unutterably grateful. The"
"5571"	"Welshman eyed him gravely, curiously--and presently said:"
"5572"	"“Yes, burglar’s tools. That appears to relieve you a good deal. But what"
"5573"	"did give you that turn? What were _you_ expecting we’d found?”"
"5574"	"Huck was in a close place--the inquiring eye was upon him--he would have"
"5575"	"given anything for material for a plausible answer--nothing suggested"
"5576"	"itself--the inquiring eye was boring deeper and deeper--a senseless"
"5577"	"reply offered--there was no time to weigh it, so at a venture he uttered"
"5578"	"it--feebly:"
"5579"	"“Sunday-school books, maybe.”"
"5580"	"Poor Huck was too distressed to smile, but the old man laughed loud and"
"5581"	"joyously, shook up the details of his anatomy from head to foot, and"
"5582"	"ended by saying that such a laugh was money in a-man’s pocket, because"
"5583"	"it cut down the doctor’s bill like everything. Then he added:"
"5584"	"“Poor old chap, you’re white and jaded--you ain’t well a bit--no wonder"
"5585"	"you’re a little flighty and off your balance. But you’ll come out of it."
"5586"	"Rest and sleep will fetch you out all right, I hope.”"
"5587"	"Huck was irritated to think he had been such a goose and betrayed such"
"5588"	"a suspicious excitement, for he had dropped the idea that the parcel"
"5589"	"brought from the tavern was the treasure, as soon as he had heard the"
"5590"	"talk at the widow’s stile. He had only thought it was not the treasure,"
"5591"	"however--he had not known that it wasn’t--and so the suggestion of a"
"5592"	"captured bundle was too much for his self-possession. But on the whole"
"5593"	"he felt glad the little episode had happened, for now he knew beyond all"
"5594"	"question that that bundle was not _the_ bundle, and so his mind was"
"5595"	"at rest and exceedingly comfortable. In fact, everything seemed to be"
"5596"	"drifting just in the right direction, now; the treasure must be still"
"5597"	"in No. 2, the men would be captured and jailed that day, and he and"
"5598"	"Tom could seize the gold that night without any trouble or any fear of"
"5599"	"interruption."
"5600"	"Just as breakfast was completed there was a knock at the door. Huck"
"5601"	"jumped for a hiding-place, for he had no mind to be connected even"
"5602"	"remotely with the late event. The Welshman admitted several ladies and"
"5603"	"gentlemen, among them the Widow Douglas, and noticed that groups of"
"5604"	"citizens were climbing up the hill--to stare at the stile. So the news"
"5605"	"had spread. The Welshman had to tell the story of the night to the"
"5606"	"visitors. The widow’s gratitude for her preservation was outspoken."
"5607"	"“Don’t say a word about it, madam. There’s another that you’re more"
"5608"	"beholden to than you are to me and my boys, maybe, but he don’t allow me"
"5609"	"to tell his name. We wouldn’t have been there but for him.”"
"5610"	"Of course this excited a curiosity so vast that it almost belittled the"
"5611"	"main matter--but the Welshman allowed it to eat into the vitals of his"
"5612"	"visitors, and through them be transmitted to the whole town, for he"
"5613"	"refused to part with his secret. When all else had been learned, the"
"5614"	"widow said:"
"5615"	"“I went to sleep reading in bed and slept straight through all that"
"5616"	"noise. Why didn’t you come and wake me?”"
"5617"	"“We judged it warn’t worth while. Those fellows warn’t likely to come"
"5618"	"again--they hadn’t any tools left to work with, and what was the use of"
"5619"	"waking you up and scaring you to death? My three negro men stood guard"
"5620"	"at your house all the rest of the night. They’ve just come back.”"
"5621"	"More visitors came, and the story had to be told and retold for a couple"
"5622"	"of hours more."
"5623"	"There was no Sabbath-school during day-school vacation, but everybody"
"5624"	"was early at church. The stirring event was well canvassed. News came"
"5625"	"that not a sign of the two villains had been yet discovered. When the"
"5626"	"sermon was finished, Judge Thatcher’s wife dropped alongside of Mrs."
"5627"	"Harper as she moved down the aisle with the crowd and said:"
"5628"	"“Is my Becky going to sleep all day? I just expected she would be tired"
"5629"	"to death.”"
"5630"	"“Your Becky?”"
"5631"	"“Yes,” with a startled look--“didn’t she stay with you last night?”"
"5632"	"“Why, no.”"
"5633"	"Mrs. Thatcher turned pale, and sank into a pew, just as Aunt Polly,"
"5634"	"talking briskly with a friend, passed by. Aunt Polly said:"
"5635"	"“Goodmorning, Mrs. Thatcher. Goodmorning, Mrs. Harper. I’ve got a boy"
"5636"	"that’s turned up missing. I reckon my Tom stayed at your house last"
"5637"	"night--one of you. And now he’s afraid to come to church. I’ve got to"
"5638"	"settle with him.”"
"5639"	"Mrs. Thatcher shook her head feebly and turned paler than ever."
"5640"	"“He didn’t stay with us,” said Mrs. Harper, beginning to look uneasy. A"
"5641"	"marked anxiety came into Aunt Polly’s face."
"5642"	"“Joe Harper, have you seen my Tom this morning?”"
"5643"	"“No’m.”"
"5644"	"“When did you see him last?”"
"5645"	"Joe tried to remember, but was not sure he could say. The people had"
"5646"	"stopped moving out of church. Whispers passed along, and a boding"
"5647"	"uneasiness took possession of every countenance. Children were anxiously"
"5648"	"questioned, and young teachers. They all said they had not noticed"
"5649"	"whether Tom and Becky were on board the ferryboat on the homeward trip;"
"5650"	"it was dark; no one thought of inquiring if any one was missing. One"
"5651"	"young man finally blurted out his fear that they were still in the cave!"
"5652"	"Mrs. Thatcher swooned away. Aunt Polly fell to crying and wringing her"
"5653"	"hands."
"5654"	"The alarm swept from lip to lip, from group to group, from street to"
"5655"	"street, and within five minutes the bells were wildly clanging and"
"5656"	"the whole town was up! The Cardiff Hill episode sank into instant"
"5657"	"insignificance, the burglars were forgotten, horses were saddled, skiffs"
"5658"	"were manned, the ferryboat ordered out, and before the horror was half"
"5659"	"an hour old, two hundred men were pouring down highroad and river toward"
"5660"	"the cave."
"5661"	"All the long afternoon the village seemed empty and dead. Many women"
"5662"	"visited Aunt Polly and Mrs. Thatcher and tried to comfort them. They"
"5663"	"cried with them, too, and that was still better than words. All the"
"5664"	"tedious night the town waited for news; but when the morning dawned at"
"5665"	"last, all the word that came was, “Send more candles--and send food.”"
"5666"	" Mrs. Thatcher was almost crazed; and Aunt Polly, also. Judge Thatcher"
"5667"	"sent messages of hope and encouragement from the cave, but they conveyed"
"5668"	"no real cheer."
"5669"	"The old Welshman came home toward daylight, spattered with"
"5670"	"candle-grease, smeared with clay, and almost worn out. He found Huck"
"5671"	"still in the bed that had been provided for him, and delirious with"
"5672"	"fever. The physicians were all at the cave, so the Widow Douglas came"
"5673"	"and took charge of the patient. She said she would do her best by him,"
"5674"	"because, whether he was good, bad, or indifferent, he was the Lord’s,"
"5675"	"and nothing that was the Lord’s was a thing to be neglected. The"
"5676"	"Welshman said Huck had good spots in him, and the widow said:"
"5677"	"“You can depend on it. That’s the Lord’s mark. He don’t leave it off."
"5678"	"He never does. Puts it somewhere on every creature that comes from his"
"5679"	"hands.”"
"5680"	"Early in the forenoon parties of jaded men began to straggle into the"
"5681"	"village, but the strongest of the citizens continued searching. All the"
"5682"	"news that could be gained was that remotenesses of the cavern were being"
"5683"	"ransacked that had never been visited before; that every corner and"
"5684"	"crevice was going to be thoroughly searched; that wherever one wandered"
"5685"	"through the maze of passages, lights were to be seen flitting hither"
"5686"	"and thither in the distance, and shoutings and pistol-shots sent their"
"5687"	"hollow reverberations to the ear down the sombre aisles. In one place,"
"5688"	"far from the section usually traversed by tourists, the names “BECKY &"
"5689"	"TOM” had been found traced upon the rocky wall with candle-smoke, and"
"5690"	"near at hand a grease-soiled bit of ribbon. Mrs. Thatcher recognized the"
"5691"	"ribbon and cried over it. She said it was the last relic she should ever"
"5692"	"have of her child; and that no other memorial of her could ever be so"
"5693"	"precious, because this one parted latest from the living body before the"
"5694"	"awful death came. Some said that now and then, in the cave, a far-away"
"5695"	"speck of light would glimmer, and then a glorious shout would burst"
"5696"	"forth and a score of men go trooping down the echoing aisle--and then a"
"5697"	"sickening disappointment always followed; the children were not there;"
"5698"	"it was only a searcher’s light."
"5699"	"Three dreadful days and nights dragged their tedious hours along, and"
"5700"	"the village sank into a hopeless stupor. No one had heart for anything."
"5701"	"The accidental discovery, just made, that the proprietor of the"
"5702"	"Temperance Tavern kept liquor on his premises, scarcely fluttered the"
"5703"	"public pulse, tremendous as the fact was. In a lucid interval, Huck"
"5704"	"feebly led up to the subject of taverns, and finally asked--dimly"
"5705"	"dreading the worst--if anything had been discovered at the Temperance"
"5706"	"Tavern since he had been ill."
"5707"	"“Yes,” said the widow."
"5708"	"Huck started up in bed, wildeyed:"
"5709"	"“What? What was it?”"
"5710"	"“Liquor!--and the place has been shut up. Lie down, child--what a turn you"
"5711"	"did give me!”"
"5712"	"“Only tell me just one thing--only just one--please! Was it Tom Sawyer"
"5713"	"that found it?”"
"5714"	"The widow burst into tears. “Hush, hush, child, hush! I’ve told you"
"5715"	"before, you must _not_ talk. You are very, very sick!”"
"5716"	"Then nothing but liquor had been found; there would have been a great"
"5717"	"powwow if it had been the gold. So the treasure was gone forever--gone"
"5718"	"forever! But what could she be crying about? Curious that she should"
"5719"	"cry."
"5720"	"These thoughts worked their dim way through Huck’s mind, and under the"
"5721"	"weariness they gave him he fell asleep. The widow said to herself:"
"5722"	"“There--he’s asleep, poor wreck. Tom Sawyer find it! Pity but somebody"
"5723"	"could find Tom Sawyer! Ah, there ain’t many left, now, that’s got hope"
"5724"	"enough, or strength enough, either, to go on searching.”"
"5725"	"CHAPTER XXXI"
"5726"	"NOW to return to Tom and Becky’s share in the picnic. They tripped along"
"5727"	"the murky aisles with the rest of the company, visiting the familiar"
"5728"	"wonders of the cave--wonders dubbed with rather over-descriptive names,"
"5729"	"such as “The Drawing-Room,” “The Cathedral,” “Aladdin’s Palace,” and"
"5730"	"so on. Presently the hide-and-seek frolicking began, and Tom and Becky"
"5731"	"engaged in it with zeal until the exertion began to grow a trifle"
"5732"	"wearisome; then they wandered down a sinuous avenue holding their"
"5733"	"candles aloft and reading the tangled webwork of names, dates,"
"5734"	"postoffice addresses, and mottoes with which the rocky walls had been"
"5735"	"frescoed (in candle-smoke). Still drifting along and talking, they"
"5736"	"scarcely noticed that they were now in a part of the cave whose walls"
"5737"	"were not frescoed. They smoked their own names under an overhanging"
"5738"	"shelf and moved on. Presently they came to a place where a little stream"
"5739"	"of water, trickling over a ledge and carrying a limestone sediment with"
"5740"	"it, had, in the slow-dragging ages, formed a laced and ruffled Niagara"
"5741"	"in gleaming and imperishable stone. Tom squeezed his small body behind"
"5742"	"it in order to illuminate it for Becky’s gratification. He found that"
"5743"	"it curtained a sort of steep natural stairway which was enclosed between"
"5744"	"narrow walls, and at once the ambition to be a discoverer seized him."
"5745"	"Becky responded to his call, and they made a smoke-mark for future"
"5746"	"guidance, and started upon their quest. They wound this way and that,"
"5747"	"far down into the secret depths of the cave, made another mark, and"
"5748"	"branched off in search of novelties to tell the upper world about. In"
"5749"	"one place they found a spacious cavern, from whose ceiling depended a"
"5750"	"multitude of shining stalactites of the length and circumference of"
"5751"	"a man’s leg; they walked all about it, wondering and admiring, and"
"5752"	"presently left it by one of the numerous passages that opened into"
"5753"	"it. This shortly brought them to a bewitching spring, whose basin was"
"5754"	"incrusted with a frostwork of glittering crystals; it was in the midst"
"5755"	"of a cavern whose walls were supported by many fantastic pillars which"
"5756"	"had been formed by the joining of great stalactites and stalagmites"
"5757"	"together, the result of the ceaseless water-drip of centuries. Under the"
"5758"	"roof vast knots of bats had packed themselves together, thousands in a"
"5759"	"bunch; the lights disturbed the creatures and they came flocking down by"
"5760"	"hundreds, squeaking and darting furiously at the candles. Tom knew their"
"5761"	"ways and the danger of this sort of conduct. He seized Becky’s hand and"
"5762"	"hurried her into the first corridor that offered; and none too soon, for"
"5763"	"a bat struck Becky’s light out with its wing while she was passing out"
"5764"	"of the cavern. The bats chased the children a good distance; but the"
"5765"	"fugitives plunged into every new passage that offered, and at last got"
"5766"	"rid of the perilous things. Tom found a subterranean lake, shortly,"
"5767"	"which stretched its dim length away until its shape was lost in the"
"5768"	"shadows. He wanted to explore its borders, but concluded that it would"
"5769"	"be best to sit down and rest awhile, first. Now, for the first time, the"
"5770"	"deep stillness of the place laid a clammy hand upon the spirits of the"
"5771"	"children. Becky said:"
"5772"	"“Why, I didn’t notice, but it seems ever so long since I heard any of"
"5773"	"the others.”"
"5774"	"“Come to think, Becky, we are away down below them--and I don’t know how"
"5775"	"far away north, or south, or east, or whichever it is. We couldn’t hear"
"5776"	"them here.”"
"5777"	"Becky grew apprehensive."
"5778"	"“I wonder how long we’ve been down here, Tom? We better start back.”"
"5779"	"“Yes, I reckon we better. P’raps we better.”"
"5780"	"“Can you find the way, Tom? It’s all a mixed-up crookedness to me.”"
"5781"	"“I reckon I could find it--but then the bats. If they put our candles"
"5782"	"out it will be an awful fix. Let’s try some other way, so as not to go"
"5783"	"through there.”"
"5784"	"“Well. But I hope we won’t get lost. It would be so awful!” and the girl"
"5785"	"shuddered at the thought of the dreadful possibilities."
"5786"	"They started through a corridor, and traversed it in silence a long"
"5787"	"way, glancing at each new opening, to see if there was anything familiar"
"5788"	"about the look of it; but they were all strange. Every time Tom made an"
"5789"	"examination, Becky would watch his face for an encouraging sign, and he"
"5790"	"would say cheerily:"
"5791"	"“Oh, it’s all right. This ain’t the one, but we’ll come to it right"
"5792"	"away!”"
"5793"	"But he felt less and less hopeful with each failure, and presently began"
"5794"	"to turn off into diverging avenues at sheer random, in desperate hope of"
"5795"	"finding the one that was wanted. He still said it was “all right,” but"
"5796"	"there was such a leaden dread at his heart that the words had lost their"
"5797"	"ring and sounded just as if he had said, “All is lost!” Becky clung to"
"5798"	"his side in an anguish of fear, and tried hard to keep back the tears,"
"5799"	"but they would come. At last she said:"
"5800"	"“Oh, Tom, never mind the bats, let’s go back that way! We seem to get"
"5801"	"worse and worse off all the time.”"
"5802"	"“Listen!” said he."
"5803"	"Profound silence; silence so deep that even their breathings were"
"5804"	"conspicuous in the hush. Tom shouted. The call went echoing down"
"5805"	"the empty aisles and died out in the distance in a faint sound that"
"5806"	"resembled a ripple of mocking laughter."
"5807"	"“Oh, don’t do it again, Tom, it is too horrid,” said Becky."
"5808"	"“It is horrid, but I better, Becky; they might hear us, you know,” and"
"5809"	"he shouted again."
"5810"	"The “might” was even a chillier horror than the ghostly laughter, it so"
"5811"	"confessed a perishing hope. The children stood still and listened; but"
"5812"	"there was no result. Tom turned upon the back track at once, and hurried"
"5813"	"his steps. It was but a little while before a certain indecision in his"
"5814"	"manner revealed another fearful fact to Becky--he could not find his way"
"5815"	"back!"
"5816"	"“Oh, Tom, you didn’t make any marks!”"
"5817"	"“Becky, I was such a fool! Such a fool! I never thought we might want to"
"5818"	"come back! No--I can’t find the way. It’s all mixed up.”"
"5819"	"“Tom, Tom, we’re lost! we’re lost! We never can get out of this awful"
"5820"	"place! Oh, why _did_ we ever leave the others!”"
"5821"	"She sank to the ground and burst into such a frenzy of crying that Tom"
"5822"	"was appalled with the idea that she might die, or lose her reason. He"
"5823"	"sat down by her and put his arms around her; she buried her face in"
"5824"	"his bosom, she clung to him, she poured out her terrors, her unavailing"
"5825"	"regrets, and the far echoes turned them all to jeering laughter. Tom"
"5826"	"begged her to pluck up hope again, and she said she could not. He fell"
"5827"	"to blaming and abusing himself for getting her into this miserable"
"5828"	"situation; this had a better effect. She said she would try to hope"
"5829"	"again, she would get up and follow wherever he might lead if only he"
"5830"	"would not talk like that any more. For he was no more to blame than she,"
"5831"	"she said."
"5832"	"So they moved on again--aimlessly--simply at random--all they could do"
"5833"	"was to move, keep moving. For a little while, hope made a show of"
"5834"	"reviving--not with any reason to back it, but only because it is its"
"5835"	"nature to revive when the spring has not been taken out of it by age and"
"5836"	"familiarity with failure."
"5837"	"By-and-by Tom took Becky’s candle and blew it out. This economy meant so"
"5838"	"much! Words were not needed. Becky understood, and her hope died again."
"5839"	"She knew that Tom had a whole candle and three or four pieces in his"
"5840"	"pockets--yet he must economize."
"5841"	"By-and-by, fatigue began to assert its claims; the children tried to pay"
"5842"	"attention, for it was dreadful to think of sitting down when time was"
"5843"	"grown to be so precious, moving, in some direction, in any direction,"
"5844"	"was at least progress and might bear fruit; but to sit down was to"
"5845"	"invite death and shorten its pursuit."
"5846"	"At last Becky’s frail limbs refused to carry her farther. She sat down."
"5847"	"Tom rested with her, and they talked of home, and the friends there,"
"5848"	"and the comfortable beds and, above all, the light! Becky cried, and Tom"
"5849"	"tried to think of some way of comforting her, but all his encouragements"
"5850"	"were grown thread-bare with use, and sounded like sarcasms. Fatigue bore"
"5851"	"so heavily upon Becky that she drowsed off to sleep. Tom was grateful."
"5852"	"He sat looking into her drawn face and saw it grow smooth and natural"
"5853"	"under the influence of pleasant dreams; and by-and-by a smile dawned and"
"5854"	"rested there. The peaceful face reflected somewhat of peace and healing"
"5855"	"into his own spirit, and his thoughts wandered away to bygone times and"
"5856"	"dreamy memories. While he was deep in his musings, Becky woke up with a"
"5857"	"breezy little laugh--but it was stricken dead upon her lips, and a groan"
"5858"	"followed it."
"5859"	"“Oh, how _could_ I sleep! I wish I never, never had waked! No! No, I"
"5860"	"don’t, Tom! Don’t look so! I won’t say it again.”"
"5861"	"“I’m glad you’ve slept, Becky; you’ll feel rested, now, and we’ll find"
"5862"	"the way out.”"
"5863"	"“We can try, Tom; but I’ve seen such a beautiful country in my dream. I"
"5864"	"reckon we are going there.”"
"5865"	"“Maybe not, maybe not. Cheer up, Becky, and let’s go on trying.”"
"5866"	"They rose up and wandered along, hand in hand and hopeless. They tried"
"5867"	"to estimate how long they had been in the cave, but all they knew was"
"5868"	"that it seemed days and weeks, and yet it was plain that this could not"
"5869"	"be, for their candles were not gone yet. A long time after this--they"
"5870"	"could not tell how long--Tom said they must go softly and listen for"
"5871"	"dripping water--they must find a spring. They found one presently, and"
"5872"	"Tom said it was time to rest again. Both were cruelly tired, yet Becky"
"5873"	"said she thought she could go a little farther. She was surprised to"
"5874"	"hear Tom dissent. She could not understand it. They sat down, and Tom"
"5875"	"fastened his candle to the wall in front of them with some clay. Thought"
"5876"	"was soon busy; nothing was said for some time. Then Becky broke the"
"5877"	"silence:"
"5878"	"“Tom, I am so hungry!”"
"5879"	"Tom took something out of his pocket."
"5880"	"“Do you remember this?” said he."
"5881"	"Becky almost smiled."
"5882"	"“It’s our wedding-cake, Tom.”"
"5883"	"“Yes--I wish it was as big as a barrel, for it’s all we’ve got.”"
"5884"	"“I saved it from the picnic for us to dream on, Tom, the way grownup"
"5885"	"people do with wedding-cake--but it’ll be our--”"
"5886"	"She dropped the sentence where it was. Tom divided the cake and Becky"
"5887"	"ate with good appetite, while Tom nibbled at his moiety. There was"
"5888"	"abundance of cold water to finish the feast with. By-and-by Becky"
"5889"	"suggested that they move on again. Tom was silent a moment. Then he"
"5890"	"said:"
"5891"	"“Becky, can you bear it if I tell you something?”"
"5892"	"Becky’s face paled, but she thought she could."
"5893"	"“Well, then, Becky, we must stay here, where there’s water to drink."
"5894"	"That little piece is our last candle!”"
"5895"	"Becky gave loose to tears and wailings. Tom did what he could to comfort"
"5896"	"her, but with little effect. At length Becky said:"
"5897"	"“Tom!”"
"5898"	"“Well, Becky?”"
"5899"	"“They’ll miss us and hunt for us!”"
"5900"	"“Yes, they will! Certainly they will!”"
"5901"	"“Maybe they’re hunting for us now, Tom.”"
"5902"	"“Why, I reckon maybe they are. I hope they are.”"
"5903"	"“When would they miss us, Tom?”"
"5904"	"“When they get back to the boat, I reckon.”"
"5905"	"“Tom, it might be dark then--would they notice we hadn’t come?”"
"5906"	"“I don’t know. But anyway, your mother would miss you as soon as they"
"5907"	"got home.”"
"5908"	"A frightened look in Becky’s face brought Tom to his senses and he saw"
"5909"	"that he had made a blunder. Becky was not to have gone home that night!"
"5910"	"The children became silent and thoughtful. In a moment a new burst of"
"5911"	"grief from Becky showed Tom that the thing in his mind had struck hers"
"5912"	"also--that the Sabbath morning might be half spent before Mrs. Thatcher"
"5913"	"discovered that Becky was not at Mrs. Harper’s."
"5914"	"The children fastened their eyes upon their bit of candle and watched it"
"5915"	"melt slowly and pitilessly away; saw the half inch of wick stand alone"
"5916"	"at last; saw the feeble flame rise and fall, climb the thin column of"
"5917"	"smoke, linger at its top a moment, and then--the horror of utter darkness"
"5918"	"reigned!"
"5919"	"How long afterward it was that Becky came to a slow consciousness that"
"5920"	"she was crying in Tom’s arms, neither could tell. All that they knew"
"5921"	"was, that after what seemed a mighty stretch of time, both awoke out of"
"5922"	"a dead stupor of sleep and resumed their miseries once more. Tom said"
"5923"	"it might be Sunday, now--maybe Monday. He tried to get Becky to talk, but"
"5924"	"her sorrows were too oppressive, all her hopes were gone. Tom said that"
"5925"	"they must have been missed long ago, and no doubt the search was going"
"5926"	"on. He would shout and maybe some one would come. He tried it; but in"
"5927"	"the darkness the distant echoes sounded so hideously that he tried it no"
"5928"	"more."
"5929"	"The hours wasted away, and hunger came to torment the captives again. A"
"5930"	"portion of Tom’s half of the cake was left; they divided and ate it. But"
"5931"	"they seemed hungrier than before. The poor morsel of food only whetted"
"5932"	"desire."
"5933"	"By-and-by Tom said:"
"5934"	"“SH! Did you hear that?”"
"5935"	"Both held their breath and listened. There was a sound like the"
"5936"	"faintest, far-off shout. Instantly Tom answered it, and leading Becky by"
"5937"	"the hand, started groping down the corridor in its direction. Presently"
"5938"	"he listened again; again the sound was heard, and apparently a little"
"5939"	"nearer."
"5940"	"“It’s them!” said Tom; “they’re coming! Come along, Becky--we’re all"
"5941"	"right now!”"
"5942"	"The joy of the prisoners was almost overwhelming. Their speed was slow,"
"5943"	"however, because pitfalls were somewhat common, and had to be guarded"
"5944"	"against. They shortly came to one and had to stop. It might be three"
"5945"	"feet deep, it might be a hundred--there was no passing it at any rate."
"5946"	"Tom got down on his breast and reached as far down as he could. No"
"5947"	"bottom. They must stay there and wait until the searchers came. They"
"5948"	"listened; evidently the distant shoutings were growing more distant!"
"5949"	"a moment or two more and they had gone altogether. The heart-sinking"
"5950"	"misery of it! Tom whooped until he was hoarse, but it was of no use. He"
"5951"	"talked hopefully to Becky; but an age of anxious waiting passed and no"
"5952"	"sounds came again."
"5953"	"The children groped their way back to the spring. The weary time dragged"
"5954"	"on; they slept again, and awoke famished and woe-stricken. Tom believed"
"5955"	"it must be Tuesday by this time."
"5956"	"Now an idea struck him. There were some side passages near at hand. It"
"5957"	"would be better to explore some of these than bear the weight of the"
"5958"	"heavy time in idleness. He took a kite-line from his pocket, tied it to"
"5959"	"a projection, and he and Becky started, Tom in the lead, unwinding the"
"5960"	"line as he groped along. At the end of twenty steps the corridor ended"
"5961"	"in a “jumping-off place.” Tom got down on his knees and felt below,"
"5962"	"and then as far around the corner as he could reach with his hands"
"5963"	"conveniently; he made an effort to stretch yet a little farther to the"
"5964"	"right, and at that moment, not twenty yards away, a human hand, holding"
"5965"	"a candle, appeared from behind a rock! Tom lifted up a glorious shout,"
"5966"	"and instantly that hand was followed by the body it belonged to--Injun"
"5967"	"Joe’s! Tom was paralyzed; he could not move. He was vastly gratified the"
"5968"	"next moment, to see the “Spaniard” take to his heels and get himself out"
"5969"	"of sight. Tom wondered that Joe had not recognized his voice and come"
"5970"	"over and killed him for testifying in court. But the echoes must have"
"5971"	"disguised the voice. Without doubt, that was it, he reasoned. Tom’s"
"5972"	"fright weakened every muscle in his body. He said to himself that if he"
"5973"	"had strength enough to get back to the spring he would stay there, and"
"5974"	"nothing should tempt him to run the risk of meeting Injun Joe again. He"
"5975"	"was careful to keep from Becky what it was he had seen. He told her he"
"5976"	"had only shouted “for luck.”"
"5977"	"But hunger and wretchedness rise superior to fears in the long run."
"5978"	"Another tedious wait at the spring and another long sleep brought"
"5979"	"changes. The children awoke tortured with a raging hunger. Tom believed"
"5980"	"that it must be Wednesday or Thursday or even Friday or Saturday, now,"
"5981"	"and that the search had been given over. He proposed to explore another"
"5982"	"passage. He felt willing to risk Injun Joe and all other terrors. But"
"5983"	"Becky was very weak. She had sunk into a dreary apathy and would not be"
"5984"	"roused. She said she would wait, now, where she was, and die--it would"
"5985"	"not be long. She told Tom to go with the kite-line and explore if he"
"5986"	"chose; but she implored him to come back every little while and speak"
"5987"	"to her; and she made him promise that when the awful time came, he would"
"5988"	"stay by her and hold her hand until all was over."
"5989"	"Tom kissed her, with a choking sensation in his throat, and made a show"
"5990"	"of being confident of finding the searchers or an escape from the cave;"
"5991"	"then he took the kite-line in his hand and went groping down one of the"
"5992"	"passages on his hands and knees, distressed with hunger and sick with"
"5993"	"bodings of coming doom."
"5994"	"CHAPTER XXXII"
"5995"	"TUESDAY afternoon came, and waned to the twilight. The village of St."
"5996"	"Petersburg still mourned. The lost children had not been found. Public"
"5997"	"prayers had been offered up for them, and many and many a private prayer"
"5998"	"that had the petitioner’s whole heart in it; but still no good news came"
"5999"	"from the cave. The majority of the searchers had given up the quest"
"6000"	"and gone back to their daily avocations, saying that it was plain the"
"6001"	"children could never be found. Mrs. Thatcher was very ill, and a great"
"6002"	"part of the time delirious. People said it was heartbreaking to hear her"
"6003"	"call her child, and raise her head and listen a whole minute at a time,"
"6004"	"then lay it wearily down again with a moan. Aunt Polly had drooped into"
"6005"	"a settled melancholy, and her gray hair had grown almost white. The"
"6006"	"village went to its rest on Tuesday night, sad and forlorn."
"6007"	"Away in the middle of the night a wild peal burst from the village"
"6008"	"bells, and in a moment the streets were swarming with frantic half-clad"
"6009"	"people, who shouted, “Turn out! turn out! they’re found! they’re found!”"
"6010"	" Tin pans and horns were added to the din, the population massed itself"
"6011"	"and moved toward the river, met the children coming in an open carriage"
"6012"	"drawn by shouting citizens, thronged around it, joined its homeward"
"6013"	"march, and swept magnificently up the main street roaring huzzah after"
"6014"	"huzzah!"
"6015"	"The village was illuminated; nobody went to bed again; it was the"
