"6016"	"greatest night the little town had ever seen. During the first half-hour"
"6017"	"a procession of villagers filed through Judge Thatcher’s house, seized"
"6018"	"the saved ones and kissed them, squeezed Mrs. Thatcher’s hand, tried to"
"6019"	"speak but couldn’t--and drifted out raining tears all over the place."
"6020"	"Aunt Polly’s happiness was complete, and Mrs. Thatcher’s nearly so. It"
"6021"	"would be complete, however, as soon as the messenger dispatched with the"
"6022"	"great news to the cave should get the word to her husband. Tom lay upon"
"6023"	"a sofa with an eager auditory about him and told the history of the"
"6024"	"wonderful adventure, putting in many striking additions to adorn it"
"6025"	"withal; and closed with a description of how he left Becky and went"
"6026"	"on an exploring expedition; how he followed two avenues as far as his"
"6027"	"kite-line would reach; how he followed a third to the fullest stretch"
"6028"	"of the kite-line, and was about to turn back when he glimpsed a far-off"
"6029"	"speck that looked like daylight; dropped the line and groped toward it,"
"6030"	"pushed his head and shoulders through a small hole, and saw the broad"
"6031"	"Mississippi rolling by!"
"6032"	"And if it had only happened to be night he would not have seen that"
"6033"	"speck of daylight and would not have explored that passage any more! He"
"6034"	"told how he went back for Becky and broke the good news and she told"
"6035"	"him not to fret her with such stuff, for she was tired, and knew she was"
"6036"	"going to die, and wanted to. He described how he labored with her and"
"6037"	"convinced her; and how she almost died for joy when she had groped to"
"6038"	"where she actually saw the blue speck of daylight; how he pushed his way"
"6039"	"out at the hole and then helped her out; how they sat there and cried"
"6040"	"for gladness; how some men came along in a skiff and Tom hailed them"
"6041"	"and told them their situation and their famished condition; how the men"
"6042"	"didn’t believe the wild tale at first, “because,” said they, “you are"
"6043"	"five miles down the river below the valley the cave is in”--then took"
"6044"	"them aboard, rowed to a house, gave them supper, made them rest till two"
"6045"	"or three hours after dark and then brought them home."
"6046"	"Before day-dawn, Judge Thatcher and the handful of searchers with him"
"6047"	"were tracked out, in the cave, by the twine clews they had strung behind"
"6048"	"them, and informed of the great news."
"6049"	"Three days and nights of toil and hunger in the cave were not to"
"6050"	"be shaken off at once, as Tom and Becky soon discovered. They were"
"6051"	"bedridden all of Wednesday and Thursday, and seemed to grow more and"
"6052"	"more tired and worn, all the time. Tom got about, a little, on Thursday,"
"6053"	"was downtown Friday, and nearly as whole as ever Saturday; but Becky"
"6054"	"did not leave her room until Sunday, and then she looked as if she had"
"6055"	"passed through a wasting illness."
"6056"	"Tom learned of Huck’s sickness and went to see him on Friday, but could"
"6057"	"not be admitted to the bedroom; neither could he on Saturday or Sunday."
"6058"	"He was admitted daily after that, but was warned to keep still about his"
"6059"	"adventure and introduce no exciting topic. The Widow Douglas stayed by"
"6060"	"to see that he obeyed. At home Tom learned of the Cardiff Hill event;"
"6061"	"also that the “ragged man’s” body had eventually been found in the river"
"6062"	"near the ferry-landing; he had been drowned while trying to escape,"
"6063"	"perhaps."
"6064"	"About a fortnight after Tom’s rescue from the cave, he started off to"
"6065"	"visit Huck, who had grown plenty strong enough, now, to hear exciting"
"6066"	"talk, and Tom had some that would interest him, he thought. Judge"
"6067"	"Thatcher’s house was on Tom’s way, and he stopped to see Becky. The"
"6068"	"Judge and some friends set Tom to talking, and some one asked him"
"6069"	"ironically if he wouldn’t like to go to the cave again. Tom said he"
"6070"	"thought he wouldn’t mind it. The Judge said:"
"6071"	"“Well, there are others just like you, Tom, I’ve not the least doubt."
"6072"	"But we have taken care of that. Nobody will get lost in that cave any"
"6073"	"more.”"
"6074"	"“Why?”"
"6075"	"“Because I had its big door sheathed with boiler iron two weeks ago, and"
"6076"	"triple-locked--and I’ve got the keys.”"
"6077"	"Tom turned as white as a sheet."
"6078"	"“What’s the matter, boy! Here, run, somebody! Fetch a glass of water!”"
"6079"	"The water was brought and thrown into Tom’s face."
"6080"	"“Ah, now you’re all right. What was the matter with you, Tom?”"
"6081"	"“Oh, Judge, Injun Joe’s in the cave!”"
"6082"	"CHAPTER XXXIII"
"6083"	"WITHIN a few minutes the news had spread, and a dozen skiff-loads of"
"6084"	"men were on their way to McDougal’s cave, and the ferryboat, well filled"
"6085"	"with passengers, soon followed. Tom Sawyer was in the skiff that bore"
"6086"	"Judge Thatcher."
"6087"	"When the cave door was unlocked, a sorrowful sight presented itself in"
"6088"	"the dim twilight of the place. Injun Joe lay stretched upon the ground,"
"6089"	"dead, with his face close to the crack of the door, as if his longing"
"6090"	"eyes had been fixed, to the latest moment, upon the light and the cheer"
"6091"	"of the free world outside. Tom was touched, for he knew by his own"
"6092"	"experience how this wretch had suffered. His pity was moved, but"
"6093"	"nevertheless he felt an abounding sense of relief and security, now,"
"6094"	"which revealed to him in a degree which he had not fully appreciated"
"6095"	"before how vast a weight of dread had been lying upon him since the day"
"6096"	"he lifted his voice against this bloody-minded outcast."
"6097"	"Injun Joe’s bowie-knife lay close by, its blade broken in two. The great"
"6098"	"foundation-beam of the door had been chipped and hacked through, with"
"6099"	"tedious labor; useless labor, too, it was, for the native rock formed a"
"6100"	"sill outside it, and upon that stubborn material the knife had wrought"
"6101"	"no effect; the only damage done was to the knife itself. But if there"
"6102"	"had been no stony obstruction there the labor would have been useless"
"6103"	"still, for if the beam had been wholly cut away Injun Joe could not have"
"6104"	"squeezed his body under the door, and he knew it. So he had only hacked"
"6105"	"that place in order to be doing something--in order to pass the weary"
"6106"	"time--in order to employ his tortured faculties. Ordinarily one could"
"6107"	"find half a dozen bits of candle stuck around in the crevices of this"
"6108"	"vestibule, left there by tourists; but there were none now. The prisoner"
"6109"	"had searched them out and eaten them. He had also contrived to catch a"
"6110"	"few bats, and these, also, he had eaten, leaving only their claws. The"
"6111"	"poor unfortunate had starved to death. In one place, near at hand, a"
"6112"	"stalagmite had been slowly growing up from the ground for ages, builded"
"6113"	"by the water-drip from a stalactite overhead. The captive had broken off"
"6114"	"the stalagmite, and upon the stump had placed a stone, wherein he had"
"6115"	"scooped a shallow hollow to catch the precious drop that fell once"
"6116"	"in every three minutes with the dreary regularity of a clock-tick--a"
"6117"	"dessertspoonful once in four and twenty hours. That drop was falling"
"6118"	"when the Pyramids were new; when Troy fell; when the foundations of Rome"
"6119"	"were laid; when Christ was crucified; when the Conqueror created the"
"6120"	"British empire; when Columbus sailed; when the massacre at Lexington was"
"6121"	"“news.”"
"6122"	"It is falling now; it will still be falling when all these things shall"
"6123"	"have sunk down the afternoon of history, and the twilight of tradition,"
"6124"	"and been swallowed up in the thick night of oblivion. Has everything a"
"6125"	"purpose and a mission? Did this drop fall patiently during five thousand"
"6126"	"years to be ready for this flitting human insect’s need? and has it"
"6127"	"another important object to accomplish ten thousand years to come? No"
"6128"	"matter. It is many and many a year since the hapless half-breed scooped"
"6129"	"out the stone to catch the priceless drops, but to this day the tourist"
"6130"	"stares longest at that pathetic stone and that slow-dropping water when"
"6131"	"he comes to see the wonders of McDougal’s cave. Injun Joe’s cup stands"
"6132"	"first in the list of the cavern’s marvels; even “Aladdin’s Palace”"
"6133"	" cannot rival it."
"6134"	"Injun Joe was buried near the mouth of the cave; and people flocked"
"6135"	"there in boats and wagons from the towns and from all the farms and"
"6136"	"hamlets for seven miles around; they brought their children, and"
"6137"	"all sorts of provisions, and confessed that they had had almost as"
"6138"	"satisfactory a time at the funeral as they could have had at the"
"6139"	"hanging."
"6140"	"This funeral stopped the further growth of one thing--the petition to the"
"6141"	"governor for Injun Joe’s pardon. The petition had been largely signed;"
"6142"	"many tearful and eloquent meetings had been held, and a committee of"
"6143"	"sappy women been appointed to go in deep mourning and wail around the"
"6144"	"governor, and implore him to be a merciful ass and trample his duty"
"6145"	"under foot. Injun Joe was believed to have killed five citizens of the"
"6146"	"village, but what of that? If he had been Satan himself there would"
"6147"	"have been plenty of weaklings ready to scribble their names to a"
"6148"	"pardon-petition, and drip a tear on it from their permanently impaired"
"6149"	"and leaky water-works."
"6150"	"The morning after the funeral Tom took Huck to a private place to have"
"6151"	"an important talk. Huck had learned all about Tom’s adventure from the"
"6152"	"Welshman and the Widow Douglas, by this time, but Tom said he reckoned"
"6153"	"there was one thing they had not told him; that thing was what he wanted"
"6154"	"to talk about now. Huck’s face saddened. He said:"
"6155"	"“I know what it is. You got into No. 2 and never found anything but"
"6156"	"whiskey. Nobody told me it was you; but I just knowed it must ‘a’ ben"
"6157"	"you, soon as I heard ‘bout that whiskey business; and I knowed you"
"6158"	"hadn’t got the money becuz you’d ‘a’ got at me some way or other and"
"6159"	"told me even if you was mum to everybody else. Tom, something’s always"
"6160"	"told me we’d never get holt of that swag.”"
"6161"	"“Why, Huck, I never told on that tavern-keeper. _You_ know his tavern"
"6162"	"was all right the Saturday I went to the picnic. Don’t you remember you"
"6163"	"was to watch there that night?”"
"6164"	"“Oh yes! Why, it seems ‘bout a year ago. It was that very night that I"
"6165"	"follered Injun Joe to the widder’s.”"
"6166"	"“_You_ followed him?”"
"6167"	"“Yes--but you keep mum. I reckon Injun Joe’s left friends behind him, and"
"6168"	"I don’t want ‘em souring on me and doing me mean tricks. If it hadn’t"
"6169"	"ben for me he’d be down in Texas now, all right.”"
"6170"	"Then Huck told his entire adventure in confidence to Tom, who had only"
"6171"	"heard of the Welshman’s part of it before."
"6172"	"“Well,” said Huck, presently, coming back to the main question, “whoever"
"6173"	"nipped the whiskey in No. 2, nipped the money, too, I reckon--anyways"
"6174"	"it’s a goner for us, Tom.”"
"6175"	"“Huck, that money wasn’t ever in No. 2!”"
"6176"	"“What!” Huck searched his comrade’s face keenly. “Tom, have you got on"
"6177"	"the track of that money again?”"
"6178"	"“Huck, it’s in the cave!”"
"6179"	"Huck’s eyes blazed."
"6180"	"“Say it again, Tom.”"
"6181"	"“The money’s in the cave!”"
"6182"	"“Tom--honest injun, now--is it fun, or earnest?”"
"6183"	"“Earnest, Huck--just as earnest as ever I was in my life. Will you go in"
"6184"	"there with me and help get it out?”"
"6185"	"“I bet I will! I will if it’s where we can blaze our way to it and not"
"6186"	"get lost.”"
"6187"	"“Huck, we can do that without the least little bit of trouble in the"
"6188"	"world.”"
"6189"	"“Good as wheat! What makes you think the money’s--”"
"6190"	"“Huck, you just wait till we get in there. If we don’t find it I’ll"
"6191"	"agree to give you my drum and every thing I’ve got in the world. I will,"
"6192"	"by jings.”"
"6193"	"“All right--it’s a whiz. When do you say?”"
"6194"	"“Right now, if you say it. Are you strong enough?”"
"6195"	"“Is it far in the cave? I ben on my pins a little, three or four days,"
"6196"	"now, but I can’t walk more’n a mile, Tom--least I don’t think I could.”"
"6197"	"“It’s about five mile into there the way anybody but me would go, Huck,"
"6198"	"but there’s a mighty short cut that they don’t anybody but me know"
"6199"	"about. Huck, I’ll take you right to it in a skiff. I’ll float the skiff"
"6200"	"down there, and I’ll pull it back again all by myself. You needn’t ever"
"6201"	"turn your hand over.”"
"6202"	"“Less start right off, Tom.”"
"6203"	"“All right. We want some bread and meat, and our pipes, and a little"
"6204"	"bag or two, and two or three kite-strings, and some of these new-fangled"
"6205"	"things they call lucifer matches. I tell you, many’s the time I wished I"
"6206"	"had some when I was in there before.”"
"6207"	"A trifle after noon the boys borrowed a small skiff from a citizen who"
"6208"	"was absent, and got under way at once. When they were several miles"
"6209"	"below “Cave Hollow,” Tom said:"
"6210"	"“Now you see this bluff here looks all alike all the way down from the"
"6211"	"cave hollow--no houses, no wood-yards, bushes all alike. But do you see"
"6212"	"that white place up yonder where there’s been a landslide? Well, that’s"
"6213"	"one of my marks. We’ll get ashore, now.”"
"6214"	"They landed."
"6215"	"“Now, Huck, where we’re a-standing you could touch that hole I got out"
"6216"	"of with a fishing-pole. See if you can find it.”"
"6217"	"Huck searched all the place about, and found nothing. Tom proudly"
"6218"	"marched into a thick clump of sumach bushes and said:"
"6219"	"“Here you are! Look at it, Huck; it’s the snuggest hole in this country."
"6220"	"You just keep mum about it. All along I’ve been wanting to be a robber,"
"6221"	"but I knew I’d got to have a thing like this, and where to run across"
"6222"	"it was the bother. We’ve got it now, and we’ll keep it quiet, only we’ll"
"6223"	"let Joe Harper and Ben Rogers in--because of course there’s got to be a"
"6224"	"Gang, or else there wouldn’t be any style about it. Tom Sawyer’s Gang--it"
"6225"	"sounds splendid, don’t it, Huck?”"
"6226"	"“Well, it just does, Tom. And who’ll we rob?”"
"6227"	"“Oh, most anybody. Waylay people--that’s mostly the way.”"
"6228"	"“And kill them?”"
"6229"	"“No, not always. Hive them in the cave till they raise a ransom.”"
"6230"	"“What’s a ransom?”"
"6231"	"“Money. You make them raise all they can, off’n their friends; and after"
"6232"	"you’ve kept them a year, if it ain’t raised then you kill them. That’s"
"6233"	"the general way. Only you don’t kill the women. You shut up the women,"
"6234"	"but you don’t kill them. They’re always beautiful and rich, and awfully"
"6235"	"scared. You take their watches and things, but you always take your hat"
"6236"	"off and talk polite. They ain’t anybody as polite as robbers--you’ll see"
"6237"	"that in any book. Well, the women get to loving you, and after they’ve"
"6238"	"been in the cave a week or two weeks they stop crying and after that"
"6239"	"you couldn’t get them to leave. If you drove them out they’d turn right"
"6240"	"around and come back. It’s so in all the books.”"
"6241"	"“Why, it’s real bully, Tom. I believe it’s better’n to be a pirate.”"
"6242"	"“Yes, it’s better in some ways, because it’s close to home and circuses"
"6243"	"and all that.”"
"6244"	"By this time everything was ready and the boys entered the hole, Tom in"
"6245"	"the lead. They toiled their way to the farther end of the tunnel, then"
"6246"	"made their spliced kite-strings fast and moved on. A few steps brought"
"6247"	"them to the spring, and Tom felt a shudder quiver all through him."
"6248"	"He showed Huck the fragment of candle-wick perched on a lump of clay"
"6249"	"against the wall, and described how he and Becky had watched the flame"
"6250"	"struggle and expire."
"6251"	"The boys began to quiet down to whispers, now, for the stillness and"
"6252"	"gloom of the place oppressed their spirits. They went on, and presently"
"6253"	"entered and followed Tom’s other corridor until they reached the"
"6254"	"“jumping-off place.” The candles revealed the fact that it was not"
"6255"	"really a precipice, but only a steep clay hill twenty or thirty feet"
"6256"	"high. Tom whispered:"
"6257"	"“Now I’ll show you something, Huck.”"
"6258"	"He held his candle aloft and said:"
"6259"	"“Look as far around the corner as you can. Do you see that? There--on the"
"6260"	"big rock over yonder--done with candle-smoke.”"
"6261"	"“Tom, it’s a _cross_!”"
"6262"	"“_Now_ where’s your Number Two? ‘_under the cross_,’ hey? Right yonder’s"
"6263"	"where I saw Injun Joe poke up his candle, Huck!”"
"6264"	"Huck stared at the mystic sign awhile, and then said with a shaky voice:"
"6265"	"“Tom, less git out of here!”"
"6266"	"“What! and leave the treasure?”"
"6267"	"“Yes--leave it. Injun Joe’s ghost is round about there, certain.”"
"6268"	"“No it ain’t, Huck, no it ain’t. It would ha’nt the place where he"
"6269"	"died--away out at the mouth of the cave--five mile from here.”"
"6270"	"“No, Tom, it wouldn’t. It would hang round the money. I know the ways of"
"6271"	"ghosts, and so do you.”"
"6272"	"Tom began to fear that Huck was right. Mis-givings gathered in his mind."
"6273"	"But presently an idea occurred to him--"
"6274"	"“Lookyhere, Huck, what fools we’re making of ourselves! Injun Joe’s"
"6275"	"ghost ain’t a going to come around where there’s a cross!”"
"6276"	"The point was well taken. It had its effect."
"6277"	"“Tom, I didn’t think of that. But that’s so. It’s luck for us, that"
"6278"	"cross is. I reckon we’ll climb down there and have a hunt for that box.”"
"6279"	"Tom went first, cutting rude steps in the clay hill as he descended."
"6280"	"Huck followed. Four avenues opened out of the small cavern which the"
"6281"	"great rock stood in. The boys examined three of them with no result."
"6282"	"They found a small recess in the one nearest the base of the rock, with"
"6283"	"a pallet of blankets spread down in it; also an old suspender, some"
"6284"	"bacon rind, and the well-gnawed bones of two or three fowls. But there"
"6285"	"was no moneybox. The lads searched and researched this place, but in"
"6286"	"vain. Tom said:"
"6287"	"“He said _under_ the cross. Well, this comes nearest to being under the"
"6288"	"cross. It can’t be under the rock itself, because that sets solid on the"
"6289"	"ground.”"
"6290"	"They searched everywhere once more, and then sat down discouraged. Huck"
"6291"	"could suggest nothing. By-and-by Tom said:"
"6292"	"“Lookyhere, Huck, there’s footprints and some candle-grease on the clay"
"6293"	"about one side of this rock, but not on the other sides. Now, what’s"
"6294"	"that for? I bet you the money _is_ under the rock. I’m going to dig in"
"6295"	"the clay.”"
"6296"	"“That ain’t no bad notion, Tom!” said Huck with animation."
"6297"	"Tom’s “real Barlow” was out at once, and he had not dug four inches"
"6298"	"before he struck wood."
"6299"	"“Hey, Huck!--you hear that?”"
"6300"	"Huck began to dig and scratch now. Some boards were soon uncovered and"
"6301"	"removed. They had concealed a natural chasm which led under the rock."
"6302"	"Tom got into this and held his candle as far under the rock as he"
"6303"	"could, but said he could not see to the end of the rift. He proposed"
"6304"	"to explore. He stooped and passed under; the narrow way descended"
"6305"	"gradually. He followed its winding course, first to the right, then to"
"6306"	"the left, Huck at his heels. Tom turned a short curve, by-and-by, and"
"6307"	"exclaimed:"
"6308"	"“My goodness, Huck, lookyhere!”"
"6309"	"It was the treasure-box, sure enough, occupying a snug little cavern,"
"6310"	"along with an empty powder-keg, a couple of guns in leather cases, two"
"6311"	"or three pairs of old moccasins, a leather belt, and some other rubbish"
"6312"	"well soaked with the water-drip."
"6313"	"“Got it at last!” said Huck, ploughing among the tarnished coins with"
"6314"	"his hand. “My, but we’re rich, Tom!”"
"6315"	"“Huck, I always reckoned we’d get it. It’s just too good to believe, but"
"6316"	"we _have_ got it, sure! Say--let’s not fool around here. Let’s snake it"
"6317"	"out. Lemme see if I can lift the box.”"
"6318"	"It weighed about fifty pounds. Tom could lift it, after an awkward"
"6319"	"fashion, but could not carry it conveniently."
"6320"	"“I thought so,” he said; “_They_ carried it like it was heavy, that day"
"6321"	"at the ha’nted house. I noticed that. I reckon I was right to think of"
"6322"	"fetching the little bags along.”"
"6323"	"The money was soon in the bags and the boys took it up to the cross"
"6324"	"rock."
"6325"	"“Now less fetch the guns and things,” said Huck."
"6326"	"“No, Huck--leave them there. They’re just the tricks to have when we"
"6327"	"go to robbing. We’ll keep them there all the time, and we’ll hold our"
"6328"	"orgies there, too. It’s an awful snug place for orgies.”"
"6329"	"“What orgies?”"
"6330"	"“I dono. But robbers always have orgies, and of course we’ve got to"
"6331"	"have them, too. Come along, Huck, we’ve been in here a long time. It’s"
"6332"	"getting late, I reckon. I’m hungry, too. We’ll eat and smoke when we get"
"6333"	"to the skiff.”"
"6334"	"They presently emerged into the clump of sumach bushes, looked warily"
"6335"	"out, found the coast clear, and were soon lunching and smoking in the"
"6336"	"skiff. As the sun dipped toward the horizon they pushed out and got"
"6337"	"under way. Tom skimmed up the shore through the long twilight, chatting"
"6338"	"cheerily with Huck, and landed shortly after dark."
"6339"	"“Now, Huck,” said Tom, “we’ll hide the money in the loft of the widow’s"
"6340"	"woodshed, and I’ll come up in the morning and we’ll count it and divide,"
"6341"	"and then we’ll hunt up a place out in the woods for it where it will be"
"6342"	"safe. Just you lay quiet here and watch the stuff till I run and hook"
"6343"	"Benny Taylor’s little wagon; I won’t be gone a minute.”"
"6344"	"He disappeared, and presently returned with the wagon, put the two small"
"6345"	"sacks into it, threw some old rags on top of them, and started off,"
"6346"	"dragging his cargo behind him. When the boys reached the Welshman’s"
"6347"	"house, they stopped to rest. Just as they were about to move on, the"
"6348"	"Welshman stepped out and said:"
"6349"	"“Hallo, who’s that?”"
"6350"	"“Huck and Tom Sawyer.”"
"6351"	"“Good! Come along with me, boys, you are keeping everybody waiting."
"6352"	"Here--hurry up, trot ahead--I’ll haul the wagon for you. Why, it’s not as"
"6353"	"light as it might be. Got bricks in it?--or old metal?”"
"6354"	"“Old metal,” said Tom."
"6355"	"“I judged so; the boys in this town will take more trouble and fool away"
"6356"	"more time hunting up six bits’ worth of old iron to sell to the foundry"
"6357"	"than they would to make twice the money at regular work. But that’s"
"6358"	"human nature--hurry along, hurry along!”"
"6359"	"The boys wanted to know what the hurry was about."
"6360"	"“Never mind; you’ll see, when we get to the Widow Douglas’.”"
"6361"	"Huck said with some apprehension--for he was long used to being falsely"
"6362"	"accused:"
"6363"	"“Mr. Jones, we haven’t been doing nothing.”"
"6364"	"The Welshman laughed."
"6365"	"“Well, I don’t know, Huck, my boy. I don’t know about that. Ain’t you"
"6366"	"and the widow good friends?”"
"6367"	"“Yes. Well, she’s ben good friends to me, anyway.”"
"6368"	"“All right, then. What do you want to be afraid for?”"
"6369"	"This question was not entirely answered in Huck’s slow mind before he"
"6370"	"found himself pushed, along with Tom, into Mrs. Douglas’ drawing-room."
"6371"	"Mr. Jones left the wagon near the door and followed."
"6372"	"The place was grandly lighted, and everybody that was of any consequence"
"6373"	"in the village was there. The Thatchers were there, the Harpers, the"
"6374"	"Rogerses, Aunt Polly, Sid, Mary, the minister, the editor, and a great"
"6375"	"many more, and all dressed in their best. The widow received the boys"
"6376"	"as heartily as any one could well receive two such looking beings. They"
"6377"	"were covered with clay and candle-grease. Aunt Polly blushed crimson"
"6378"	"with humiliation, and frowned and shook her head at Tom. Nobody suffered"
"6379"	"half as much as the two boys did, however. Mr. Jones said:"
"6380"	"“Tom wasn’t at home, yet, so I gave him up; but I stumbled on him and"
"6381"	"Huck right at my door, and so I just brought them along in a hurry.”"
"6382"	"“And you did just right,” said the widow. “Come with me, boys.”"
"6383"	"She took them to a bedchamber and said:"
"6384"	"“Now wash and dress yourselves. Here are two new suits of"
"6385"	"clothes--shirts, socks, everything complete. They’re Huck’s--no, no"
"6386"	"thanks, Huck--Mr. Jones bought one and I the other. But they’ll fit both"
"6387"	"of you. Get into them. We’ll wait--come down when you are slicked up"
"6388"	"enough.”"
"6389"	"Then she left."
"6390"	"CHAPTER XXXIV"
"6391"	"HUCK said: “Tom, we can slope, if we can find a rope. The window ain’t"
"6392"	"high from the ground.”"
"6393"	"“Shucks! what do you want to slope for?”"
"6394"	"“Well, I ain’t used to that kind of a crowd. I can’t stand it. I ain’t"
"6395"	"going down there, Tom.”"
"6396"	"“Oh, bother! It ain’t anything. I don’t mind it a bit. I’ll take care of"
"6397"	"you.”"
"6398"	"Sid appeared."
"6399"	"“Tom,” said he, “auntie has been waiting for you all the afternoon. Mary"
"6400"	"got your Sunday clothes ready, and everybody’s been fretting about you."
"6401"	"Say--ain’t this grease and clay, on your clothes?”"
"6402"	"“Now, Mr. Siddy, you jist ‘tend to your own business. What’s all this"
"6403"	"blowout about, anyway?”"
"6404"	"“It’s one of the widow’s parties that she’s always having. This time"
"6405"	"it’s for the Welshman and his sons, on account of that scrape they"
"6406"	"helped her out of the other night. And say--I can tell you something, if"
"6407"	"you want to know.”"
"6408"	"“Well, what?”"
"6409"	"“Why, old Mr. Jones is going to try to spring something on the people"
"6410"	"here tonight, but I overheard him tell auntie today about it, as a"
"6411"	"secret, but I reckon it’s not much of a secret now. Everybody knows--the"
"6412"	"widow, too, for all she tries to let on she don’t. Mr. Jones was bound"
"6413"	"Huck should be here--couldn’t get along with his grand secret without"
"6414"	"Huck, you know!”"
"6415"	"“Secret about what, Sid?”"
"6416"	"“About Huck tracking the robbers to the widow’s. I reckon Mr. Jones was"
"6417"	"going to make a grand time over his surprise, but I bet you it will drop"
"6418"	"pretty flat.”"
"6419"	"Sid chuckled in a very contented and satisfied way."
"6420"	"“Sid, was it you that told?”"
"6421"	"“Oh, never mind who it was. _Somebody_ told--that’s enough.”"
"6422"	"“Sid, there’s only one person in this town mean enough to do that, and"
"6423"	"that’s you. If you had been in Huck’s place you’d ‘a’ sneaked down the"
"6424"	"hill and never told anybody on the robbers. You can’t do any but mean"
"6425"	"things, and you can’t bear to see anybody praised for doing good ones."
"6426"	"There--no thanks, as the widow says”--and Tom cuffed Sid’s ears and helped"
"6427"	"him to the door with several kicks. “Now go and tell auntie if you"
"6428"	"dare--and tomorrow you’ll catch it!”"
"6429"	"Some minutes later the widow’s guests were at the supper-table, and a"
"6430"	"dozen children were propped up at little side-tables in the same room,"
"6431"	"after the fashion of that country and that day. At the proper time Mr."
"6432"	"Jones made his little speech, in which he thanked the widow for the"
"6433"	"honor she was doing himself and his sons, but said that there was"
"6434"	"another person whose modesty--"
"6435"	"And so forth and so on. He sprung his secret about Huck’s share in"
"6436"	"the adventure in the finest dramatic manner he was master of, but the"
"6437"	"surprise it occasioned was largely counterfeit and not as clamorous and"
"6438"	"effusive as it might have been under happier circumstances. However,"
"6439"	"the widow made a pretty fair show of astonishment, and heaped so many"
"6440"	"compliments and so much gratitude upon Huck that he almost forgot"
"6441"	"the nearly intolerable discomfort of his new clothes in the entirely"
"6442"	"intolerable discomfort of being set up as a target for everybody’s gaze"
"6443"	"and everybody’s laudations."
"6444"	"The widow said she meant to give Huck a home under her roof and have him"
"6445"	"educated; and that when she could spare the money she would start him in"
"6446"	"business in a modest way. Tom’s chance was come. He said:"
"6447"	"“Huck don’t need it. Huck’s rich.”"
"6448"	"Nothing but a heavy strain upon the good manners of the company kept"
"6449"	"back the due and proper complimentary laugh at this pleasant joke. But"
"6450"	"the silence was a little awkward. Tom broke it:"
"6451"	"“Huck’s got money. Maybe you don’t believe it, but he’s got lots of it."
"6452"	"Oh, you needn’t smile--I reckon I can show you. You just wait a minute.”"
"6453"	"Tom ran out of doors. The company looked at each other with a perplexed"
"6454"	"interest--and inquiringly at Huck, who was tongue-tied."
"6455"	"“Sid, what ails Tom?” said Aunt Polly. “He--well, there ain’t ever any"
"6456"	"making of that boy out. I never--”"
"6457"	"Tom entered, struggling with the weight of his sacks, and Aunt Polly"
"6458"	"did not finish her sentence. Tom poured the mass of yellow coin upon the"
"6459"	"table and said:"
"6460"	"“There--what did I tell you? Half of it’s Huck’s and half of it’s mine!”"
"6461"	"The spectacle took the general breath away. All gazed, nobody spoke for"
"6462"	"a moment. Then there was a unanimous call for an explanation. Tom said"
"6463"	"he could furnish it, and he did. The tale was long, but brimful of"
"6464"	"interest. There was scarcely an interruption from any one to break the"
"6465"	"charm of its flow. When he had finished, Mr. Jones said:"
"6466"	"“I thought I had fixed up a little surprise for this occasion, but it"
"6467"	"don’t amount to anything now. This one makes it sing mighty small, I’m"
"6468"	"willing to allow.”"
"6469"	"The money was counted. The sum amounted to a little over twelve thousand"
"6470"	"dollars. It was more than any one present had ever seen at one time"
"6471"	"before, though several persons were there who were worth considerably"
"6472"	"more than that in property."
"6473"	"CHAPTER XXXV"
"6474"	"THE reader may rest satisfied that Tom’s and Huck’s windfall made a"
"6475"	"mighty stir in the poor little village of St. Petersburg. So vast a"
"6476"	"sum, all in actual cash, seemed next to incredible. It was talked"
"6477"	"about, gloated over, glorified, until the reason of many of the citizens"
"6478"	"tottered under the strain of the unhealthy excitement. Every “haunted”"
"6479"	" house in St. Petersburg and the neighboring villages was dissected,"
"6480"	"plank by plank, and its foundations dug up and ransacked for hidden"
"6481"	"treasure--and not by boys, but men--pretty grave, unromantic men, too,"
"6482"	"some of them. Wherever Tom and Huck appeared they were courted, admired,"
"6483"	"stared at. The boys were not able to remember that their remarks had"
"6484"	"possessed weight before; but now their sayings were treasured and"
"6485"	"repeated; everything they did seemed somehow to be regarded as"
"6486"	"remarkable; they had evidently lost the power of doing and saying"
"6487"	"commonplace things; moreover, their past history was raked up and"
"6488"	"discovered to bear marks of conspicuous originality. The village paper"
"6489"	"published biographical sketches of the boys."
"6490"	"The Widow Douglas put Huck’s money out at six per cent., and Judge"
"6491"	"Thatcher did the same with Tom’s at Aunt Polly’s request. Each lad had"
"6492"	"an income, now, that was simply prodigious--a dollar for every weekday in"
"6493"	"the year and half of the Sundays. It was just what the minister got--no,"
"6494"	"it was what he was promised--he generally couldn’t collect it. A dollar"
"6495"	"and a quarter a week would board, lodge, and school a boy in those old"
"6496"	"simple days--and clothe him and wash him, too, for that matter."
"6497"	"Judge Thatcher had conceived a great opinion of Tom. He said that no"
"6498"	"commonplace boy would ever have got his daughter out of the cave. When"
"6499"	"Becky told her father, in strict confidence, how Tom had taken her"
"6500"	"whipping at school, the Judge was visibly moved; and when she pleaded"
"6501"	"grace for the mighty lie which Tom had told in order to shift that"
"6502"	"whipping from her shoulders to his own, the Judge said with a fine"
"6503"	"outburst that it was a noble, a generous, a magnanimous lie--a lie that"
"6504"	"was worthy to hold up its head and march down through history breast to"
"6505"	"breast with George Washington’s lauded Truth about the hatchet! Becky"
"6506"	"thought her father had never looked so tall and so superb as when he"
"6507"	"walked the floor and stamped his foot and said that. She went straight"
"6508"	"off and told Tom about it."
"6509"	"Judge Thatcher hoped to see Tom a great lawyer or a great soldier some"
"6510"	"day. He said he meant to look to it that Tom should be admitted to the"
"6511"	"National Military Academy and afterward trained in the best law school"
"6512"	"in the country, in order that he might be ready for either career or"
"6513"	"both."
"6514"	"Huck Finn’s wealth and the fact that he was now under the Widow Douglas’"
"6515"	"protection introduced him into society--no, dragged him into it, hurled"
"6516"	"him into it--and his sufferings were almost more than he could bear. The"
"6517"	"widow’s servants kept him clean and neat, combed and brushed, and they"
"6518"	"bedded him nightly in unsympathetic sheets that had not one little spot"
"6519"	"or stain which he could press to his heart and know for a friend. He had"
"6520"	"to eat with a knife and fork; he had to use napkin, cup, and plate;"
"6521"	"he had to learn his book, he had to go to church; he had to talk so"
"6522"	"properly that speech was become insipid in his mouth; whithersoever he"
"6523"	"turned, the bars and shackles of civilization shut him in and bound him"
"6524"	"hand and foot."
"6525"	"He bravely bore his miseries three weeks, and then one day turned up"
"6526"	"missing. For forty-eight hours the widow hunted for him everywhere in"
"6527"	"great distress. The public were profoundly concerned; they searched high"
"6528"	"and low, they dragged the river for his body. Early the third morning"
"6529"	"Tom Sawyer wisely went poking among some old empty hogsheads down behind"
"6530"	"the abandoned slaughter-house, and in one of them he found the refugee."
"6531"	"Huck had slept there; he had just breakfasted upon some stolen odds and"
"6532"	"ends of food, and was lying off, now, in comfort, with his pipe. He was"
"6533"	"unkempt, uncombed, and clad in the same old ruin of rags that had made"
"6534"	"him picturesque in the days when he was free and happy. Tom routed him"
"6535"	"out, told him the trouble he had been causing, and urged him to go home."
"6536"	"Huck’s face lost its tranquil content, and took a melancholy cast. He"
"6537"	"said:"
"6538"	"“Don’t talk about it, Tom. I’ve tried it, and it don’t work; it don’t"
"6539"	"work, Tom. It ain’t for me; I ain’t used to it. The widder’s good to me,"
"6540"	"and friendly; but I can’t stand them ways. She makes me get up just"
"6541"	"at the same time every morning; she makes me wash, they comb me all"
"6542"	"to thunder; she won’t let me sleep in the woodshed; I got to wear them"
"6543"	"blamed clothes that just smothers me, Tom; they don’t seem to any air"
"6544"	"git through ‘em, somehow; and they’re so rotten nice that I can’t"
"6545"	"set down, nor lay down, nor roll around anywher’s; I hain’t slid on a"
"6546"	"cellar-door for--well, it ‘pears to be years; I got to go to church"
"6547"	"and sweat and sweat--I hate them ornery sermons! I can’t ketch a fly in"
"6548"	"there, I can’t chaw. I got to wear shoes all Sunday. The widder eats by"
"6549"	"a bell; she goes to bed by a bell; she gits up by a bell--everything’s so"
"6550"	"awful reg’lar a body can’t stand it.”"
"6551"	"“Well, everybody does that way, Huck.”"
"6552"	"“Tom, it don’t make no difference. I ain’t everybody, and I can’t"
"6553"	"_stand_ it. It’s awful to be tied up so. And grub comes too easy--I don’t"
"6554"	"take no interest in vittles, that way. I got to ask to go a-fishing;"
"6555"	"I got to ask to go in a-swimming--dern’d if I hain’t got to ask to do"
"6556"	"everything. Well, I’d got to talk so nice it wasn’t no comfort--I’d got"
"6557"	"to go up in the attic and rip out awhile, every day, to git a taste"
"6558"	"in my mouth, or I’d a died, Tom. The widder wouldn’t let me smoke;"
"6559"	"she wouldn’t let me yell, she wouldn’t let me gape, nor stretch, nor"
"6560"	"scratch, before folks--” [Then with a spasm of special irritation and"
"6561"	"injury]--“And dad fetch it, she prayed all the time! I never see such a"
"6562"	"woman! I _had_ to shove, Tom--I just had to. And besides, that school’s"
"6563"	"going to open, and I’d a had to go to it--well, I wouldn’t stand _that_,"
"6564"	"Tom. Looky-here, Tom, being rich ain’t what it’s cracked up to be. It’s"
"6565"	"just worry and worry, and sweat and sweat, and a-wishing you was dead"
"6566"	"all the time. Now these clothes suits me, and this bar’l suits me, and"
"6567"	"I ain’t ever going to shake ‘em any more. Tom, I wouldn’t ever got into"
"6568"	"all this trouble if it hadn’t ‘a’ ben for that money; now you just take"
"6569"	"my sheer of it along with your’n, and gimme a ten-center sometimes--not"
"6570"	"many times, becuz I don’t give a dern for a thing ‘thout it’s tollable"
"6571"	"hard to git--and you go and beg off for me with the widder.”"
"6572"	"“Oh, Huck, you know I can’t do that. ‘Tain’t fair; and besides if you’ll"
"6573"	"try this thing just a while longer you’ll come to like it.”"
"6574"	"“Like it! Yes--the way I’d like a hot stove if I was to set on it long"
"6575"	"enough. No, Tom, I won’t be rich, and I won’t live in them cussed"
"6576"	"smothery houses. I like the woods, and the river, and hogsheads, and"
"6577"	"I’ll stick to ‘em, too. Blame it all! just as we’d got guns, and a cave,"
"6578"	"and all just fixed to rob, here this dern foolishness has got to come up"
"6579"	"and spile it all!”"
"6580"	"Tom saw his opportunity--"
"6581"	"“Lookyhere, Huck, being rich ain’t going to keep me back from turning"
"6582"	"robber.”"
"6583"	"“No! Oh, good-licks; are you in real dead-wood earnest, Tom?”"
"6584"	"“Just as dead earnest as I’m sitting here. But Huck, we can’t let you"
"6585"	"into the gang if you ain’t respectable, you know.”"
"6586"	"Huck’s joy was quenched."
"6587"	"“Can’t let me in, Tom? Didn’t you let me go for a pirate?”"
"6588"	"“Yes, but that’s different. A robber is more high-toned than what a"
"6589"	"pirate is--as a general thing. In most countries they’re awful high up in"
"6590"	"the nobility--dukes and such.”"
"6591"	"“Now, Tom, hain’t you always ben friendly to me? You wouldn’t shet me"
"6592"	"out, would you, Tom? You wouldn’t do that, now, _would_ you, Tom?”"
"6593"	"“Huck, I wouldn’t want to, and I _don’t_ want to--but what would people"
"6594"	"say? Why, they’d say, ‘Mph! Tom Sawyer’s Gang! pretty low characters in"
"6595"	"it!’ They’d mean you, Huck. You wouldn’t like that, and I wouldn’t.”"
"6596"	"Huck was silent for some time, engaged in a mental struggle. Finally he"
"6597"	"said:"
"6598"	"“Well, I’ll go back to the widder for a month and tackle it and see if I"
"6599"	"can come to stand it, if you’ll let me b’long to the gang, Tom.”"
"6600"	"“All right, Huck, it’s a whiz! Come along, old chap, and I’ll ask the"
"6601"	"widow to let up on you a little, Huck.”"
"6602"	"“Will you, Tom--now will you? That’s good. If she’ll let up on some of"
"6603"	"the roughest things, I’ll smoke private and cuss private, and crowd"
"6604"	"through or bust. When you going to start the gang and turn robbers?”"
"6605"	"“Oh, right off. We’ll get the boys together and have the initiation"
"6606"	"tonight, maybe.”"
"6607"	"“Have the which?”"
"6608"	"“Have the initiation.”"
"6609"	"“What’s that?”"
"6610"	"“It’s to swear to stand by one another, and never tell the gang’s"
"6611"	"secrets, even if you’re chopped all to flinders, and kill anybody and"
"6612"	"all his family that hurts one of the gang.”"
"6613"	"“That’s gay--that’s mighty gay, Tom, I tell you.”"
"6614"	"“Well, I bet it is. And all that swearing’s got to be done at midnight,"
"6615"	"in the lonesomest, awfulest place you can find--a ha’nted house is the"
"6616"	"best, but they’re all ripped up now.”"
"6617"	"“Well, midnight’s good, anyway, Tom.”"
"6618"	"“Yes, so it is. And you’ve got to swear on a coffin, and sign it with"
"6619"	"blood.”"
"6620"	"“Now, that’s something _like_! Why, it’s a million times bullier than"
"6621"	"pirating. I’ll stick to the widder till I rot, Tom; and if I git to be"
"6622"	"a reg’lar ripper of a robber, and everybody talking ‘bout it, I reckon"
"6623"	"she’ll be proud she snaked me in out of the wet.”"
"6624"	"CONCLUSION"
"6625"	"SO endeth this chronicle. It being strictly a history of a _boy_, it"
"6626"	"must stop here; the story could not go much further without becoming the"
"6627"	"history of a _man_. When one writes a novel about grown people, he knows"
"6628"	"exactly where to stop--that is, with a marriage; but when he writes of"
"6629"	"juveniles, he must stop where he best can."
"6630"	"Most of the characters that perform in this book still live, and are"
"6631"	"prosperous and happy. Some day it may seem worth while to take up the"
"6632"	"story of the younger ones again and see what sort of men and women they"
"6633"	"turned out to be; therefore it will be wisest not to reveal any of that"
"6634"	"part of their lives at present."
"6635"	"End of the Project Gutenberg Ebook of Adventures of Tom Sawyer,"
"6636"	"Complete, by Mark Twain (Samuel Clemens)"
